Act done by a person bound, or by mistake of fact believing himself bound, \nby law \n77. Act of Judge when acting judicially\n\n6                                         Laws of Malaysia                        ACT 574 \n \nSection \n78. Act done pursuant to the judgment or order of a Court \n79. Act done by a person justified, or by mistake of fact believing himself \njustified by law \n80. Accident in the doing of a lawful act \n81. Act likely to cause harm but done without a criminal intent, and to prevent \nother harm \n82. Act of a child under 10 years of age \n83. Act of a child above 10 and under 12 years of age, who has not attained \nsufficient maturity of understanding \n84. Act of a person of unsound mind \n85. Intoxication when a defence \n86. Effect of defence of intoxication when established \n87. Act not intended and not known to be likely to cause death or grievous hurt, \ndone by consent \n88. Act not intended to cause death, done by consent in good faith for the benefit \nof a person \n89. Act done in good faith for the benefit of a child or person of unsound mind, \nby or by consent of guardian \n90. Consent known to be given under fear or misconception and consent of a \nchild or person of unsound mind \n91. Acts which are offences independently of harm caused to the person \nconsenting, are not within the exceptions in sections 87, 88 and 89 \n92. Act done in good faith for the benefit of a person without consent \n93. Communication made in good faith \n94. Act to which a person is compelled by threats \n95. Act causing slight harm \n \nRight of Private Defence \n \n96. Nothing done in private defence is an offence \n97. Right of private defence of the body and of property \n98. Right of private defence against the act of a person of unsound mind\n\nPenal Code                                            7 \n \nSection \n99. Acts against which there is no right of private defence \n100. When the right of private defence of the body extends to causing death \n101. Commencement and continuance of the right of private defence of property \n106. Punishment for attempting to commit offences punishable with \nimprisonment\n\n31 \n \nLAWS OF MALAYSIA \n \n \nAct 574 \n \n \nPENAL CODE \n \n \nAn Act relating to criminal offences. \n \n[Throughout Malaysia\u201431 March 1976, \nAct A327; P.U. (B) 139/1976] \n \n \nCHAPTER I \n \nPRELIMINARY \n \n \nShort title \n \n1. This Act may be cited as the Penal Code. \n \n \nPunishment of offences committed within Malaysia \n \n2. Every person shall be liable to punishment under this Code and not \notherwise for every act or omission contrary to the provisions thereof, \nof which he shall be guilty within Malaysia. \n \n \nPunishment of offences committed beyond, but which by law may \nbe tried within Malaysia \n \n3. Any person liable by law to be tried for an offence committed \nbeyond the limits of Malaysia, shall be dealt with according to the \nprovisions of this Code for any act committed beyond Malaysia, in the \nsame manner as if such act had been committed within Malaysia.\n\n32                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nExtension of Code to extraterritorial offences \n \n4.  (1) The provisions of Chapters VI, VIA and VIB shall apply to any \noffence committed\u2014 \n \n(a) by any citizen or any permanent resident on the high seas \non board any ship or on any aircraft whether or not such \nship or aircraft is registered in Malaysia; \n \n(b) by any citizen or any permanent resident in any place \nwithout and beyond the limits of Malaysia; \n \n(c) by any person against a citizen of Malaysia; \n \n(d) by any person against property belonging to, or operated \nor controlled by, in whole or in part, the Government of \nMalaysia or the Government of any State in Malaysia, \nincluding diplomatic or consular premises of Malaysia, \nany citizen of Malaysia, or any corporation created by or \nunder the laws of Malaysia located outside Malaysia; \n \n(e) by any person to compel the Government of Malaysia or \nthe Government of any State in Malaysia to do or refrain \nfrom doing any act; \n \n(f) by any stateless person who has his habitual residence in \nMalaysia; \n \n(g) by any person against or on board a fixed platform while \nit is located on the continental shelf of Malaysia; or \n \n(h) by any person who after the commission of the offence is \npresent in Malaysia,  \n \nas if the offence had been committed in Malaysia. \n \n(2) In this section\u2014\n\nPenal Code                                            33 \n \n(a) \u201coffence\u201d includes every act done outside Malaysia which, \nif done in Malaysia, would be an offence punishable under \nthis Code; \n \n(b) \u201cpermanent resident\u201d has the meaning assigned by the \nCourts of Judicature Act 1964 [Act 91]. \n \n \nCertain laws not to be affected by this Code \n \n5. Nothing in this Code is intended to repeal, vary, suspend or affect \nany of the provisions of any written law for punishing mutiny and \ndesertion of officers, soldiers and airmen in the Malaysian Armed \nForces, or of any other law for the time being in force. \n \n \nCHAPTER II \n \nGENERAL EXPLANATIONS \n \nDefinitions in the Code to be understood subject to exceptions \n \n6. Throughout this Code every definition of an offence, every penal \nprovision and every illustration of every such definition or penal \nprovision, shall be understood subject to the exceptions contained in \nthe Chapter entitled \u201cGeneral Exceptions\u201d, though those exceptions are \nnot repeated in such definition, penal provision or illustration. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a) The sections in this Code which contain definitions of offences, do not \nexpress that a child under ten years of age cannot commit such offences, but the \ndefinitions are to be understood subject to the general exception which provides \nthat \u201cnothing shall be an offence which is done by a child under ten years of \nage\u201d. \n \n(b) A, a police officer, without warrant, apprehends Z, who has committed \nmurder. Here A is not guilty of the offence of wrongful confinement, for he was \nbound by law to apprehend Z, and therefore the case falls within the general \nexception which provides that \u201cnothing is an offence which is done by a person \nwho is bound by law to do it\u201d.\n\n34                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nExpression once explained is used in the same sense throughout \nthe Code \n \n7. Every expression which is explained in any part of this Code, is \nused in every part of this Code in conformity with the explanation. \n \n \n\u201cGender\u201d \n \n8. The pronoun \u201che\u201d and its derivatives are used of any person, \nwhether male or female. \n \n \n\u201cNumber\u201d \n \n9. Unless the contrary appears from the context, words importing the \nsingular number include the plural number, and words importing the \nplural number include the singular number. \n \n \n\u201cMan\u201d and \u201cwoman\u201d \n \n10. The word \u201cman\u201d denotes a male human being of any age; the \nword \u201cwoman\u201d denotes a female human being of any age. \n \n \n\u201cPerson\u201d \n \n11. The word \u201cperson\u201d includes any company or association or body \nof persons, whether incorporated or not. \n \n \n\u201cPublic\u201d \n \n12. The word \u201cpublic\u201d includes any class of the public or any \ncommunity. \n \n \n13. (Deleted by L.N. (N.S.) 1 of 1957).\n\nPenal Code                                            35 \n \n \n14\u201316. (There are no ss. 14\u201316). \n \n \n\u201cGovernment\u201d \n \n17. \u201cGovernment\u201d includes the Government of Malaysia and of the \nStates and any person lawfully performing executive functions of \nGovernment under any written law. \n \n \n18. (There is no s. 18). \n \n \n\u201cJudge\u201d \n \n19. The word \u201cjudge\u201d denotes not only every person who is officially \ndesignated as a Judge, but also every person who is empowered by law \nto give, in any legal proceeding, civil or criminal, a definitive \njudgment, or a judgment which, if not appealed against, would be \ndefinitive, or a judgment which if confirmed by some other authority, \nwould be definitive, or who is one of a body of persons, which body of \npersons is empowered by law to give such a judgment. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a) A Magistrate exercising jurisdiction in respect of a charge on which he \nhas power to sentence to fine or imprisonment, with or without appeal, is a \nJudge. \n \n(b) A President of a Town Board holding an enquiry as to the origin of a \nfire under the provisions of the Town Boards Enactment is a Judge. \n \n \n\u201cCourt\u201d \n \n20. The word \u201cCourt\u201d denotes a judge who is empowered by law to \nact judicially alone, or a body of judges which is empowered by law to \nact judicially as a body, when such judge or body of judges is acting \njudicially.\n\n36                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \n \u201cPublic servant\u201d \n \n21. The words \u201cpublic servant\u201d denote a person falling under any of \nthe descriptions hereinafter following: \n \n(a) (Deleted by L.N. (N.S.) 1 of 1957); \n \n(b) every Commissioned Officer in the Malaysian Armed \nForces; \n \n(c) every Judge; \n \n(d) every officer of a Court whose duty it is, as such officer, \nto investigate or report on any matter of law or fact, or to \nmake, authenticate, or keep any document, or to take \ncharge or dispose of any property or to execute any judicial \nprocess, or to administer any oath, or to interpret, or to \npreserve order in the Court, and every person specially \nauthorized by a Court to perform any of such duties; \n \n(e) every juryman or assessor assisting a Court or public \nservant; \n \n(f) every arbitrator or other person to whom any cause or \nmatter has been referred for decision or report by any \nCourt, or by any other competent public authority; \n \n(g) every person who holds any office by virtue of which he \nis empowered to place or keep any person in confinement; \n \n(h) every officer of Government whose duty it is, as such \nofficer, to prevent offences, to give information of \noffences, to bring offenders to justice, or to protect the \npublic health, safety or convenience; \n \n(i) every officer whose duty it is, as such officer, to take, \nreceive, keep or expend any property, on behalf of \nGovernment, or to make any survey, assessment, or \ncontract on behalf of Government, or to execute any\n\nPenal Code                                            37 \n \nrevenue process, or to investigate, or to report on any \nmatter affecting the pecuniary interests of Government, or \nto make, authenticate, or keep any document relating to \nthe pecuniary interests of Government, or to prevent the \ninfraction of any law for the protection of the pecuniary \ninterests of Government, and every officer in the service \nor pay of Government, or remunerated by fees or \ncommission for the performance of any public duty; \n \n(j) every officer whose duty it is, as such officer, to take, \nreceive, keep or expend any property, to make any survey \nor assessment, or to levy any rate or tax for any secular \ncommon purpose of any village, town or district, or to \nmake, authenticate or keep any document for the \nascertaining of the rights of the people of any village, town \nor district. \n \nExplanation 1\u2014Persons falling under any of the above descriptions are \npublic servants, whether appointed by the Government or not. \n \nExplanation 2\u2014Wherever the words \u201cpublic servant\u201d occur, they shall be \nunderstood of every person who is in actual possession of the situation of a \npublic servant, whatever legal defect there may be in his right to hold that \nsituation. \n \n \n\u201cMovable property\u201d \n \n22. The words \u201cmovable property\u201d are intended to include corporeal \nproperty of every description, except land and things attached to the \nearth, or permanently fastened to anything which is attached to the \nearth. \n \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nWritings, relating to real or personal property or rights, are movable \nproperty.\n\n38                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \n \u201cWrongful gain\u201d and \u201cwrongful loss\u201d \n \n23. \u201cWrongful gain\u201d is gain by unlawful means of property to which \nthe person gaining is not legally entitled. \n \n\u201cWrongful loss\u201d is the loss by unlawful means of property to which \nthe person losing it is legally entitled. \n \nA person is said to gain wrongfully when such person retains \nwrongfully, as well as when such person acquires wrongfully.   \nA person is said to lose wrongfully when such person is wrongfully \nkept out of any property, as well as when such person is wrongfully \ndeprived of property. \n \n \n\u201cDishonestly\u201d \n \n24. Whoever does anything with the intention of causing wrongful \ngain to one person, or wrongful loss to another person, irrespective of \nwhether the act causes actual wrongful loss or gain, is said to do that \nthing \u201cdishonestly\u201d. \n \n \nExplanation\u2014In relation to the offence of criminal misappropriation or \ncriminal breach of trust it is immaterial whether there was an intention to defraud \nor to deceive any person. \n \n \n\u201cFraudulently\u201d \n \n25. A person is said to do a thing fraudulently if he does that thing \nwith intend to defraud, but not otherwise. \n \n \n\u201cReason to believe\u201d \n \n26. A person is said to have \u201creason to believe\u201d a thing, if he has \nsufficient cause to believe that thing, but not otherwise.\n\nPenal Code                                            39 \n \n \n\u201cProperty in possession of wife, clerk or servant\u201d \n \n27. When property is in the possession of a person\u2019s wife, clerk or \nservant, on account of that person, it is in that person\u2019s possession \nwithin the meaning of this Code. \n \n \nExplanation\u2014A person employed temporarily or on a particular occasion \nin the capacity of a clerk or servant, is a clerk or servant within the meaning of \nthis section. \n \n \n\u201cCounterfeit\u201d \n \n28. A person is said to \u201ccounterfeit\u201d, who causes one thing to \nresemble another thing, intending by means of that resemblance to \npractise deception, or knowing it to be likely that deception will \nthereby be practised. \n \n \nExplanation 1\u2014It is not essential to counterfeiting that the imitation should \nbe exact. \n \nExplanation 2\u2014Where a person causes one thing to resemble another thing \nand the resemblance is such that a person might be deceived thereby it shall be \npresumed until the contrary is proved that the person so causing the one thing to \nresemble the other thing intended by means of that resemblance to practise \ndeception or knew it to be likely that deception would thereby be practised. \n \n \n\u201cDocument\u201d \n \n29. (1) \nThe word \u201cdocument\u201d means any matter expressed, \ndescribed or howsoever represented, upon any substance, material, \nthing or article, including any matter embodied in a disc, tape, film, \nsound track or other device whatsoever, by means of\u2014 \n \n(a) letters, figures, marks, symbols, signals, signs or other \nforms of expression, description or representation \nwhatsoever;\n\n40                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \n(b) any visual recording (whether of still or moving images); \n \n(c) any sound recording, or any electronic, magnetic, \nmechanical or other recording whatsoever and howsoever \nmade, or any sounds, electronic impulses, or other data \nwhatsoever; \n \n(d) a recording, or transmission, over a distance of any matter \nby any, or any combination, of the means mentioned in \nparagraph (a), (b) or (c),  \n \nor by more than one of the means mentioned in paragraphs (a), (b), (c) \nand (d), intended to be used or which may be used for the purpose of \nexpressing, describing, or howsoever representing, that matter. \n \n(2) For the purposes of this section\u2014 \n \n(a) \u201cfilm\u201d includes a microfilm and any negative; \n \n(b) \u201cmicrofilm\u201d means any transparent material bearing a \nvisual image in reduced size either singly or as a series and \nincludes a microfiche; \n \n(c) \u201cnegative\u201d means a transparent negative photograph on \nany substance or material, and includes any transparent \nnegative photograph made from the original negative \nphotograph. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \nA writing is a document. \n \nWords printed, lithographed or photographed are documents. \n \nA map, plan, graph or sketch is a document. \n \nAn inscription on wood, metal, stone or any other substance, material or \nthing is a document. \n \nA drawing, painting, picture or caricature is a document.\n\nPenal Code                                            41 \n \n \nA photograph or a negative is a document. \n \nA tape recording of a telephonic communication, including a recording of \nsuch communication transmitted over distance, is a document. \n \nA photographic or other visual recording, including a recording of a \nphotographic or other visual transmission over a distance, is a document. \n \nA matter recorded, stored, processed, retrieved or produced by a computer \nis a document. \n \nExplanation\u2014Whatever is expressed by means of letters, figures or marks \nas explained by mercantile or other usage, shall be deemed to be expressed by \nsuch letters, figures or marks within the meaning of this section, although the \nsame may not be actually expressed. \n \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nA writes his name on the back of a bill of exchange payable to his order. \nThe meaning of the endorsement, as explained by mercantile usage, is that the \nbill is to be paid to the holder. The endorsement is a document, and must be \nconstrued in the same manner as if the words \u201cpay to the holder\u201d, or words to \nthat effect, has been written over the signature. \n \n \n\u201cValuable security\u201d \n \n30. The words \u201cvaluable security\u201d denote a document which is, or \npurports to be, a document whereby any legal right is created, \nextended, transferred, restricted, extinguished, or released, or whereby \nany person acknowledges that he lies under legal liability, or has not a \ncertain legal right. \n \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nA writes his name on the back of a bill of exchange. As the effect of this \nendorsement is to transfer the right to the bill to any person who may become \nthe lawful holder of it, the endorsement is a \u201cvaluable security\u201d.\n\n42                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \n\u201cA will\u201d \n \n31. The words \u201ca will\u201d denote any testamentary document. \n \n \nWords referring to acts include illegal omissions \n \n32. In every part of this Code, except where a contrary intention \nappears from the context, words which refer to acts done extend also \nto illegal omissions. \n \n \n\u201cAct\u201d and \u201comission\u201d \n \n33. The word \u201cact\u201d denotes as well a series of acts as a single act: the \nword \u201comission\u201d denotes as well a series of omissions as a single \nomission. \n \n \nEach of several persons liable for an act done by all, in like manner \nas if done by him alone \n \n34. When a criminal act is done by several persons, in furtherance of \nthe common intention of all, each of such persons is liable for that act \nin the same manner as if the act were done by him alone. \n \n \nWhen such an act is criminal by reason of its being done with a \ncriminal knowledge or intention \n \n35. Whenever an act, which is criminal only by reason of its being \ndone with a criminal knowledge or intention, is done by several \npersons, each of such persons who joins in the act with such knowledge \nor intention, is liable for the act in the same manner as if the act were \ndone by him alone with that knowledge or intention.\n\nPenal Code                                            43 \n \nEffect caused partly by act and partly by omission \n \n36. Wherever the causing of a certain effect, or an attempt to cause \nthat effect, by an act or by an omission, is an offence, it is to be \nunderstood that the causing of that effect partly by an act and partly by \nan omission is the same offence. \n \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nA intentionally causes Z\u2019s death, partly by illegally omitting to give Z food, \nand partly by beating Z. A has committed murder. \n \n \nCooperation by doing one of several acts constituting an offence \n \n37. When an offence is committed by means of several acts, whoever \nintentionally cooperates in the commission of that offence by doing \nany one of those acts, either singly or jointly with any other person, \ncommits that offence. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a) A and B agree to murder Z, by severally, and at different times, giving \nhim small doses of poison. A and B administer the poison, according to the \nagreement with intent to murder Z. Z dies from the effects of the several doses \nof poison so administered to him. Here A and B intentionally cooperate in the \ncommission of murder, and as each of them does an act by which the death is \ncaused, they are both guilty of the offence, though their acts are separate. \n \n(b) A and B are joint jailors, and as such have the charge of Z, a prisoner, \nalternately for six hours at a time. A and B, intending to cause Z\u2019s death, knowingly \ncooperate in causing that effect by illegally omitting, each during the time of his \nattendance, to furnish Z with food supplied to them for that purpose. Z dies of hunger. \nBoth A and B are guilty of the murder of Z. \n \n(c) A, a jailor, has the charge of Z, a prisoner. A, intending to cause Z\u2019s \ndeath, illegally omits to supply Z with food; in consequence of which Z is much \nreduced in strength, but the starvation is not sufficient to cause his death. A is \ndismissed from his office, and B succeeds him. B, without collusion or \ncooperation with A, illegally omits to supply Z with food, knowing that he is \nlikely thereby to cause Z\u2019s death. Z dies of hunger. B is guilty of murder; but as \nA did not cooperate with B, A is guilty only of an attempt to commit murder.\n\n44                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \n \nSeveral persons engaged in the commission of a criminal act, may \nbe guilty of different offences \n \n38. Where several persons are engaged or concerned in the \ncommission of a criminal act, they may be guilty of different offences \nby means of that act. \n \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nA attacks Z under such circumstances of grave provocation that his killing \nof Z would be only culpable homicide not amounting to murder. B, having ill \nwill towards Z, and intending to kill him, and not having been subject to the \nprovocation, assists A in killing Z. Here, though A and B are both engaged in \ncausing Z\u2019s death, B is guilty of murder, and A is guilty only of culpable \nhomicide. \n \n \n\u201cVoluntarily\u201d \n \n39. A person is said to cause an effect \u201cvoluntarily\u201d when he causes \nit by means whereby he intended to cause it, or by means which, at \ntime of employing those means, he knew or had reason to believe to be \nlikely to cause it. \n \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nA sets fire, by night, to an inhabited house in a large town, for the purpose \nof facilitating a robbery, and thus causes the death of a person. Here A may not \nhave intended to cause death, and may even be sorry that death has been caused \nby his act; yet, if he knew that he was likely to cause death, he has caused death \nvoluntarily. \n \n \n\u201cOffence\u201d \n \n40. (1) \nExcept in the Chapter and sections mentioned in \nsubsections (2) and (3), the word \u201coffence\u201d denotes a thing made \npunishable by this Code.\n\nPenal Code                                            45 \n \n \n(2) In Chapter IV and in sections 71, 109, 110, 112, 114, 115, 116, \n117, 187, 194, 195, 203, 211, 213, 214, 221, 222, 223, 224, 225, 327, \n328, 329, 330, 331, 347, 348, 388, 389 and 445, the word \u201coffence\u201d \ndenotes a thing punishable under this Code or under any other law for \nthe time being in force. \n \n(3) In sections 141, 176, 177, 201, 202, 212, 216 and 441, the word \n\u201coffence\u201d has the same meaning when the thing punishable under any \nother law for the time being in force is punishable under such law with \nimprisonment for a term of six months or upwards, whether with or \nwithout fine. \n \n \n41\u201342. (There are no ss. 41\u201342). \n \n \n\u201cIllegal\u201d, \u201cunlawful\u201d and \u201clegally bound to do\u201d \n \n43. The word \u201cillegal\u201d or \u201cunlawful\u201d is applicable to everything \nwhich is an offence, or which is prohibited by law, or which furnishes \nground for a civil action. \n \nAnd in respect of the word \u201cillegal\u201d, a person is said to be \u201clegally \nbound to do\u201d whatever it is illegal in him to omit. \n \n \n\u201cInjury\u201d \n \n44. The word \u201cinjury\u201d denotes any harm whatever illegally caused to \nany person, in body, mind, reputation or property. \n \n \n\u201cLife\u201d \n \n45. The word \u201clife\u201d denotes the life of a human being, unless the \ncontrary appears from the context.\n\n46                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \n \n\u201cDeath\u201d \n \n46. The word \u201cdeath\u201d denotes the death of a human being, unless the \ncontrary appears from the context. \n \n \n\u201cAnimal\u201d \n \n47. The word \u201canimal\u201d denotes any living creature, other than a \nhuman being. \n \n \n\u201cVessel\u201d \n \n48. The word \u201cvessel\u201d denotes anything made for the conveyance by \nwater of human beings, or of property. \n \n \n\u201cYear\u201d and \u201cmonth\u201d \n \n49. Whenever the word \u201cyear\u201d or the word \u201cmonth\u201d is used, it is to \nbe understood that the year or the month is to be reckoned according \nto the Gregorian Calendar. \n \n \n\u201cSection\u201d \n \n50. The word \u201csection\u201d denotes one of those portions of a Chapter of \nthis Code which are distinguished by prefixed numeral figures. \n \n \n\u201cOath\u201d \n \n51. The word \u201coath\u201d includes a solemn affirmation substituted by \nlaw for an oath, and any declaration required or authorized by law to \nbe made before a public servant, or to be used for the purpose of proof, \nwhether in a Court or not.\n\nPenal Code                                            47 \n \n \n\u201cGood faith\u201d \n \n52. Nothing is said to be done or believed in good faith which is done \nor believed without due care and attention. \n \n \n\u201cNon-serious offence\u201d \n \n52A. The words \u201cnon-serious offence\u201d denote an offence punishable \nwith imprisonment for a term of not more than ten years. \n \n \n \u201cSerious offence\u201d \n \n52B. The words \u201cserious offence\u201d denote an offence punishable with \nimprisonment for a term of ten years or more. \n \n \nCHAPTER III \n \nPUNISHMENTS \n \n53. \n(Deleted by F.M. Ord. 14 of 1953). \n \n54\u201555. (Deleted by L.N. (N.S.) 1 of 1957). \n \n56. \n(There is no s. 56). \n \n \nFractions of terms of punishment \n \n57. \nIn calculating fractions of terms of punishment, imprisonment \nfor life shall be reckoned as equivalent to imprisonment for thirty \nyears. \n \n \n58. \n(There is no s. 58).\n\n48                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \n59\u221260. (Deleted by F.M. Ord. 14 of 1953). \n \n \n61\u201362. (There are no ss. 61\u201362). \n \n \n63\u221264. (Deleted by F.M.S. En. 1 of 1936). \n \n \n65. \n(There is no s. 65). \n \n \n66\u221270. (Deleted by F.M.S. En. 1 of 1936). \n \n \nLimit of punishment of offence which is made up of several \noffences \n \n71. (1) \nWhere anything which is an offence is made up of parts, \nany of which parts is itself an offence, the offender shall not be \npunished with the punishment of more than one of such of his offences, \nunless it be so expressly provided. \n \n(2) Where anything is an offence falling within two or more \nseparate definitions of any law in force for the time being by which \noffences are defined or punished, or where several acts of which one \nor more than one would by itself or themselves constitute an offence \nconstitute when combined a different offence the offender shall not be \npunished with a more severe punishment than the Court which tries \nhim could award for any one of such offences. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a) A gives Z fifty strokes with a stick. Here A may have committed the \noffence of voluntarily causing hurt to Z by the whole beating, and also by each \nof the blows which make up the whole beating. If A were liable to punishment \nfor every blow, he might be imprisoned for fifty years, one for each blow. But \nhe is liable only to one punishment for the whole beating.\n\nPenal Code                                            49 \n \n(b) But if, while A is beating Z, Y interferes, and A intentionally strikes Y, \nhere, as the blow given to Y is no part of the act whereby A voluntarily causes \nhurt to Z, A is liable to one punishment for voluntarily causing hurt to Z, and to \nanother for the blow given to Y. \n \n \nPunishment of a person found guilty of one of several offences, the \njudgment stating that it is doubtful of which \n \n72. In all cases in which judgment is given that a person is guilty of \none of several offences specified in the judgment, but that it is doubtful \nof which of these offences he is guilty, the offender shall be punished \nfor the offence for which the lowest punishment is provided, if the \nsame punishment is not provided for all. \n \n \n73\u201574. (Deleted by F.M. Ord. 14 of 1953). \n \n \nPunishment of persons convicted, after a previous conviction of an \noffence punishable with three years imprisonment \n \n75. Whoever, having been convicted of an offence punishable under \nChapter XII or Chapter XVII with imprisonment for a term of three \nyears or upwards, or having been convicted in any other part of \nMalaysia, in the Republic of Singapore or in the State of Brunei of an \noffence of a nature similar to any of those offences, shall be guilty of \nany offence punishable under either of those Chapters with \nimprisonment for a term of three years or upwards,  and shall be subject \nfor every such subsequent offence to double the amount of punishment \nto which he would otherwise have been liable for the same. \n \n \nPunishment of mandatory imprisonment for persons convicted of \nmultiple serious offences \n \n75A. Whoever, having been convicted at least two times of a serious \noffence and was punished with at least two years of imprisonment for \neach of those convictions, shall be punished with mandatory \nimprisonment for the third and subsequent offences and the term of\n\n50                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nimprisonment shall not be less than double the term of the longer term \nof imprisonment imposed for the previous convictions. \n \n \nCHAPTER IV \n \nGENERAL EXCEPTIONS \n \nAct done by a person bound, or by mistake of fact believing himself \nbound, by law \n \n76. Nothing is an offence which is done by a person who is, or who, \nby reason of a mistake of fact and not by reason of a mistake of law, in \ngood faith believes himself to be, bound by law to do it. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a) A, a soldier, fires on a mob by the order of his superior officer, in \nconformity with the commands of the law. A has committed no offence. \n \n(b) A, an officer of a Court, being ordered by that Court to arrest Y, and, \nafter due enquiry, believing Z to be Y, arrests Z. A has committed no offence. \n \n \nAct of Judge when acting judicially \n \n77. Nothing is an offence which is done by a Judge when acting \njudicially in the exercise of any power which is, or which in good faith \nhe believes to be, given to him by law. \n \n \nAct done pursuant to the judgment or order of a Court \n \n78. Nothing which is done in pursuance of, or which is warranted by \nthe judgment or order of a Court, if done while such judgment or order \nremains in force, is an offence, notwithstanding the Court may have \nhad no jurisdiction to pass such judgment or order, provided the person \ndoing the act in good faith believes that the Court had such jurisdiction.\n\nPenal Code                                            51 \n \n \n \nAct done by a person justified, or by mistake of fact believing \nhimself justified by law \n \n79. Nothing is an offence which is done by any person who is \njustified by law, or who by reason of a mistake of fact and not by reason \nof a mistake of law in good faith believes himself to be justified by \nlaw, in doing it. \n \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nA sees Z commit what appears to A to be a murder. A, in the exercise, to the \nbest of his judgment exerted in good faith, of the power which the law gives to \nall persons of apprehending murderers in the act, seizes Z, in order to bring Z \nbefore the proper authorities. A has committed no offence, though it may turn \nout that Z was acting in self-defence. \n \n \nAccident in the doing of a lawful act \n \n80. Nothing is an offence which is done by accident or misfortune, \nand without any criminal intention or knowledge, in the doing of a \nlawful act in a lawful manner, by lawful means, and with proper care \nand caution. \n \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nA is at work with a hatchet; the head flies off and kills a man who is standing \nby. Here, if there was no want of proper caution on the part of A, his act is \nexcusable and not an offence. \n \n \nAct likely to cause harm but done without a criminal intent, and \nto prevent other harm \n \n81. Nothing is an offence merely by reason of its being done with the \nknowledge that it is likely to cause harm, if it be done without any \ncriminal intention to cause harm, and in good faith for the purpose of \npreventing or avoiding other harm to person or property.\n\n52                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \n \nExplanation\u2014It is a question of fact in such a case whether the harm to be \nprevented or avoided was of such a nature and so imminent as to justify or excuse \nthe risk of doing the act with the knowledge that it was likely to cause harm. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a) A, the captain of a steam vessel, suddenly and without any fault or \nnegligence on his part, finds himself in such a position that, before he can stop \nhis vessel, he must inevitably run down a boat B, with 20 or 30 passengers on \nboard, unless he changes the course of his vessel; and that, by changing his \ncourse, he must incur risk of running down a boat, C, with only two passengers \non board, which he may possibly clear. Here, if A alters his course without any \nintention to run down the boat C, and in good faith for the purposes of avoiding \nthe danger to the passengers in the boat B, he is not guilty of an offence, though \nhe may run down the boat C, by doing an act which he knew was likely to cause \nthat effect, if it be found as a matter of fact that the danger which he intended to \navoid was such as to excuse him in incurring the risk of running down the boat \nC. \n \n(b) A in a great fire pulls down houses in order to prevent the conflagration \nfrom spreading. He does this with the intention, in good faith, of saving human \nlife or property. Here, if it be found that the harm to be prevented was of such a \nnature and so imminent as to excuse A\u2019s act, A is not guilty of the offence. \n \n \nAct of a child under 10 years of age \n \n82. Nothing is an offence which is done by a child under ten years of \nage. \n \n \nAct of a child above 10 and under 12 years of age, who has not \nattained sufficient maturity of understanding \n \n83. Nothing is an offence which is done by a child above ten years \nof age and under twelve, who has not attained sufficient maturity of \nunderstanding to judge of the nature and consequence of his conduct \non that occasion.\n\nPenal Code                                            53 \n \n \nAct of a person of unsound mind \n \n84. Nothing is an offence which is done by a person who, at the time \nof doing it, by reason of unsoundness of mind, is incapable of knowing \nthe nature of the act, or that he is doing what is either wrong or contrary \nto law. \n \n \nIntoxication when a defence \n \n85. (1) \nSave as provided in this section and in section 86, \nintoxication shall not constitute a defence to any criminal charge. \n \n(2) Intoxication shall be a defence to any criminal charge if by \nreason thereof the person charged at the time of the act or omission \ncomplained of did not know that such act or omission was wrong or \ndid not know what he was doing and\u2014 \n \n(a) the state of intoxication was caused without his consent by \nthe malicious or negligent act of another person; or \n \n(b) the person charged was by reason of intoxication insane, \ntemporarily or otherwise, at the time of such act or \nomission. \n \n \nEffect of defence of intoxication when established \n \n86. (1) \nWhere the defence under subsection 85(2) is established, \nthen in a case falling under paragraph (a) thereof the accused person \nshall be acquitted, and in a case falling under paragraph (b), the \nprovisions of section 84 of this Code, sections 347 and 348 of the \nCriminal Procedure Code [Act 593] shall apply. \n \n(2) Intoxication shall be taken into account for the purpose of \ndetermining whether the person charged had formed any intention, \nspecific or otherwise, in the absence of which he would not be guilty \nof the offence.\n\n54                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \n(3) For the purpose of this and the preceding section \u201cintoxication\u201d \nshall be deemed to include a state produced by narcotics or drugs. \n \n \nAct not intended and not known to be likely to cause death or \ngrievous hurt, done by consent \n \n87. Nothing, which is not intended to cause death or grievous hurt, \nand which is not known by the doer to be likely to cause death or \ngrievous hurt, is an offence by reason of any harm which it may cause, \nor be intended by the doer to cause, to any person above eighteen years \nof age, who has given consent, whether express or implied, to suffer \nthat harm; or by reason of any harm which it may be known by the \ndoer to be likely to cause to any such person who has consented to take \nthe risk of that harm. \n \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nA and Z agree to fence with each other for amusement. This agreement \nimplies the consent of each to suffer any harm which, in the course of such \nfencing, may be caused without foul play; and if A, while playing fairly, hurts Z, \nA commits no offence. \n \n \nAct not intended to cause death, done by consent in good faith for \nthe benefit of a person \n \n88. Nothing, which is not intended to cause death, is an offence by \nreason of any harm which it may cause, or be intended by the doer to \ncause, or be known by the doer to be likely to cause, to any person for \nwhose benefit it is done in good faith, and who has given a consent, \nwhether express or implied, to suffer that harm, or to take the risk of \nthat harm. \n \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nA, a surgeon, knowing that a particular operation is likely to cause the death \nof Z, who suffers under a painful complaint, but not intending to cause Z\u2019s death,\n\nPenal Code                                            55 \n \nand intending in good faith, Z\u2019s benefit, performs that operation on Z, with Z\u2019s \nconsent. A has committed no offence. \n \n \nAct done in good faith for the benefit of a child or person of \nunsound mind, by or by consent of guardian \n \n89. Nothing, which is done in good faith for the benefit of a person \nunder twelve years of age, or of unsound mind, by or by consent, either \nexpress or implied, of the guardian or other person having lawful \ncharge of that person, is an offence by reason of any harm which it may \ncause, or be intended by the doer to cause, or be known by the doer to \nbe likely to cause, to that person: \n \nProvided that this exception shall not extend to\u2014 \n \n(a) the intentional causing of death, or to the attempting to \ncause death; \n \n(b) the doing of anything which the person doing it knows to \nbe likely to cause death for any purpose other than the \npreventing of death or grievous hurt, or the curing of any \ngrievous disease or infirmity; \n \n(c) the voluntary causing of grievous hurt, or to the attempting \nto cause grievous hurt, unless it be for the purpose of \npreventing death or grievous hurt, or the curing of any \ngrievous disease or infirmity; \n \n(d) the abetment of any offence, to the committing of which \noffence it would not extend. \n \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nA, in good faith, for his child\u2019s benefit, without his child\u2019s consent, has his \nchild cut for the stone by a surgeon, knowing it to be likely that the operation \nwill cause the child\u2019s death, but not intending to cause the child\u2019s death. A is \nwithin the exception, inasmuch as his object was the cure of the child.\n\n56                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nConsent known to be given under fear or misconception and \nconsent of a child or person of unsound mind \n \n90. A consent is not such a consent as is intended by any section of \nthis Code\u2014 \n \n(a) if the consent is given by a person under fear of injury, or \nunder a misconception of fact, and if the person doing the \nact knows, or has reason to believe, that the consent was \ngiven in consequence of such fear or misconception; \n \n(b) if the consent is given by a person who, from unsoundness \nof mind or intoxication, is unable to understand the nature \nand consequence of that to which he gives his consent; or \n \n(c) unless the contrary appears from the context, if the consent \nis given by a person who is under twelve years of age. \n \n \nActs which are offences independently of harm caused to the \nperson consenting, are not within the exceptions in sections 87, 88 \nand 89 \n \n91. The exceptions in sections 87, 88 and 89 do not extend to acts \nwhich are offences independently of any harm which they may cause, \nor be intended to cause, or be known to be likely to cause, to the person \ngiving the consent, or on whose behalf the consent is given. \n \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nCausing miscarriage, except in cases excepted under section 312, is an \noffence independently of any harm which it may cause or be intended to cause \nto the woman. Therefore it is not an offence \u201cby reason of such harm\u201d; and the \nconsent of the woman, or of her guardian, to the causing of such miscarriage \ndoes not justify the act.\n\nPenal Code                                            57 \n \nAct done in good faith for the benefit of a person without consent \n \n92. Nothing is an offence by reason of any harm which it may cause \nto a person for whose benefit it is done in good faith, even without \nthat person\u2019s consent, if the circumstances are such that it is \nimpossible for that person to signify consent, or if that person is \nincapable of giving consent, and has no guardian or other person in \nlawful charge of him from whom it is possible to obtain consent in \ntime for the thing to be done with benefit: \n \nProvided that, this exception shall not extend to\u2014 \n \n(a) the intentional causing of death, or the attempting to cause \ndeath; \n \n(b) the doing of anything which the person doing it knows to \nbe likely to cause death, for any purpose other than the \npreventing of death or grievous hurt, or the curing of any \ngrievous disease or infirmity; \n \n(c) the voluntary causing of hurt, or to the attempting to cause \nhurt,  for any purpose other than the preventing of death or \nhurt; \n \n(d) the abetment of any offence, to the committing of which \noffence it would not extend. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a) Z is thrown from his horse and is insensible. A, a surgeon, finds that Z \nrequires to be trepanned. A, not intending Z\u2019s death, but in good faith, for Z\u2019s \nbenefit, performs the trepan before Z recovers his power of judging for himself. \nA has committed no offence. \n \n(b) Z is carried off by a tiger. A fires at the tiger, knowing it to be likely \nthat the shot may kill Z, but not intending to kill Z, and in good faith intending \nZ\u2019s benefit. A\u2019s ball gives Z a mortal wound. A has committed no offence. \n \n(c) A, a surgeon, sees a child suffer an accident which is likely to prove \nfatal unless an operation be immediately performed. There is no time to apply to\n\n58                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nthe child\u2019s guardian. A performs the operation in spite of the entreaties of the \nchild, intending, in good faith, the child\u2019s benefit. A has committed no offence. \n \n(d) A is in a house which is on fire, with Z, a child. People below hold out \na blanket. A drops the child from the housetop, knowing it to be likely that the \nfall may kill the child, but not intending to kill the child, and intending in good \nfaith, the child\u2019s benefit. Here, even if the child is killed by the fall, A has \ncommitted no offence. \n \nExplanation\u2014Mere pecuniary benefit is not benefit within the meaning of \nsections 88, 89 and 92. \n \n \nCommunication made in good faith \n \n93. No communication made in good faith is an offence by reason \nof any harm to the person to whom it is made, if it is made for the \nbenefit of that person. \n \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nA, a surgeon, in good faith, communicates to a patient his opinion that he   \ncannot live.  The patient dies in consequence of the shock.  A has committed no \noffence, though he knew it to be likely that the communication might cause the \npatient\u2019s death. \n \n \nAct to which a person is compelled by threats \n \n94. Except murder, offences included in Chapter VI punishable with \ndeath and offences included in Chapter VIA, nothing is an offence \nwhich is done by a person who is compelled to do it by threats, which, \nat the time of doing it, reasonably cause the apprehension that instant \ndeath to that person will otherwise be the consequence: \n \nProvided that the person doing the act did not of his own accord, or \nfrom a reasonable apprehension of harm to himself short of instant \ndeath, place himself in the situation by which he became subject to \nsuch constraint.\n\nPenal Code                                            59 \n \nExplanation 1\u2014A person who, of his own accord, or by reason of a threat \nof being beaten, joins gang-robbers knowing their character, is not entitled to the \nbenefit of this exception on the ground of his having been compelled by his \nassociates to do anything that is an offence by law. \n \nExplanation 2\u2014A person seized by gang-robbers, and forced by threat of \ninstant death to do a thing which is an offence by law\u2014for example, a smith \ncompelled to take his tools and to force the door of a house for the gang-robbers \nto enter and plunder it\u2014is entitled to the benefit of this exception. \n \n \nAct causing slight harm \n \n95. Nothing is an offence by reason that it causes, or that it is \nintended to cause, or that it is known to be likely to cause, any harm, \nif that harm is so slight that no person of ordinary sense and temper \nwould complain of such harm. \n \n \nRight of Private Defence \n \nNothing done in private defence is an offence \n \n96. Nothing is an offence which is done in the exercise of the right \nof private defence. \n \n \nRight of private defence of the body and of property \n \n97. Every person has a right, subject to the restrictions contained in \nsection 99, to defend\u2014 \n \n(a) his own body, and the body of any other person, against \nany offence affecting the human body; \n \n(b) the property, whether movable or immovable, of himself \nor of any other person, against any act which is an offence \nfalling under the definition of theft, robbery, mischief or \ncriminal trespass, or which is an attempt to commit theft, \nrobbery, mischief or criminal trespass.\n\n60                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \n \nRight of private defence against the act of a person of unsound \nmind \n \n98. When an act, which would otherwise be a certain offence, is not \nthat offence, by reason of the youth, the want of maturity of \nunderstanding, the unsoundness of mind, or the intoxication of the \nperson doing that act, or by reason of any misconception on the part of \nthat person, every person has the same right of private defence against \nthat act which he would have if the act were that offence. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a) Z, under the influence of madness, attempts to kill A. Z is guilty of no \noffence. But A has the same right of private defence which he would have if Z \nwere sane. \n \n(b)  A enters, by night, a house which he is legally entitled to enter. Z, in \ngood faith, taking A, for a housebreaker, attacks A. Here Z, by attacking A, under \nthis misconception, commits no offence. But A has the same right of private \ndefence against Z, which he would have if Z were not acting under that \nmisconception. \n \n \nActs against which there is no right of private defence \n \n99. (1) \nThere is no right of private defence against an act which \ndoes not reasonably cause the apprehension of death or of grievous \nhurt, if done, or attempted to be done, by a public servant acting in \ngood faith under colour of his office, though that act may not be strictly \njustifiable by law. \n \n(2) There is no right of private defence against an act which does \nnot reasonably cause the apprehension of death or of grievous hurt, if \ndone, or attempted to be done, by the direction of a public servant \nacting in good faith under colour of his office, though that direction \nmay not be strictly justifiable by law. \n \n(3) There is no right of private defence in cases in which there is \ntime to have recourse to the protection of the public authorities.\n\nPenal Code                                            61 \n \n \n(4) The right of private defence in no case extends to the inflicting \nof more harm than it is necessary to inflict for the purpose of defence. \n \nExplanation 1\u2014A person is not deprived of the right of private defence \nagainst an act done, or attempted to be done, by a public servant, as such, unless \nhe knows, or has reason to believe, that the person doing the act is such public \nservant. \n \nExplanation 2\u2014A person is not deprived of the right of private defence \nagainst an act done, or attempted to be done, by the direction of a public servant, \nunless he knows, or has reason to believe, that the person doing the act is acting \nby such direction; or unless such person states the authority under which he acts, \nor, if he has authority in writing, unless he produces such authority, if demanded. \n \n \nWhen the right of private defence of the body extends to causing \ndeath \n \n100. The right of private defence of the body extends, under the \nrestrictions mentioned in the last preceding section, to the voluntary \ncausing of death or of any other harm to the assailant, if the offence \nwhich occasions the exercise of the right is of any of the following \ndescriptions: \n \n(a) such an assault as may reasonably cause the apprehension \nthat death will otherwise be the consequence of such \nassault; \n \n(b) such an assault as may reasonably cause the apprehension \nthat grievous hurt will otherwise be the consequence of \nsuch assault; \n \n(c) an assault with the intention of committing rape; \n \n(d) an assault with the intention of gratifying unnatural lust; \n \n(e) an assault with the intention of kidnapping or abducting; \n \n(f) an assault with the intention of wrongfully confining a \nperson, under circumstances which may reasonably cause\n\n62                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nhim to apprehend that he will be unable to have recourse \nto the public authorities for his release. \n \n \nWhen such right extends to causing any harm other than death \n \n101. If the offence is not of any of the descriptions enumerated in \nsection 100, the right of private defence of the body does not extend to \nthe voluntary causing of death to the assailant, but does extend, under \nthe restrictions mentioned in section 99, to the voluntary causing to the \nassailant of any harm other than death. \n \n \nCommencement and continuance of the right of private defence of \nthe body \n \n102. The right of private defence of the body commences as soon as \na reasonable apprehension of danger to the body arises from an attempt \nor threat to commit the offence, though the offence may not have been \ncommitted; and it continues as long as such apprehension of danger to \nthe body continues. \n \n \nWhen the right of private defence of property extends to causing \ndeath \n \n103. The right of private defence of property extends, under the \nrestrictions mentioned in section 99, to the voluntary causing of death \nor of any other harm to the wrongdoer, if the offence, the committing \nof which, or the attempting to commit which, occasions the exercise of \nthe right, is an offence of any of the following descriptions: \n \n(a) robbery; \n \n(b) housebreaking by night; \n \n(c) mischief by fire committed on any building, tent or vessel, \nwhich building, tent or vessel is used as a human dwelling, \nor as a place for the custody of property;\n\nPenal Code                                            63 \n \n \n(d) theft, \nmischief \nor \nhouse-trespass, \nunder \nsuch \ncircumstances as may reasonably cause apprehension that \ndeath or grievous hurt will be the consequence, if such \nright of private defence is not exercised. \n \n \nWhen such right extends to causing any harm other than death \n \n104. If the offence, the committing of which, or the attempting to \ncommit which, occasions the exercise of the right of private defence, \nis theft, mischief or criminal trespass, not of any of the descriptions \nenumerated in section 103, that right does not extend to the voluntary \ncausing of death, but does extend subject to the restrictions mentioned \nin section 99, to the voluntary causing to the wrongdoer of any harm \nother than death. \n \n \nCommencement and continuance of the right of private defence of \nproperty \n \n105. (1) The right of private defence of property commences when \na reasonable apprehension of danger to the property commences. \n \n(2) The right of private defence of property against theft continues \ntill the offender has effected his retreat with the property, or till \nassistance of the public authorities is obtained, or till the property has \nbeen recovered. \n \n(3) The right of private defence of property against robbery \ncontinues as long as the offender causes or attempts to cause to any \nperson death, or hurt, or wrongful restrain, or as long as the fear of \ninstant death, or of instant hurt, or of instant personal restraint \ncontinues. \n \n(4) The right of private defence of property against criminal \ntrespass or mischief, continues as long as the offender continues in the \ncommission of criminal trespass or mischief.\n\n64                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \n(5) The right of private defence of property against housebreaking \nby night continues as long as house-trespass which has been begun by \nsuch housebreaking continues. \n \n \nRight of private defence against a deadly assault when there is risk \nof harm to an innocent person \n \n106. If, in the exercise of the right of private defence against an \nassault which reasonably causes the apprehension of death, the \ndefender is so situated that he cannot effectually exercise that right \nwithout risk of harm to an innocent person, his right of private defence \nextends to the running of that risk. \n \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \n A is attacked by a mob who attempt to murder him. He cannot effectually \nexercise his right of private defence without firing on the mob, and he cannot \nfire without risk of harming young children who are mingled with the mob. A \ncommits no offence if by so firing he harms any of the children. \n \n \nCHAPTER V \n \nABETMENT \n \nAbetment of a thing \n \n107. A person abets the doing of a thing who\u2014 \n \n(a) instigates any person to do that thing; \n \n(aa) commands any person to do that thing; \n \n(b) engages with one or more other person or persons in any \nconspiracy for the doing of that thing, if an act or illegal \nomission takes place in pursuance of that conspiracy, and \nin order to the doing of that thing; or\n\nPenal Code                                            65 \n \n(c) intentionally aids, by any act or illegal omission, the doing \nof that thing. \n \nExplanation 1\u2014A person who, by wilful misrepresentation, or by wilful \nconcealment of a material fact which he is bound to disclose, voluntarily causes \nor procures, or attempts to cause or procure, a thing to be done, is said to instigate \nthe doing of that thing. \n \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nA, a public officer, is authorized by a warrant from a Court to apprehend Z. \nB, knowing that fact and also that C is not Z, wilfully represents to A that C is Z, \nand thereby intentionally causes A to apprehend C. Here B abets by instigation \nthe apprehension of C. \n \nExplanation 2\u2014Whoever, either prior to or at the time of the commission \nof an act, does anything in order to facilitate the commission of that act, and \nthereby facilitates the commission thereof, is said to aid the doing of that act. \n \nExplanation 3\u2014Whoever masterminds the doing of an act is said to \ncommand the doing of that act. \n \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nA, the head of an organized criminal group B, masterminds C and D to \nkidnap E. A is guilty of abetment. \n \n \nAbettor \n \n108. A person abets an offence who abets either the commission of \nan offence, or the commission of an act which would be an offence, if \ncommitted by a person capable by law of committing an offence with \nthe same intention or knowledge as that of the abettor. \n \nExplanation 1\u2014The abetment of the illegal omission of an act may amount \nto an offence, although the abettor may not himself be bound to do that act. \n \nExplanation 2\u2014To constitute the offence of abetment, it is not necessary \nthat the act abetted should be committed, or that the effect requisite to constitute \nthe offence should be caused.\n\n66                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a) A instigates B to murder C.  B refuses to do so.  A is guilty of abetting \nB to commit murder. \n \n(b) A instigates B to murder D. B, in pursuance of the instigation stabs D. \nD recovers from the wound. A is guilty of instigating B to commit murder. \n  \nExplanation 3\u2014It is not necessary that the person abetted should be capable \nby law of committing an offence, or that he should have the same guilty intention \nor knowledge as that of the abettor, or any guilty intention or knowledge. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a) A, with a guilty intention, abets a child or a lunatic to commit an act \nwhich would be an offence if committed by a person capable by law of \ncommitting an offence, and having the same intention as A. Here A, whether the \nact is committed or not, is guilty of abetting an offence. \n \n(b) A, with the intention of murdering Z, instigates B, a child under seven \nyears of age, to do an act which causes Z\u2019s death. B, in consequence of  the  \nabetment,  does  the  act,  and  thereby  causes  Z\u2019s  death.  Here, though B was \nnot capable by law of committing an offence, A is liable to be punished in the \nsame manner as if B had been capable by law of committing an offence and had \ncommitted murder, and he is therefore subject to the punishment of death. \n \n(c) A instigates B to set fire to a dwelling house. B, in consequence of the \nunsoundness of his mind, being incapable of knowing the nature of the act, or \nthat he is doing what is wrong or contrary to law, sets fire to the house in \nconsequence of A\u2019s instigation. B has committed no offence, but A is guilty of \nabetting the offence of setting fire to a dwelling house, and is liable to the \npunishment provided for that offence. \n \n(d) A, intending to cause a theft to be committed, instigates B to take \nproperty belonging to Z out of Z\u2019s possession. A induces B to believe that the \nproperty belongs to A. B takes the property out of Z\u2019s possession, in good faith \nbelieving it to be A\u2019s property. B, acting under this misconception, does not take \ndishonestly, and therefore does not commit theft. But A is guilty of abetting theft, \nand is liable to the same punishment as if B had committed theft. \n \nExplanation 4\u2014The abetment of an offence being an offence, the abetment \nof such an abetment is also an offence.\n\nPenal Code                                            67 \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nA instigates B to instigate C to murder Z. B accordingly instigates C to \nmurder Z, and C commits that offence in consequence of B\u2019s instigation. B is \nliable to be punished for his offence with the punishment for murder; and as A \ninstigated B to commit the offence A is also liable to the same punishment. \n \nExplanation 5\u2014It is not necessary to the commission of the offence of \nabetment by conspiracy that the abettor should concert the offence with the \nperson who commits it. It is sufficient if he engages in the conspiracy in \npursuance of which the offence is committed. \n \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nA concerts with B a plan for poisoning Z. It is agreed that A shall administer \nthe poison. B then explains the plan to C, mentioning that a third person is to \nadminister the poison, but without mentioning A\u2019s name. C agrees to procure the \npoison, and procures and delivers it to B for the purpose of its being used in the \nmanner explained. A administers the poison; Z dies in consequence. Here, \nthough A and C have not conspired together, yet C has been engaged in the \nconspiracy in pursuance of which Z has been murdered. C has therefore \ncommitted the offence defined in this section, and is liable to the punishment for \nmurder. \n \n \nAbetment in Malaysia of offences outside Malaysia \n \n108A. \nA person abets an offence within the meaning of this Code who, \nin Malaysia, abets the commission of any act without and beyond \nMalaysia which would constitute an offence if committed in Malaysia. \n \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nA, in Malaysia, instigates B, a foreigner in Java, to commit murder in Java. \nA is guilty of abetting murder. \n \n \nPunishment of abetment if the act abetted is committed in \nconsequence, and where no express provision is made for its \npunishment \n \n109. Whoever abets any offence shall, if the act abetted is committed\n\n68                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nin consequence of the abetment, and no express provision is made by \nthis Code for the punishment of such abetment, be punished with the \npunishment provided for the offence. \n \nExplanation\u2014An act or offence is said to be committed in consequence of \nabetment, when it is committed in consequence of the instigation, or in \npursuance of the conspiracy, or with the aid which constitutes the abetment. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a) A offers a bribe to B, a public servant, as a reward for showing A   some \nfavour in the exercise of B\u2019s official functions. B accepts the bribe. A has abetted \nthe offence defined in section 161. \n \n(b) A instigates B to give false evidence. B, in consequence of the \ninstigation, commits that offence. A is guilty of abetting that offence, and is \nliable to the same punishment as B. \n \n(c) A and B conspire to poison Z. A, in pursuance of the conspiracy, \nprocures the poison and delivers it to B, in order that he may administer it to Z. \nB, in pursuance of the conspiracy administers the poison to Z in A\u2019s absence and \nthereby causes Z\u2019s death. Here B is guilty of murder. A is guilty of abetting that \noffence by conspiracy, and is liable to the punishment for murder. \n \n \nPunishment of abetment if the person abetted does the act with a \ndifferent intention from that of the abettor \n \n110. Whoever abets the commission of an offence shall, if the person \nabetted does the act with a different intention or knowledge from that of \nthe abettor, be punished with the punishment provided for the offence \nwhich would have been committed if the act had been done with the \nintention or knowledge of the abettor and with no other. \n \n \nLiability of abettor when one act is abetted and a different act is \ndone \n \n111. When an act is abetted and a different act is done, the abettor is \nliable for the act done, in the same manner, and to the same extent, as \nif he had directly abetted it:\n\nPenal Code                                            69 \n \n \nProvided that the act done was a probable consequence of the \nabetment, and was committed under the influence of the instigation, or \nwith the aid or in pursuance of the conspiracy which constituted the \nabetment. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a) A instigates a child to put poison into the food of Z, and gives him \npoison for that purpose. The child, in consequence of the instigation, by mistake \nputs the poison into the food of Y, which is by the side of that of Z. Here, if the \nchild was acting under the influence of A\u2019s instigation, and the act done was \nunder the circumstances a probable consequence of the abetment, A is liable in \nthe same manner, and to the same extent, as if he had instigated the child to put \nthe poison into the food of Y. \n \n(b) A instigates B to burn Z\u2019s house. B sets fire to the house, and at the same \ntime commits theft of property there. A, though guilty of the burning of the \nhouse, is not guilty of abetting the theft for the theft was a distinct act, and not a \nprobable consequence of the burning. \n \n(c) A, instigates B and C to break into an inhabited house at midnight for \nthe purpose of robbery, and provides them with arms for that purpose. B and C \nbreak into the house, and being resisted by Z, one of the inmates, murder Z. Here, \nif that murder was the probable consequence of the abetment, A is liable to the \npunishment provided for murder. \n \n \nAbettor, when liable to cumulative punishment for act abetted and \nfor act done \n \n112. If the act for which the abettor is liable under section 111 is \ncommitted in addition to the act abetted, and constitutes a distinct \noffence, the abettor is liable to punishment for each of the offences. \n \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nA instigates B to resist by force a distress made by a public servant. B, in \nconsequence, resists that distress. In offering the resistance, B voluntarily causes \ngrievous hurt to the officer executing the distress. As B has committed both the \noffence of resisting the distress, and the offence of voluntarily causing grievous \nhurt, B is liable to punishment for both these offences; and if A knew that B was\n\n70                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nlikely voluntarily to cause grievous hurt in resisting the distress, A will also be \nliable to punishment for each of the offences. \n \n \nLiability of abettor for an offence caused by the act abetted \ndifferent from that intended by the abettor \n \n113. When an act is abetted with the intention on the part of the \nabettor of causing a particular effect, and an act for which the abettor \nis liable in consequence of the abetment causes a different effect from \nthat intended by the abettor, the abettor is liable for the effect caused, \nin the same manner, and to the same extent, as if he had abetted the act \nwith the intention of causing that effect, provided he knew that the act \nabetted was likely to cause that effect. \n \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nA instigates B to cause grievous hurt to Z, B, in consequence of the \ninstigation, causes grievous hurt to Z. Z dies in consequence. Here, if A knew \nthat the grievous hurt abetted was likely to cause death,  A is liable to be punished \nwith the punishment provided for murder. \n \n \nAbettor present when offence committed \n \n114. Whenever any person who, if absent, would be liable to be \npunished as an abettor, is present when the act or offence for which he \nwould be punishable in consequence of the abetment is committed, he \nshall be deemed to have committed such act or offence. \n \n \nAbetment of an offence punishable with death or imprisonment \nfor life \n \n115. Whoever abets the commission of an offence punishable with \ndeath or imprisonment for life or imprisonment for a term which may \nextend to twenty years, shall, if that offence is not committed in \nconsequence of the abetment, and no express provision is made by this \nCode for the punishment of such abetment, be punished with\n\nPenal Code                                            71 \n \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to seven years, and shall \nalso be liable to fine; and shall if any act for which the abettor is liable \nin consequence of the abetment and which causes hurt to any person, \nis done, the abettor shall be liable to imprisonment for a term which \nmay extend to fourteen years, and shall also  be liable to fine. \n \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nA instigates B to murder Z. The offence is not committed. If B had murdered \nZ, he would have been subject to the punishment of death. Therefore, A is liable \nto imprisonment for a term which may extend to seven years, and also to a fine; \nand if any hurt be done to Z in consequence of the abetment, he will be liable to \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to fourteen years, and to fine. \n \n \nAbetment of an offence punishable with imprisonment \n \n116. Whoever abets an offence punishable with imprisonment shall, \nif that offence is not committed in consequence of the abetment, and \nno express provision is made by this Code for the punishment of such \nabetment, be punished with imprisonment for a term which may extend \nto one-fourth part of the longest term provided for that offence or with \nsuch fine as is provided for that offence or with both; and if the abettor \nor the person abetted is a public servant, whose duty it is to prevent the \ncommission of such offence, the abettor shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to one-half of the longest \nterm provided for that offence or with such fine as is provided for the \noffence or with both. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a) A offers a bribe to B, a public servant, as a reward for showing A some \nfavour in the exercise of B\u2019s official functions. B refuses to accept the bribe. A \nis punishable under this section. \n \n(b) A instigates B to give false evidence. Here, if B does not give false \nevidence, A has nevertheless committed the offence defined in this section, and \nis punishable accordingly. \n \n(c) A, a police officer, whose duty it is to prevent robbery, abets the \ncommission of robbery. Here, though the robbery is not committed, A is liable\n\n72                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nto one-half of the longest term of imprisonment provided for that offence, and \nalso to fine. \n \n(d)  B abets the commission of a robbery by A, a police officer, whose duty \nit is to prevent that offence. Here, though the robbery is not committed, B is \nliable to one-half of the longest term of imprisonment provided for the offence \nof robbery, and also to fine. \n \n \nAbetting the commission of an offence by the public, or by more \nthan ten persons \n \n117. Whoever abets the commission of an offence by the public \ngenerally, or by any number or class of persons exceeding ten, shall be \npunished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to three \nyears or with fine or with both. \n \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nA affixes in a public place a placard, instigating a sect consisting of more \nthan ten members, to meet at a certain time and place for the purpose of attacking \nthe members of an adverse sect while engaged in a procession. A has committed \nthe offence defined in this section. \n \n \nConcealing a design to commit an offence punishable with death \nor imprisonment for life \n \n118. Whoever, intending to facilitate, or knowing it to be likely that \nhe will thereby facilitate, the commission of an offence punishable \nwith death or  imprisonment for life or imprisonment for a term which \nmay extend to twenty years, voluntarily conceals, by any act or illegal \nomission, the existence of a design to commit such offence, or makes \nany representation which he knows to be false respecting such design, \nshall, if that offence is committed, be  punished with imprisonment for \na term which may extend to seven years, or if the offence is not \ncommitted, with imprisonment for a term which may  extend to three \nyears, and, in either case, shall also be liable to fine.\n\nPenal Code                                            73 \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nA, knowing that a gang-robbery is about to be committed at B, falsely \ninforms the police that a gang-robbery is about to be committed at C, a place in \nan opposite direction, and thereby misleads the police with intent to facilitate the \ncommission of the offence. The gang-robbery is committed at B in pursuance of \nthe design. A is punishable under this section. \n \n \nA public servant concealing a design to commit an offence which \nit is his duty to prevent \n \n119. Whoever, being a public servant, intending to facilitate, or \nknowing it to be likely that he will thereby facilitate, the commission \nof an offence, the commission of which it is his duty as such public \nservant  to prevent, voluntarily conceals, by any act or illegal omission, \nthe existence  of a design to commit such offence, or makes any \nrepresentation which he knows to be false respecting such design, \nshall, if the offence is committed, be punished with imprisonment for \na term which may extend to one-half of the longest term provided for \nthe offence or with such fine as is provided for the offence or with both; \nor if the offence is punishable with death or imprisonment for life or \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to twenty years, with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to ten years; or, if the \noffence is not committed, shall be punished with imprisonment for a \nterm which may extend to one-fourth part of the longest term provided \nfor the offence or with such fine as is provided for the offence or with \nboth. \n \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nA, an officer of police, being legally bound to give information of all designs \nto commit robbery, which may come to his knowledge, and knowing that B \ndesigns to commit robbery, omits to give such information, with intent to \nfacilitate the commission of that offence. Here A has by an illegal omission \nconcealed the existence of B\u2019s design, and is liable to punishment according to \nthis section.\n\n74                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nConcealing a design to commit an offence punishable with \nimprisonment \n \n120. Whoever, intending to facilitate, or knowing it to be likely that \nhe will thereby facilitate, the commission of an offence punishable \nwith imprisonment, voluntarily conceals, by any act or illegal \nomission, the existence of a design to commit such offence, or makes \nany representation which he knows to be false respecting such  design, \nshall, if the offence is committed, be punished with imprisonment for \na term which may extend to one-fourth, and if the offence is not \ncommitted, to one-eighth of the longest term provided for the offence \nor with such fine as is provided for the offence or with both. \n \n \nCHAPTER VA \n \nCRIMINAL CONSPIRACY \n \nDefinition of criminal conspiracy \n \n120A. \nWhen two or more persons agree to do, or cause to be done\u2014 \n \n(a) an illegal act; or \n \n(b) an act, which is not illegal, by illegal means, \n \nsuch an agreement is designated a criminal conspiracy: \n \nProvided that no agreement except an agreement to commit an \noffence shall amount to a criminal conspiracy unless some act besides \nthe agreement is done by one or more parties to such agreement in \npursuance thereof. \n \n \nExplanation 1\u2014It is immaterial whether the illegal act is the ultimate object \nof such agreement, or is merely incidental to that object. \n \nExplanation 2\u2014Where liability for any offence may be incurred without \nknowledge on the part of the person committing it of any particular fact or \ncircumstance necessary for the commission of the offence, a person shall\n\nPenal Code                                            75 \n \nnevertheless not be guilty of conspiracy to commit the offence unless he and at \nleast one other party to the agreement intend or know that that fact or \ncircumstance shall or will exist at the time when the conduct constituting the \noffence is to take place. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a) If A and B agree to embark on a bombing campaign throughout \nMalaysia, and either one of them commits an act in furtherance of the agreement \nsuch as acquiring Ammonium Nitrate fertilizer or other bomb making \ncomponents, they will each be guilty of conspiracy to cause explosions even \nthough no bombing targets were identified and no bombing was actually \nattempted. \n \n(b)  A wilfully and knowingly joins an enterprise of persons consisting of \nB, C and D where they share a common criminal purpose to commit certain \noffences such as attacking civilian objects, murder and terrorism, and at least \none of them acts on the plan by surveilling targets or securing a weapon to be \nused in the attacks. All four are guilty of conspiracy to attack civilian objects, \nand commit murder and terrorism the moment any one of them acts on the plan. \n \n(c) A and B agree to cheat the Government on a contract for goods by \ninflating the price of goods quoted in the tender document. A and B intend to \nconceal the real price of the goods to the Government.
