A sells to Z shares in a bank at a premium, when they are \nselling in the market at a discount. Z pays A for the shares accordingly. The \nmoney so obtained by A is a valuable thing obtained by him without adequate \nconsideration. \n \n \nPublic servant disobeying a direction of the law, with intent to \ncause injury to any person \n \n166. Whoever, being a public servant, knowingly disobeys any \ndirection of the law as to the way in which he is to conduct himself as\n\nPenal Code                                            123 \n \nsuch public servant, intending to cause, or knowing it to be likely that \nhe will, by such disobedience, cause injury to any person, shall be \npunished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to one year \nor with fine or with both. \n \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nA, being an officer directed by law to take property in execution, in order to \nsatisfy a decree pronounced in Z\u2019s favour by a Court, knowingly disobeys that  \ndirection of law, with the knowledge that he is likely thereby to cause injury to \nZ. A has committed the offence defined in this section. \n \n \nPublic servant framing an incorrect document with intent to cause \ninjury \n \n167. Whoever, being a public servant, and being, as such public \nservant, charged with the preparation or translation of any document, \nframes or translates that document in a manner which he knows or \nbelieves to be incorrect, intending thereby to cause, or knowing it to be \nlikely that he may thereby cause, injury to any person, shall be \npunished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to three \nyears or with fine or with both. \n \n \nPublic servant unlawfully engaging in trade \n \n168. Whoever, being a public servant, and being legally bound as \nsuch public servant not to engage in trade engages in trade, shall be \npunished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to one year \nor with fine or with both. \n \n \nPublic servant unlawfully buying or bidding for property \n \n169. Whoever, being a public servant, and being legally bound as \nsuch public servant not to purchase or bid for certain property, \npurchases or bids for that property, either in his own name or in the \nname of another, or jointly or in shares with others, shall be punished \nwith imprisonment for a term which may extend to two years or with\n\n124                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nfine or with both; and the property, if purchased, shall be confiscated. \n \n \nPersonating a public servant \n \n170. Whoever pretends to hold any particular office as a public \nservant, knowing that he does not hold such office, or falsely \npersonates any other person holding such office, and in such assumed \ncharacter does or attempts to do any act under colour of such office, \nshall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to \ntwo years or with fine or with both. \n \n \nWearing garb or carrying token used by public servant with \nfraudulent intent \n \n171. Whoever, not belonging to a certain class of public servants, \nwears any garb or carries any token resembling any garb or token used \nby that class of public servants, with the intention that it may be \nbelieved, or with the knowledge that it is likely to be believed, that he \nbelongs to that class of public servants, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to three months or with \nfine which may extend to four hundred ringgit or with both. \n \n \nCHAPTER X \n \nCONTEMPTS OF THE LAWFUL AUTHORITY OF PUBLIC \nSERVANTS \n \nAbsconding to avoid service of summons or other proceeding from \na public servant \n \n172. Whoever absconds in order to avoid being arrested on a warrant, \nor to avoid being served with a summons, notice or order proceeding \nfrom any public servant, legally competent, as such public servant, to \nissue such warrant, summons, notice or order, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to one month or with fine \nwhich may extend to one thousand ringgit or with both; or, if the\n\nPenal Code                                            125 \n \nsummons, notice or order is to attend in person or by agent, or to \nproduce a document before a Court, with imprisonment for a term \nwhich may extend to six months or with fine which may extend to two \nthousand ringgit or with both. \n \n \nPreventing service of summons or other proceeding, or preventing \npublication thereof \n \n173. Whoever in any manner intentionally prevents the serving on \nhimself, or on any other person, of any summons, notice or order, \nproceeding from any public servant legally competent, as such public \nservant, to issue such summons, notice or order, or intentionally \nprevents the lawful affixing to any place of any such summons, notice \nor order, or intentionally removes any such summons, notice or order \nfrom any place to which it is lawfully affixed, or intentionally prevents \nthe lawful making of any proclamation, under the authority of any \npublic servant legally competent, as such public servant, to direct such \nproclamation to be made, shall be punished, with imprisonment for a \nterm which may extend to one month or with fine which may extend \nto one thousand ringgit or with both; or, if the summons, notice, order \nor proclamation is to attend in person or by agent, or to produce a \ndocument before a Court, with imprisonment for a term which may \nextend to six months or with fine which may extend to two thousand \nringgit or with both. \n \n \nNon-attendance in obedience to an order from a public servant \n \n174. Whoever, being legally bound to attend in person or by an agent \nat a certain place and time in obedience to a summons, notice, order, \nor proclamation, proceeding from any public servant legally \ncompetent, as such public servant, to issue the same, intentionally \nomits to attend at that place or time, or departs from the place where \nhe is bound to attend before the time at which it is  lawful for him to \ndepart, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may \nextend to one month or with fine which may extend to one thousand \nringgit or with both; or, if the summons, notice, order or proclamation \nis to attend in person or by agent before a Court, with imprisonment \nfor a term which may extend to six months or with fine which may\n\n126                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nextend to two  thousand  ringgit or with both. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a) \nA, being legally bound to appear before the High Court at Kuala \nLumpur, in obedience to a subpoena issuing from that Court, intentionally omits \nto appear. A has committed the offence defined in this section. \n \n(b) A, being legally bound to appear before a Magistrate, as a witness, in \nobedience to a summons issued by that Magistrate, intentionally omits to appear. \nA has committed the offence defined in this section. \n \n \nOmission to produce a document to a public servant by a person \nlegally bound to produce such document \n \n175. Whoever, being legally bound to produce or deliver up any \ndocument to any public servant, as such, intentionally omits so to \nproduce or deliver up the same, shall be punished with imprisonment \nfor a term which may extend to one month or with fine which may \nextend to one thousand ringgit or with both; or, if the document is to \nbe produced or  delivered up to a Court, with imprisonment for a term \nwhich may extend to six months or with fine  which may extend to two \nthousand ringgit or with both. \n \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nA, being legally bound to produce a document before a Court of a \nMagistrate, intentionally omits to produce the same. A has committed the \noffence defined in this section. \n \n \nOmission to give notice or information to a public servant by a \nperson legally bound to give notice or information \n \n176. Whoever, being legally bound to give any notice or to furnish \ninformation on any subject to any public servant, as such, intentionally \nomits to give such notice or to furnish such information in the manner \nand at the time required by law, shall be  punished with imprisonment\n\nPenal Code                                            127 \n \nfor a term which may extend to one month or with fine which may \nextend to one thousand ringgit or with both; or, if the notice or \ninformation required to be given respects the commission of an \noffence, or is required for the  purpose of preventing the commission \nof an offence or in order to the  apprehension of an offender, with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to six months or with fine \nwhich may extend to two thousand ringgit or with both and in relation \nto offences under Chapter VIB, with imprisonment for a term which \nmay extend to seven years or with fine or with both. \n \n \nFurnishing false information \n \n177. Whoever, being legally bound to furnish information on any \nsubject to any public servant, as such, furnishes, as true, information \non the subject which he knows or has reason to believe to be false, shall \nbe punished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to six \nmonths or with fine which may extend to two thousand ringgit or with \nboth; or, if the information which he is legally bound to furnish \nrespects the commission of an offence, or is required for the purpose \nof preventing the commission of an offence or in order to the \napprehension of an offender, with imprisonment for a term which may \nextend to two years or with fine or with both. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a) A, a landholder, knowing of the commission of a murder, within the \nlimits of his estate, wilfully misinforms the police of the district that the death \nhas occurred by accident in consequence of the bite of a snake. A is guilty of the \noffence defined in this section. \n \n(b) A, a police officer, or Penghulu, knowing that a considerable body of \nstrangers has passed through his village in order to commit a gang-robbery in \nthe house of Z, a wealthy merchant residing in a neighbouring place, and being \nbound to give information of the above to his superior officer, wilfully \nmisinforms the officer that a body of suspicious characters passed through the \nvillage with a view to commit a gang-robbery in a certain distant place in a \ndifferent direction. Here A is guilty of the offence defined in this section. \n \nExplanation\u2014In section 176 and in this section the word \u201coffence\u201d includes \nany act committed at any place out of Malaysia, which if committed in Malaysia \nwould be punishable under any of the following sections, namely, 302, 304, 382,\n\n128                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \n392, 393, 394, 395, 396, 397, 399, 402, 435, 436, 449, 450, 457, 458, 459 and \n460, and the word \u201coffender\u201d includes any person who is alleged to have been \nguilty of any such act. \n \n \nRefusing oath when duly required to take oath by a public servant \n \n178. Whoever refuses to bind himself by an oath to state the truth, \nwhen required so to bind himself by a public servant legally competent \nto require that he shall so bind himself, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to six months or with fine \nwhich may extend to two thousand ringgit or with both. \n \n \nRefusing to answer a public servant authorized to question \n \n179. Whoever, being legally bound to state the truth on any subject \nto any public servant, refuses to answer any question demanded of him \ntouching that subject by such public servant, in the exercise of the legal \npowers of such public servant, shall be punished with imprisonment \nfor a term which may extend to six months or with fine which may \nextend to two thousand ringgit or with both. \n \n \nRefusing to sign statement \n \n180. Whoever refuses to sign any statement made by him, when \nrequired to sign that statement by a public servant legally competent to \nrequire that he shall sign that statement, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to three months or with \nfine which may extend to one thousand ringgit or with both. \n \n \nFalse statement on oath to public servant or person authorized to \nadminister an oath \n \n181. Whoever, being legally bound by an oath to state the truth on \nany subject to any public servant or other person authorized by law to \nadminister such oath, makes to such public servant or other person as\n\nPenal Code                                            129 \n \naforesaid, touching that subject, any statement which is false, and \nwhich he either knows or believes to be false or does not believe to be \ntrue, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may extend \nto three years, and shall also be liable to fine. \n \n \nFalse information, with intent to cause a public servant to use his \nlawful power to the injury of another person \n \n182. Whoever gives to any public servant any information orally or \nin writing which he knows or believes to be false, intending thereby to \ncause, or knowing it to be likely that he will thereby cause, such public \nservant to use the lawful power of such public servant to the injury or \nannoyance of any person, or to do or omit anything which such public \nservant ought not to do or omit if the true state of facts respecting which \nsuch information is given were known by him, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to six months or with fine \nwhich may extend to two thousand ringgit or with both. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a) A informs the Inspector General of Police that Z, a police officer \nsubordinate to the Inspector General, has been guilty of neglect of duty or \nmisconduct, knowing such information to be false, and knowing it to be likely \nthat the information will cause the Inspector General to commence disciplinary \nproceedings against Z. A has committed the offence defined in this section. \n \n(b) A falsely informs a public servant that Z has contraband opium in a \nsecret place, knowing such information to be false, and knowing that it is likely \nthat the consequence of the information will be a search of  Z\u2019s  premises,  \nattended  with  annoyance  to  Z. A has committed the offence defined in this \nsection. \n \n(c) A falsely informs a policeman that he has been assaulted and robbed in \nthe neighbourhood of a particular village. He does not mention the name of any \nperson as one of his assailants but knows it to be likely that in consequence of \nthis information the police will make inquiries and institute searches in the \nvillage to the annoyance of the villagers or some of them. A has committed an \noffence under this section.\n\n130                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nResistance to the taking of property by the lawful authority of a \npublic servant \n \n183. Whoever offers any resistance to the taking of any property by \nthe lawful authority of any public servant, knowing or having reason \nto believe that he is such public servant, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to six months or with fine \nwhich may extend to two thousand ringgit or with both. \n \n \nObstructing sale of property offered for sale by authority of a \npublic servant \n \n184.  Whoever intentionally obstructs any sale of property offered for \nsale by the lawful authority of any public servant, as such, shall be \npunished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to one month \nor with fine which may extend to one thousand ringgit or with both. \n \n \nIllegal purchase or bid for property offered for sale by authority \nof a public servant \n \n185. Whoever, at any sale of property held by the lawful authority of \na public  servant, as such, purchases or bids for any property on account \nof any person, whether himself or any other, whom he knows to be \nunder a legal incapacity to purchase that property at that sale, or bids \nfor such property not intending to perform the obligations under which \nhe lays himself by such bidding, shall be punished with imprisonment \nfor a term which may extend to one month or with fine which may \nextend to four hundred ringgit or with both. \n \n \nObstructing public servant in discharge of his public functions \n \n186. Whoever voluntarily obstructs any public servant in the \ndischarge of his public functions, shall be punished with imprisonment \nfor a term which may extend to two years or with fine which may \nextend to ten thousand ringgit or with both.\n\nPenal Code                                            131 \n \n \nOmission to assist public servant when bound by law to give \nassistance \n \n187. Whoever, being bound by law to render or furnish assistance to \nany public servant in the execution of his public duty, intentionally \nomits to give such assistance, shall be punished with imprisonment for \na term which may extend to one month or with fine which may extend \nto four hundred ringgit or with both; and if such assistance is demanded \nof him by a public servant legally competent to make such demand for \nthe purposes of executing any process lawfully issued by a Court, or \nof preventing the commission of an offence, or of suppressing a riot or \naffray, or of apprehending a person charged with or guilty of an \noffence, or of having escaped from lawful custody, shall be punished \nwith imprisonment for a term which may extend to six months or with \nfine which may extend to one  thousand ringgit or with both. \n \n \nDisobedience to an order duly promulgated by a public servant \n \n188. Whoever, knowing that by an order promulgated by a public \nservant lawfully empowered to promulgate such order he is directed to \nabstain from a certain act, or to take certain order with certain property \nin his possession or under his management, disobeys such direction, \nshall, if such disobedience causes or tends to cause obstruction, \nannoyance or injury, or risk of obstruction, annoyance or injury, to any \nperson lawfully employed, be punished with imprisonment for a term \nwhich may extend to one month or with fine which may extend to four \nhundred ringgit or with both; and if  such disobedience causes or tends \nto cause danger to human life, health or safety, or causes or tends to \ncause a riot or affray, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term \nwhich may extend to six months or with fine which may extend to two \nthousand ringgit or with both. \n \nExplanation\u2014It is not necessary that the offender should intend to produce \nharm, or contemplate his disobedience as likely to produce harm. It is sufficient \nthat he knows of the order which he disobeys, and that his disobedience \nproduces, or is likely to produce, harm.\n\n132                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nAn order is promulgated by a public servant lawfully empowered to \npromulgate such order, directing that a religious procession shall not pass down \na certain street. A knowingly disobeys the order, and thereby causes danger of \nriot. A has committed the offence defined in this section. \n \n \nThreat of injury to a public servant \n \n189. Whoever holds out any threat of injury to any public servant, or \nto any person in whom he believes that public servant to be interested, \nfor the purpose of inducing that public servant to do any act, or to \nforbear or delay to do any act, connected with the exercise of the public \nfunctions of such public servant, shall be punished with imprisonment \nfor a term which may extend to two years or with fine or with both. \n \n \nThreat of injury to induce any person to refrain from applying for \nprotection to a public servant \n \n190. Whoever holds out any threat of injury to any person for the \npurpose of inducing that person to refrain or desist from making a legal \napplication, for protection against any injury, to any public servant \nlegally empowered as such to give such protection or to cause such \nprotection to be given, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term \nwhich may extend to one year or with fine or with both. \n \n \nCHAPTER XI \n \nFALSE EVIDENCE AND OFFENCES AGAINST PUBLIC \nJUSTICE \n \nGiving false evidence \n \n191. Whoever, being legally bound by an oath, or by any express \nprovision of law to state the truth, or being bound by law  to make a \ndeclaration upon any subject, makes any statement which is false, and \nwhich he either knows or believes to be false, or does not believe to be\n\nPenal Code                                            133 \n \ntrue, is said to give false evidence. \n \n \nExplanation 1\u2014A statement is within the meaning of this section, whether \nit is made verbally or otherwise. \n \nExplanation 2\u2014A false statement as to the belief of the person attesting is \nwithin the meaning of this section, and a person may be guilty of giving false \nevidence by stating that he believes a thing which he does not believe, as well \nas by stating that he knows a thing which he does not know. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a) A, in support of a just claim which B has against Z for one thousand \nringgit, falsely swears on a trial that he heard Z admit the justice of B\u2019s claim. A \nhas given false evidence. \n \n(b)  A, being bound by an oath to state the truth, states that he believes a \ncertain signature to be the handwriting of Z, when he does not believe it to be \nthe handwriting of Z. Here A states that which he knows to be false, and therefore \ngives false evidence. \n \n(c)  A, knowing the general character of Z\u2019s handwriting states that he \nbelieves a certain signature to be the handwriting of Z; A in good faith believing \nit to be so. Here A\u2019s statement is merely as to his belief, and is true as to his \nbelief, and therefore, although the signature may not be the handwriting of Z, A \nhas not given false evidence. \n \n(d) A, being bound by an oath to state the truth, states that he knows that Z \nwas at a particular place on a particular day, not knowing anything upon the \nsubject. A gives false evidence as to whether Z was at that place on the day \nnamed, or not. \n \n(e) A, an interpreter or translator, gives or certifies as a true interpretation \nor translation of a statement or document which he is bound by oath to interpret \nor translate truly, that which is not and which he does not believe to  be a true \ninterpretation or translation. A has given false evidence. \n \n \nFabricating false evidence \n \n192. Whoever causes any circumstances to exist, or makes any false \nentry in any book or record, or makes any document containing a false \nstatement, intending that such circumstance, false entry, or false\n\n134                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nstatement may appear in evidence in a judicial proceeding, or in a \nproceeding taken by law before a  public servant as such, or before an \narbitrator, and that such circumstance,  false entry or false statement, \nso appearing in evidence, may cause any person, who in such \nproceeding is to form an opinion upon the evidence, to entertain an \nerroneous opinion touching any point material to the result of such  \nproceeding, is said \u201cto fabricate false evidence\u201d. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a) A puts jewels into a box belonging to Z, with the intention that they may \nbe found in that box, and that this circumstance may cause Z to be convicted of \ntheft. A has fabricated false evidence. \n \n(b) A makes a false entry in his shop-book for the purpose of using it as \ncorroborative evidence in a Court. A has fabricated false evidence. \n \n \n(c) A, with the intention of causing Z to be convicted of a criminal \nconspiracy, writes a letter in imitation of Z\u2019s handwriting, purporting to be \naddressed to an accomplice in such criminal conspiracy, and puts the letter in a \nplace which he knows that the officers of the police are likely to search. A has \nfabricated false evidence. \n \n \nPunishment for false evidence \n \n193. Whoever intentionally gives false evidence in any stage of a \njudicial proceeding, or fabricates false evidence for the purpose of \nbeing used in any stage of a judicial proceeding, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to seven years, and shall \nalso be liable to fine; and whoever intentionally gives or fabricates \nfalse evidence in any other case, shall be punished with imprisonment \nfor a term which may extend to three years, and shall also be liable to \nfine. \n \nExplanation 1\u2014A trial before a court martial is a judicial proceeding. \n \nExplanation 2\u2014An investigation directed by law preliminary to a \nproceeding before a Court, is a stage of a judicial proceeding, though that \ninvestigation may not take place before a Court.\n\nPenal Code                                            135 \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nA, in an enquiry before a Justice of the Peace for the purpose of ascertaining \nwhether Z ought to be committed for trial, makes on oath a statement which he \nknows to be false. As this enquiry is a stage of a judicial proceeding, A has given \nfalse evidence. \n \n \nGiving or fabricating false evidence with intent to procure \nconviction of a capital offence \n \n194. Whoever gives or fabricates false evidence, intending thereby to \ncause, or knowing it to be likely that he will thereby cause, any person \nto be convicted of an offence which is capital by the law for the time \nbeing in force in Malaysia, shall be punished with imprisonment for a \nterm which may extend to twenty years, and shall also be liable to fine; \nand if an innocent person is convicted and executed in consequence of \nsuch false evidence, the person who gives such false evidence shall be \npunished either with death or the punishment hereinbefore described. \n \n \nGiving or fabricating false evidence with intent to procure \nconviction of an offence punishable with imprisonment \n \n195. Whoever gives or fabricates false evidence, intending thereby to \ncause, or knowing it to be likely that he will thereby cause, any person \nto be convicted of an offence which by this Code is not capital, but \npunishable with imprisonment for life, or imprisonment for a term of \nseven years or upwards, shall be punished as a person convicted of that \noffence would be liable to be punished. \n \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nA gives false evidence before a Court, intending thereby to cause Z to be \nconvicted of a gang-robbery. The punishment of gang-robbery is imprisonment \nfor life, or imprisonment for a term which may extend to ten years, with or \nwithout fine. A, therefore, is liable to such imprisonment, with or without fine.\n\n136                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nUsing evidence known to be false \n \n196. Whoever corruptly uses or attempts to use as true or genuine \nevidence any evidence which he knows to be false or fabricated, shall be \npunished in the same manner as if he gave or fabricated false evidence. \n \n \nIssuing or signing a false certificate \n \n197. Whoever issues or signs any certificate required by law to be \ngiven or signed, or relating to any fact of which such certificate is by \nlaw admissible in evidence, knowing or believing that such certificate \nis false in any material point, shall be punished in the same manner as \nif he gave false evidence. \n \n \nUsing as a true certificate one known to be false in a material point \n \n198. Whoever corruptly uses or attempts to use any such certificate as a \ntrue certificate, knowing the same to be false in any material point, shall \nbe punished in the same manner as if he gave false evidence. \n \n \nFalse statement made in any declaration which is by law receivable \nas evidence \n \n199. Whoever, in any declaration made or subscribed by him, which \ndeclaration any Court, or any public servant or other person, is bound \nor authorized by law to receive as evidence of any fact, makes any \nstatement which is false, and which he either knows or believes to be \nfalse or does not believe to be true, touching any point material to the \nobject for which the declaration is made or used, shall be punished in \nthe same manner as if he gave false evidence. \n \n \nUsing as true any such declaration known to be false \n \n200. Whoever corruptly uses or attempts to use as true any such \ndeclaration knowing the same to be false in any material point, shall\n\nPenal Code                                            137 \n \nbe punished in the same manner as if he gave false evidence. \n \n \nExplanation\u2014A declaration which is inadmissible merely upon the ground \nof some informality, is a declaration within the meaning of sections 199 and 200. \n \n \nCausing disappearance of evidence of an offence committed, or \ngiving false information touching it, to screen the offender \n \n201. Whoever, knowing or having reason to believe that an offence \nhas been committed, causes any evidence of the commission of that \noffence to disappear with the intention of screening the offender from \nlegal punishment, or with the knowledge that he is likely thereby to \nscreen the offender from legal punishment, or with that intention or \nknowledge gives any information respecting the offence which he \nknows or believes to be false, shall, if the offence which he knows or \nbelieves to have been committed is punishable with death, be punished \nwith imprisonment for a term which may extend to seven years, and \nshall also be liable to fine; and if the offence is punishable with \nimprisonment for life or with imprisonment which may extend to ten \nyears, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may \nextend to three years, and shall also be liable to fine; and if  the offence \nis punishable with imprisonment for any term not extending to ten \nyears, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may \nextend to one-fourth part of the longest term of the imprisonment \nprovided for the offence or with fine or with both. \n \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nA, knowing that B has murdered Z, assists B to hide the body with the \nintention of screening B, from punishment. A is liable to imprisonment for seven \nyears, and also to fine. \n \n \nIntentional omission, by a person bound to inform, to give \ninformation of an offence \n \n202. Whoever, knowing or having reason to believe that an offence \nhas been committed, intentionally omits to give any information\n\n138                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nrespecting that offence which he is legally bound to give, shall be \npunished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to six \nmonths or with fine or with both. \n \n \nGiving false information respecting an offence committed \n \n203. Whoever, knowing or having reason to believe that an offence \nhas been committed, gives any information respecting that offence \nwhich he knows or believes to be false, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to two years or with fine \nor with both. \n \nExplanation\u2014In sections 201 and 202 and in this section the word \n\u201coffence\u201d includes any act committed at any place out of Malaysia which if \ncommitted in Malaysia would be punishable under any of the following sections, \nnamely, 302, 304, 382, 384, 385, 386, 387, 388, 389, 392, 393, 394, 395, 396, \n397, 399, 402, 435, 436, 449, 450, 457, 458, 459 and 460. \n \n \nDisclosure of information \n \n203A. (1) Whoever discloses any information or matter which has \nbeen obtained by him in the performance of his duties or the exercise \nof his functions under any written law shall be punished with fine of \nnot more than one million ringgit, or with imprisonment for a term \nwhich may extend to one year, or with both. \n \n(2) Whoever has any information or matter which to his knowledge \nhas been disclosed in contravention of subsection (1) who discloses \nthat information or matter to any other person shall be punished with \nfine of not more than one million ringgit, or with imprisonment for a \nterm which may extend to one year, or with both. \n \n \nDestruction of document to prevent its production as evidence \n \n204. Whoever secretes or destroys any document which he may be \nlawfully compelled to produce as evidence before a Court, or in any \nproceeding lawfully held before a public servant as such, or obliterates\n\nPenal Code                                            139 \n \nor renders illegible the whole or any part of such document with the \nintention of preventing the same from being produced or used as \nevidence before such Court or public servant as aforesaid, or after he \nshall have been lawfully summoned or required to produce the same \nfor that purpose, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which \nmay extend to two years or with  fine or with both. \n \n \nFalse personation for the purpose of any act or proceeding in a suit \n \n205. Whoever falsely personates another, and in such assumed \ncharacter makes any admission or statement, or confesses judgment, or \ncauses any process to be issued, or becomes bail or security, or does \nany other act in any suit or criminal prosecution, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to three years or with fine \nor with both. \n \n \nFraudulent removal or concealment of property to prevent its \nseizure as a forfeiture or in execution of a decree \n \n206. Whoever fraudulently removes, conceals, transfers, or delivers \nto any person any property or any interest therein, intending thereby to \nprevent that property or interest therein from being taken as a forfeiture \nor in satisfaction of a fine, under a sentence which has been \npronounced, or which he knows to be likely to be pronounced by a \nCourt or other competent authority, or from being taken in execution \nof a decree or order which has  been made, or which he knows to be \nlikely to be made by a Court in a civil suit, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to two years or with fine \nor with both. \n \n \nFraudulent claim to property to prevent its seizure as a forfeiture \nor in execution of a decree \n \n207. Whoever fraudulently accepts, receives or claims any property or \nany interest therein, knowing that he has no right or rightful claim to \nsuch property or interest, or practices any deception touching any right \nto any property or any interest therein, intending thereby to prevent that\n\n140                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nproperty or interest therein from being taken as a forfeiture or in \nsatisfaction of a fine under a sentence which has been pronounced, or \nwhich he knows to be likely to be pronounced by a Court or other \ncompetent authority, or from being taken in execution of a decree or \norder which has been made or which he knows to be likely to be made \nby a Court in a civil suit, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term \nwhich may extend to two years or with fine or with both. \n \n \nFraudulently suffering a decree for a sum not due \n \n208. Whoever fraudulently causes or suffers a decree or order to be \npassed against him at the suit of any person for a sum not due, or for a \nlarger sum than is due to such person, or for any property or interest in \nproperty to which such person is not entitled, or fraudulently causes or \nsuffers a decree or order to be executed against him after it has been \nsatisfied, or for anything in respect of which it has been satisfied, shall \nbe punished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to two \nyears or with fine or with both. \n \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nA institutes a suit against Z. Z, knowing that A is likely to obtain a decree \nagainst him, fraudulently suffers a judgment to pass against him for a larger \namount at the suit of B, who has no just claim against him, in order that B, either \non his own account or for the benefit of Z, may share in the proceeds of any sale \nof Z\u2019s property which may be made under A\u2019s decree. Z has committed an \noffence under this section. \n \n \nDishonestly making a false claim before a Court \n \n209. Whoever fraudulently, or dishonestly, or with intent to injure or \nannoy any person, makes before a Court any claim which he knows to \nbe false, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may \nextend to two years, and shall also be liable to fine.\n\nPenal Code                                            141 \n \nFraudulently obtaining a decree for a sum not due \n \n210. Whoever fraudulently obtains a decree or order against any \nperson for a sum not due, or for a larger sum than is due, or for any \nproperty or interest in property to which he is not entitled, or \nfraudulently causes a decree or order to be executed against any person \nafter it has been satisfied, or for anything in respect of which it has \nbeen satisfied, or fraudulently suffers or permits any such act to be \ndone in his name, shall be punished  with imprisonment for a term \nwhich may extend to two years or with fine or with  both. \n \n \nFalse charge of offence made with intent to injure \n \n211. Whoever, with intent to cause injury to any person, institutes or \ncauses to be instituted any criminal proceeding against that person, or \nfalsely charges any person with having committed an offence, knowing \nthat there is no just or lawful ground for such proceeding or charge \nagainst that person, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term \nwhich may extend to two years or with fine or with both; and if such \ncriminal proceeding is instituted on a false charge of an offence \npunishable with death, imprisonment for life, or imprisonment for \nseven years or upwards, shall be punishable with imprisonment for a \nterm which may extend to seven years, and shall also be liable to fine. \n \n \nHarbouring an offender \n \n212.  (1) Whenever an offence has been committed, whoever \nharbours or conceals a person whom he knows or has reason to believe \nto be the offender, with the intention of screening him from legal \npunishment, shall, if the offence is punishable with death, be punished \nwith imprisonment for a term which may extend to five years, and shall \nalso be liable to fine; and if the offence is punishable with \nimprisonment for life, or with imprisonment which may extend to ten \nyears, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may \nextend to three years, and shall also be liable to fine; and if the offence \nis punishable with imprisonment which may extend to one year but less \nthan ten years, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which \nmay extend to one-fourth part of the longest term of imprisonment\n\n142                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nprovided for the offence or with fine or with  both. \n \n(2) In this section \u201coffence\u201d includes any act committed at any place \nout of Malaysia which if committed in Malaysia would be punishable \nunder any of the following sections, namely, 302, 304, 382, 392, 393, \n394, 395, 396, 397, 399, 402, 435, 436, 449, 450, 457, 458, 459 and \n460, and every such act shall for the purposes of this section be deemed \nto be punishable as if the accused person had been guilty of it in \nMalaysia. \n \nException\u2014This provision shall not extend to any case in which the harbour \nor concealment is by the husband or wife of the offender. \n \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nA, knowing that B, has committed gang-robbery, knowingly conceals B in \norder to screen him from legal punishment. Here, as B is liable to imprisonment \nfor life, A is liable to imprisonment for a term not exceeding three years, and is \nalso liable to fine. \n \n \nTaking gifts, etc., to screen an offender from punishment \n \n213. Whoever accepts, or agrees to accept, or attempts to obtain any \ngratification for himself or any other person, or any restitution of \nproperty to himself or any other person, in consideration of his \nconcealing an offence, or of his screening any person from legal \npunishment for any offence, or of his not proceeding against any \nperson for the purpose of bringing him to legal punishment shall, if the \noffence is punishable with death, be punished with imprisonment for a \nterm which may extend to seven years, and shall also be liable to fine; \nand if the offence is punishable with imprisonment for life, or with \nimprisonment which may extend to ten years, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to three years, and shall \nalso be liable to fine; and if the offence is punishable with \nimprisonment not extending to ten years, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to one-fourth part of the \nlongest term of imprisonment provided for the offence or with fine or \nwith both.\n\nPenal Code                                            143 \n \n \n \nOffering gift or restoration of property in consideration of \nscreening offender \n \n214. Whoever gives or causes, or offers or agrees to give or cause, \nany gratification to any person, or to restore or cause the restoration of \nany property to any person, in consideration of that person\u2019s \nconcealing an offence, or of his screening any person from legal \npunishment for any offence, or of his not proceeding against any \nperson for the purpose of bringing him to legal punishment, shall, if \nthe offence is punishable with death be punished with imprisonment \nfor a term which may extend to seven years, and shall also be liable to \nfine; and if the offence is punishable with imprisonment for life, or \nwith imprisonment which may extend to ten years, shall be punished \nwith imprisonment for a term which may extend to three years, and \nshall also be liable to fine; and if the offence is punishable with \nimprisonment not extending to ten years, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to one-fourth part of the \nlongest term of imprisonment provided for the offence or with fine or \nwith both. \n \n \nException\u2014The provisions of sections 213 and 214 do not extend to any \ncase in which the offence may lawfully be compounded. \n \n \nTaking gift to help to recover stolen property, etc. \n \n215. Whoever takes, or agrees or consents to take, any gratification \nfor himself or any other person under pretence or on account of helping \nany person to recover any movable property of which he shall have \nbeen deprived by any offence punishable under this Code, shall, unless \nhe uses all means in his power to cause the offender to be apprehended \nand convicted of the offence, be punished with imprisonment for a \nterm which may extend to two years or with fine or with both.\n\n144                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nHarbouring an offender who has escaped from custody, or whose \napprehension has been ordered \n \n216. (1) Whenever any person convicted of, or charged with an \noffence, being in lawful custody for that offence, escapes from such \ncustody, or whenever a public servant, in the exercise of the lawful \npowers of such public servant, orders a certain person to be \napprehended for an offence, whoever, knowing of such escape or order \nfor apprehension, harbours or conceals that person with the intention \nof preventing him from being apprehended, shall be punished in the \nmanner following, that is to say, if the offence for which the person \nwas in custody, or is ordered to be apprehended, is punishable with \ndeath, he shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may \nextend to seven years, and shall also be  liable to fine; if the offence is \npunishable with imprisonment for life, or imprisonment for ten years, \nhe shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may extend \nto three years, with or without fine; and if the offence is punishable \nwith imprisonment for not less than one year but less than ten  years, \nhe shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may extend \nto one-fourth part of the longest term of the imprisonment provided for \nsuch offence or with fine or with both. \n \n(2) In this section \u201coffence\u201d includes also any act or omission of \nwhich a person is alleged to have been guilty out of Malaysia which if \nhe had been  guilty of it in Malaysia would have been punishable as an \noffence and for which he is under any law relating to extradition or \nfugitive offences, or otherwise liable to be apprehended or detained in \ncustody in Malaysia and every such act or omission shall for the \npurpose of this section be deemed to  be punishable as if the accused \nperson had been guilty of it in Malaysia. \n \n \nException\u2014This provision does not extend to the case in which the harbour \nor concealment is by the husband or wife of the person to be apprehended. \n \n \nHarbouring robbers or gang-robbers, etc. \n \n216A. Whoever, knowing or having reason to believe that any persons\n\nPenal Code                                            145 \n \nare about to commit or have recently committed robbery or gang-\nrobbery, harbours them or any of them with the intention of facilitating \nthe commission of such robbery or gang-robbery or of screening them \nor any of them from punishment, shall be punished with imprisonment \nfor a term which may extend to seven years, and shall also be liable to \nfine. \n \nExplanation\u2014For the purpose of this section it is immaterial whether the \nrobbery or gang-robbery is intended to be committed or has been committed \nwithin or without Malaysia. \n \nException\u2014This provision does not extend to the case in which the \nharbouring is by the husband or wife of the offender. \n \n \n\u201cHarbour\u201d \n \n216B. In sections 212, 216 and 216A the word \u201charbour\u201d includes the \nsupplying a person with shelter, food, drink, money, clothes, arms, \nammunition or means of conveyance, or assisting a person in any way \nto evade apprehension. \n \n \nPublic servant disobeying a direction of law with intent to save \nperson from punishment, or property from forfeiture \n \n217. Whoever, being a public servant, knowingly disobeys any \ndirection of the law as to the way in which he is to conduct himself as \nsuch public servant, intending thereby to save, or knowing it to be \nlikely that he will thereby save, any person from legal punishment, or \nsubject him to a less punishment than that to which he is liable, or with \nintent to save, or knowing that he is likely thereby to save, any property \nfrom forfeiture or any charge to which it is liable by law, shall be \npunished with imprisonment for  a term which may extend to two years \nor with fine or with both. \n \n \nPublic servant framing an incorrect record or writing with intent \nto save person from punishment, or property from forfeiture \n \n218. Whoever, being a public servant, and being, as such public\n\n146                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nservant, charged with the preparation of any record or other writing, \nframes that record or writing in a manner which he knows to be \nincorrect, with intent to cause, or knowing it to be likely that he will \nthereby cause, loss or injury to the public or to any person, or with \nintent thereby to save, or knowing it to be likely that he will thereby \nsave, any person from legal punishment, or with intent to save, or \nknowing that he is likely thereby to save, any property from forfeiture \nor other charge to which it is liable by law, shall be  punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to three years or with fine \nor with both. \n \n \nPublic servant in a judicial proceeding corruptly making an order, \nreport, etc., which he knows to be contrary to law \n \n219. Whoever, being a public servant, corruptly or maliciously \nmakes or pronounces in any stage of a judicial proceeding, any report, \norder, verdict or decision which he knows to be contrary to law, shall \nbe punished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to seven \nyears or with fine or with both. \n \n \nCommitment for trial or confinement by a person having authority \nwho knows that he is acting contrary to law \n \n220. Whoever, being in any office which gives him legal authority to \ncommit persons for trial or to confinement, or to keep persons in \nconfinement, corruptly or maliciously commits any person for trial or \nto confinement, or keeps any person in confinement, in the exercise of \nthat authority, knowing that in so doing he is acting contrary to law, \nshall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to \nseven years or with fine or with both. \n \n \nIntentional omission to apprehend on the part of a public servant \nbound by law to apprehend \n \n221. Whoever, being a public servant, legally bound as such public \nservant to apprehend or to keep in confinement any person charged\n\nPenal Code                                            147 \n \nwith or liable to be apprehended for an offence, intentionally omits to \napprehend such person, or intentionally suffers such person to escape, \nor intentionally aids such person in escaping or attempting to escape \nfrom such confinement, shall be punished as follows: \n \n(a) with imprisonment for a term which may extend to seven \nyears, with or without fine, if the person in confinement, \nor who ought to have been apprehended, was charged with \nor liable to be apprehended for an offence punishable with \ndeath; \n \n(b) with imprisonment for a term which may extend to three \nyears, with or without fine, if the person in confinement, \nor who ought to have been apprehended, was charged with \nor liable to be apprehended for an offence punishable with \nimprisonment for life, or imprisonment for a term which \nmay extend to ten years; or \n \n(c) with imprisonment for a term which may extend to two \nyears, with or without fine, if the person in confinement, or \nwho ought to have been apprehended, was charged with or \nliable to be apprehended for an offence punishable with \nimprisonment for a term less than ten years. \n \n \nIntentional omission to apprehend on the part of a public servant \nbound by law to apprehend person under sentence of a Court \n \n222. Whoever, being a public servant, legally bound as such public \nservant to apprehend or to keep in confinement any person under \nsentence of a Court for any offence, or lawfully committed to custody, \nintentionally omits to apprehend such person, or intentionally suffers \nsuch person to escape, or intentionally aids such person in escaping or \nattempting to escape from such confinement, shall be punished as \nfollows: \n \n(a) with imprisonment for a term which may extend to twenty \nyears, with or without fine, if the person in confinement, \nor who ought to have been apprehended, is under sentence \nof death;\n\n148                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \n \n(b) with imprisonment for a term which may extend to seven \nyears, with or without fine, if the person in confinement, \nor who ought to have been apprehended, is subject, by a \nsentence of a Court, or by virtue of a commutation of such \nsentence, to imprisonment for a term which may extend to \ntwenty years; or \n \n(c) with imprisonment for a term which may extend to three \nyears or with fine or with both, if the person in \nconfinement, or who ought to have been apprehended, is \nsubject, by a sentence of a Court, to imprisonment for a \nterm not exceeding ten years, or if the person was lawfully \ncommitted to custody. \n \n \nEscape from confinement negligently suffered by a public servant \nand facilitating or enabling any terrorist act, etc. \n \n223. (1) \nWhoever, being a public servant, legally bound as such \npublic servant to keep in confinement any person charged with or \nconvicted of any offence, or lawfully committed to custody, \nnegligently suffers such person to escape from confinement, shall be \npunished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to two years \nor with fine or with both. \n \n(2) Whoever commits an offence under subsection (1) to facilitate \nor enable any terrorist act or organized criminal activity shall be \npunished with imprisonment for a term of twice as long as the \nmaximum term for which he would have been liable on conviction for \nthat offence, and shall also be liable to whipping. \n \n \nResistance or obstruction by a person to his lawful apprehension \n \n224. Whoever intentionally offers any resistance or illegal \nobstruction to the lawful apprehension of himself for any offence with \nwhich he is charged, or of which he has been convicted, or escapes or \nattempts to escape from any custody in which he is lawfully detained\n\nPenal Code                                            149 \n \nfor any such offence, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term \nwhich may extend to two years or with fine or with both. \n \nExplanation\u2014The punishment in this section is in addition to the \npunishment for which the person to be apprehended or detained in custody was \nliable for the offence with which he was charged, or of which he was convicted. \n \n \nResistance or obstruction to the lawful apprehension of another \nperson \n \n225. Whoever intentionally offers any resistance or illegal \nobstruction to the lawful apprehension of any other person for an \noffence, or rescues or attempts to rescue any other person from any \ncustody in which that person is lawfully detained for an offence\u2014 \n \n(a) shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may \nextend to two years or with fine or with both; \n \n(b) if the person to be apprehended, or the person rescued, or \nattempted to be rescued, is charged with or liable to be \napprehended for an offence punishable with imprisonment \nfor a term which may extend to twenty years, shall be \npunished with imprisonment for a term which may extend \nto three years, and shall also be liable to fine; \n \n(c) if the person to be apprehended or rescued, or attempted to \nbe rescued, is charged with or liable to be apprehended for \nan offence punishable with death, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to seven years, \nand shall also be liable to fine; \n \n(d) if the person to be apprehended or rescued, or attempted to \nbe rescued, is liable, under the sentence of a Court, or by \nvirtue of a commutation of such a sentence, to \nimprisonment for a term of ten years or upwards, shall be \npunished with imprisonment for a term which may extend \nto seven years, and shall also be liable to fine; or \n \n(e) if the person to be apprehended or rescued, or attempted to \nbe rescued, is under sentence of death, shall be punished\n\n150                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nwith imprisonment for a term which may extend to twenty \nyears, and shall also be liable to fine. \n \n \nPublic servant omitting to apprehend or suffering other persons \nto escape in cases not already provided for \n \n225A. \n(1) Whoever, being a public servant legally bound as such \npublic servant to apprehend or to keep in confinement any person in \nany case not provided for in section 221, 222 or 223, or in any other \nlaw for the time being in force, omits to apprehend that person or \nsuffers him to escape from confinement shall be punished\u2014 \n \n(a) if he does so intentionally, with imprisonment for a term \nwhich may extend to three years or with fine or with both; \nor \n \n(b) if he does so negligently, with imprisonment for a term \nwhich may extend to two years or with fine or with both. \n \n(2) Whoever, in any case not provided for in section 224 or 225, or \nin any other law for the time being in force, intentionally offers any \nresistance or illegal obstruction to the lawful apprehension of himself \nor of any other person, or escapes or attempts to escape from any \ncustody in which he is lawfully detained, or rescues or attempts to \nrescue any other person from any custody in which that person is \nlawfully detained, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term \nwhich may extend to six months or with fine or with both. \n \n \nOffences against laws of Malaysia where no special punishment is \nprovided \n \n225B. Whoever does anything which by any law in force in Malaysia \nhe is prohibited from doing, or omits to do anything which he is so \nenjoined to do, shall, when no special punishment is provided by the \nlaw for such commission or omission, be punished with imprisonment \nfor a term which may extend to twelve months or with fine which may \nextend to two thousand ringgit or, with both.\n\nPenal Code                                            151 \n \n \n226. (Deleted by Ord. 11 of 1959). \n \n \nViolation of condition of remission of punishment \n \n227. Whoever, having accepted any conditional remission of \npunishment, knowingly violates any condition on which such \nremission was granted, shall be punished with the punishment to \nwhich he was originally sentenced if he has already suffered no part \nof that punishment, and if he has suffered any part of that punishment, \nthen with so much of that punishment as he has not already suffered. \n \n \nIntentional insult or interruption to a public servant sitting in any \nstage of a judicial proceeding \n \n228. Whoever intentionally offers any insult or causes any \ninterruption to any public servant, while such public servant is sitting \nin any stage of a judicial proceeding, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to six months or with fine \nwhich may extend to two thousand ringgit or with both. \n \n \nPersonation of a juror or assessor \n \n229. Whoever, by personation or otherwise, intentionally cause or \nknowingly suffer himself to be returned, empanelled or sworn as \njuryman or an assessor in any case in which he knows that he is not \nentitled by law to be so returned, empanelled or sworn, or knowing \nhimself to have been so returned, empanelled or sworn contrary to \nlaw, voluntarily serve on such jury or as such assessor, shall be \npunished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to two \nyears or with fine or with both.\n\n152                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nCHAPTER XII \n \nOFFENCES RELATING TO COIN AND GOVERNMENT \nSTAMPS \n \nInterpretation \n \n230. \u201cCoin\u201d is metal used as money stamped and issued by the \nauthority of the Government or by the authority of any State or \nsovereign power in order to be so used. \n \n\u201cCounterfeit\u201d includes the causing of a genuine coin to appear like a \ndifferent coin if it is done with the intention of practising deception or \nwith the knowledge that deception will thereby be caused. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a) Cowries are not coin. \n \n(b) Lumps of unstamped metal, though used as money, are not coin. \n \n(c) \nMedals are not coin, inasmuch as they are not intended to be used as \nmoney. \n \n \n231. (Deleted by Act A538). \n \n \nCounterfeiting coin \n \n232. Whoever counterfeits or knowingly performs any part of the \nprocess of counterfeiting coin, shall be punished with imprisonment \nfor a term which may extend to twenty years, and shall also be liable \nto fine. \n \n \n233. (Deleted by Act A327).\n\nPenal Code                                            153 \n \nMaking or selling instrument for counterfeiting coin \n \n234. Whoever makes or mends, or performs any part of the process \nof making or mending, or buys, sells, or disposes of any die or \ninstrument for the purpose of being used, or knowing or having reason \nto believe that it is intended to be used, for the purpose of \ncounterfeiting coin, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term \nwhich may extend to seven years, and shall also be liable to fine. \n \n \nPossession of instrument or material for the purpose of using the \nsame for counterfeiting coin \n \n235. Whoever is in possession of any instrument or material for the \npurpose of using the same for counterfeiting coin, or knowing or \nhaving reason to believe that the same is intended to be used for that \npurpose, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may \nextend to ten years, and shall also be liable to fine. \n \n \nAbets the counterfeiting of coin out of Malaysia \n \n236. Whoever, being within Malaysia, abets the counterfeiting of \ncoin out of Malaysia, shall be punished in the same manner as if he \nabetted the counterfeiting of such coin within Malaysia. \n \n \n237. (Deleted by Act A327). \n \n \nImport or export of counterfeit coin \n \n238. Whoever imports or exports any counterfeit coin which he \nknows or has reason to believe to be counterfeit, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to twenty years, and shall \nalso be liable to fine.\n\n154                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \n239. (Deleted by Act A327). \n \n \nDelivery of coin, possessed with the knowledge that it is counterfeit \n \n240. Whoever, having any counterfeit coin which at the time when \nhe became possessed of it he knew to be a counterfeit coin, \nfraudulently or with intent that fraud may be committed, delivers the \nsame to any person, or attempts to induce any person to receive it, shall \nbe punished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to ten \nyears, and shall also be liable to fine. \n \n \nDelivery to another of coin as genuine, which when first possessed \nthe deliverer did not know to be counterfeit \n \n241. Whoever delivers to any other person as genuine, or attempts to \ninduce any other person to receive as genuine, any counterfeit coin \nwhich he knows to be counterfeit, but which he did not know to be \ncounterfeit at the time when he took it into his possession, shall be \npunished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to five years, \nand shall also be liable to fine. \n \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nA, a coiner, delivers counterfeit coins to his accomplice B, for the purpose of \nuttering them. B sells the coins to C, another utterer, who buys them knowing them \nto be counterfeit. C pays away the coins for goods to D, who receives them, not \nknowing them to be counterfeit. D, after receiving the coins discovers that they are \ncounterfeit, and pays them away as if they were good. Here D is punishable only \nunder this section, but B and C are punishable under section 240. \n \n \n242. (Deleted by Act A327).\n\nPenal Code                                            155 \n \nPossession of coin by a person who knew it to be counterfeit when \nhe became possessed thereof \n \n243. Whoever, fraudulently or with intent that fraud may be \ncommitted, is in possession of counterfeit coin, having known at the \ntime when he became possessed of it that it was a counterfeit, shall be \npunished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to seven \nyears, and shall also be liable to fine. \n \n \n244\u2013245. \n(There are no ss. 244\u2013245). \n \n \n246. (Deleted by Act A327). \n \n \nFraudulently or dishonestly diminishing the weight or altering the \ncomposition of coin \n \n247. Whoever fraudulently or dishonestly performs on any coin any \noperation which diminishes the weight or alters the composition of that \ncoin, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may \nextend to seven years, and shall also be liable to fine. \n \n \n248. (Deleted by Act A327). \n \n \nAltering appearance of coin with intent that it shall pass as a coin \nof a different description \n \n249. Whoever performs on any coin any operation which alters the \nappearance of that coin, with the intention that the said coin shall pass \nas a coin of a different description, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to seven years, and shall \nalso be liable to fine. \n \n250. (Deleted by Act A327).\n\n156                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nDelivery of coin, possessed with the knowledge that it is altered \n \n251. Whoever, having coin in his possession with respect to which \nthe offence defined in section 247 or 249 has been committed, and \nhaving known at the time when he became possessed of such coin that \nsuch offence had been committed with respect to it, fraudulently or \nwith intent that fraud may be  committed, delivers such coin to any \nother person, or attempts to induce any other person to receive the \nsame, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may \nextend to ten years, and shall also be liable to fine. \n \n \n252. (Deleted by Act A327). \n \n \nPossession of coin by a person who knew it to be altered when he \nbecame possessed thereof \n \n253. Whoever, fraudulently or with intent that fraud may be \ncommitted, is in possession of coin with respect to which the offence \ndefined in section 247 or 249 has been committed, having known at \nthe time of becoming possessed thereof that such offence had been \ncommitted with respect to such coin, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to five years, and shall also \nbe liable to fine. \n \n \nDelivery to another of coin as genuine, which when first possessed, \nthe deliverer did not know to be altered \n \n254. Whoever delivers to any other person as genuine or as a coin of \na different description from what it is, or attempts to induce any person \nto receive as genuine or as a different coin from what it is, any coin in \nrespect of which he knows that any such operation as that mentioned \nin section 247 or 249, has been performed, but in respect of which he \ndid not, at the time when he took it into his possession, know that such \noperation had been performed, shall be punished with imprisonment \nfor a term which may  extend to five years, and shall also be liable to \nfine.\n\nPenal Code                                            157 \n \n \nCounterfeiting a Government stamp \n \n255. Whoever counterfeits, or knowingly performs any part of the \nprocess of counterfeiting, any stamp issued by Government for the \npurpose of revenue, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term \nwhich may extend to twenty years, and shall also be liable to fine. \n \n \nExplanation\u2014A person commits this offence who counterfeits by causing \na genuine stamp of one denomination to appear like a genuine stamp of a \ndifferent denomination. \n \n \nHaving possession of an instrument or material for the purpose of \ncounterfeiting a Government stamp \n \n256. Whoever has in his possession any instrument or material for \nthe purpose of being used, or knowing or having reason to believe that \nit is intended to be used, for the purpose of counterfeiting any stamp \nissued by Government for the purpose of revenue, shall be punished \nwith imprisonment for a term which may extend to seven years, and \nshall also be liable to fine. \n \n \nMaking or selling an instrument for the purpose of counterfeiting \na Government stamp \n \n257. Whoever makes, or performs any part of the process of making, \nor buys, or sells, or disposes of, any instrument for the purpose of being \nused, or knowing or having reason to believe that it is intended to be \nused, for the purpose of counterfeiting any stamp issued by \nGovernment for the purpose of revenue, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to seven years, and shall \nalso be liable to fine.\n\n158                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nSale of counterfeit Government stamp \n \n258. Whoever sells, or offers for sale, any stamp which he knows or \nhas reason to believe to be a counterfeit of any stamp issued by \nGovernment for the purpose of revenue, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to seven years, and shall \nalso be liable to fine. \n \n \nHaving possession of a counterfeit Government stamp \n \n259. Whoever has in his possession any stamp which he knows to be \na counterfeit of any stamp issued by Government for the purpose of \nrevenue, intending to use or dispose of the same as a genuine stamp, \nor in order that it may be used as a genuine stamp, shall be punished \nwith imprisonment for a term which may extend to seven years, and \nshall also be liable to fine. \n \n \nUsing as genuine a Government stamp known to be counterfeit \n \n260. Whoever uses as genuine any stamp, knowing it to be a \ncounterfeit of any stamp issued by Government for the purpose of \nrevenue, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may \nextend to seven years or with fine or with both. \n \n \nEffacing any writing from a substance bearing a Government \nstamp, or removing from a document a stamp used for it, with \nintent to cause loss to Government \n \n261. Whoever, fraudulently or with intent to cause loss to the \nGovernment, removes or effaces from any substance bearing any \nstamp issued by Government for  the purpose of revenue, any writing \nor document for which such stamp has been used, or removes from any \nwriting or document a stamp which has been used for such writing or \ndocument, in order that such stamp may be used for a different writing \nor document, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which \nmay extend to three years or with fine or with both.\n\nPenal Code                                            159 \n \n \nUsing a Government stamp known to have been before used \n \n262. Whoever, fraudulently or with intent to cause loss to the \nGovernment, uses for any purpose a stamp issued by Government for \nthe purpose of revenue, which he knows to have been before used, shall \nbe punished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to two \nyears or with fine or with both. \n \n \nErasure of mark denoting that stamp has been used \n \n263. Whoever, fraudulently or with intent to cause loss to \nGovernment, erases or removes from a stamp issued by Government \nfor the purpose of revenue, any mark put or impressed upon such stamp \nfor the purpose of denoting that the same has been used, or knowingly \nhas in his possession, or sells or disposes of, any such stamp from \nwhich such mark has been erased or removed, or sells or disposes of \nany such stamp which he knows to have been used, shall be punished \nwith imprisonment for a term which may extend to three years or with \nfine or with both. \n \n \nCHAPTER XIII \n \nOFFENCES RELATING TO WEIGHTS AND MEASURES \n \nFraudulent use of false instrument for weighing \n \n264. Whoever fraudulently uses any instrument for weighing which \nhe knows to be false, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term \nwhich may extend to one year or with fine or with both. \n \n \nFraudulent use of false weight or measure \n \n265. Whoever fraudulently uses any false weight or false measure of \nlength or capacity, or fraudulently uses any weight or any measure of \nlength or capacity as a different weight or measure from what it is, shall\n\n160                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nbe punished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to one \nyear or with fine or with both. \n \n \nBeing in possession of false weights or measures \n \n266. Whoever is in possession of any instrument for weighing, or of \nany weight, or of any measure of length or capacity, which he knows \nto be false, and intending that the same may be fraudulently used, shall \nbe punished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to one \nyear or with fine or with both. \n \n \nMaking or selling false weights or measures \n \n267. Whoever makes, sells, or disposes of, any instrument for \nweighing, or any weight, or any measure of length or capacity, which \nhe knows to be false, in order that the same may be used as true, or \nknowing that the same is likely to be used as true, shall be punished \nwith imprisonment for a term which may extend to one year or with \nfine or with both. \n \n \nCHAPTER XIV \n \nOFFENCES AFFECTING THE PUBLIC HEALTH, SAFETY, \nCONVENIENCE, DECENCY AND MORALS \n \nPublic nuisance \n \n268. (1) A person is guilty of a public nuisance, who does any act, \nor is guilty of an illegal omission, which causes any common injury, \ndanger, or annoyance to the public, or to the people in general who \ndwell or occupy property in the vicinity, or which must necessarily \ncause injury, obstruction, danger, or annoyance to persons who may \nhave occasion to use any public right. \n \n(2) A common nuisance is not excused on the ground that it causes \nsome convenience or advantage.\n\nPenal Code                                            161 \n \nNegligent act likely to spread infection of any disease dangerous to \nlife \n \n269. Whoever unlawfully or negligently does any act which is, and \nwhich he knows or has reason to believe to be, likely to spread the \ninfection of any disease dangerous to life, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to six months or with fine \nor with both. \n \n \nMalignant act likely to spread infection of any disease dangerous \nto life \n \n270. Whoever malignantly does any act which is, and which he \nknows or has reason to believe to be, likely to spread the infection of \nany disease dangerous to life, shall be punished with imprisonment for \na term which may extend to two years or with fine or with both. \n \n \nDisobedience to a quarantine rule \n \n271. Whoever knowingly disobeys any rule lawfully made and \npromulgated for putting any vessel into a state of quarantine, or for \nregulating the intercourse of vessels in a state of quarantine with the \nshore or with other vessels, or for regulating the intercourse between \nplaces where an infectious disease prevails and other places, shall be \npunished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to six \nmonths or with fine or with both. \n \n \nAdulteration of food or drink which is intended for sale \n \n272. Whoever adulterates any article of food or drink, so as to make \nsuch article noxious as food or drink, intending to sell such article as \nfood or drink, or knowing it to be likely that the same will be sold as \nfood or drink, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which \nmay extend to six months or with fine which may extend to two \nthousand ringgit or with both.\n\n162                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nSale of noxious food or drink \n \n273. Whoever sells, or offers or exposes for sale, as food or drink, \nany article which has been rendered or has become noxious, or is in a \nstate unfit for food or drink, knowing or having reason to believe that \nthe same is noxious as food or drink, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to six months or with fine \nwhich may extend to two thousand ringgit or with both. \n \n \nAdulteration of drugs \n \n274. Whoever adulterates any drug or medical preparation in such a \nmanner as to lessen the efficacy, or change the operation of such drug \nor medical preparation, or to make it noxious, intending that it shall be \nsold or used for, or knowing it to be likely that it will be sold or used \nfor  any medicinal purpose, as if it had not undergone such adulteration, \nshall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to \nsix months or with fine which may extend to two thousand ringgit or \nwith both. \n \n \nSale of adulterated drugs \n \n275. Whoever, knowing any drug or medical preparation to have \nbeen adulterated in such a manner as to lessen its efficacy, to change \nits operation, or to render it noxious, sells the same, or offers or exposes \nit for sale, or issues it from any dispensary for medicinal purposes as \nunadulterated, or causes it to be used for medicinal purposes by any \nperson not knowing of the adulteration, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to six months or with fine \nwhich may extend to two thousand ringgit. \n \n \nSale of any drug as a different drug or preparation \n \n276. Whoever knowingly sells, or offers or exposes for sale, or issues \nfrom a dispensary for medicinal purposes, any drug or medical \npreparation, as a different drug or medical preparation, shall be\n\nPenal Code                                            163 \n \npunished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to six \nmonths or with fine which may extend to two thousand ringgit or with \nboth. \n \n \nFouling the water of a public spring or reservoir \n \n277. Whoever voluntarily corrupts or fouls the water of any public \nspring or reservoir, so as to render it less fit for the purpose for which \nit is ordinarily used, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term \nwhich may extend to three months or with fine which may extend to \none thousand ringgit or with both. \n \n \nMaking atmosphere noxious to health \n \n278. Whoever voluntarily vitiates the atmosphere in any place so as \nto make it noxious to the health of persons in general dwelling or \ncarrying on business in the neighbourhood or passing along a public \nway, shall be punished with fine which may extend to one thousand \nringgit. \n \n \nRash driving or riding on a public way \n \n279. Whoever drives any vehicle, or rides on any public way in a \nmanner so rash or negligent as to endanger human life, or to be likely \nto cause hurt or injury to any other person, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to six months or with fine \nwhich may extend to two thousand ringgit or with both. \n \n \nRash navigation of a vessel \n \n280. Whoever navigates any vessel in a manner so rash or negligent \nas to endanger human life, or to be likely to cause hurt or injury to any \nother person, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which \nmay extend to six months or with fine which may extend to two \nthousand ringgit or with both.\n\n164                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nExhibition of a false light, mark or buoy \n \n281. Whoever exhibits any false light, mark or buoy, intending or \nknowing it to be likely that such exhibition will mislead any navigator, \nshall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to \nseven years or with fine or with both. \n \n \nConveying person by water for hire in a vessel overloaded or \nunsafe \n \n282. Whoever knowingly or negligently conveys, or causes to be \nconveyed for hire, any person by water in any vessel, when that vessel \nis in such a state or so loaded as to endanger the life of that person, \nshall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to \nsix months or with fine which may extend to two thousand ringgit or \nwith both. \n \n \nDanger or obstruction in a public way or navigation \n \n283.
