Whoever, by doing any act, or by omitting to take order with \nany property in his possession or under his charge, causes danger, \nobstruction or injury to any person in any public way or public line of \nnavigation, shall be punished with fine which may extend to four \nhundred ringgit. \n \n \nNegligent conduct with respect to any poisonous substance \n \n284. Whoever does, with any poisonous substance, any act in a \nmanner so  rash or negligent as to endanger human life, or to be likely \nto cause hurt or injury to any other person, or knowingly or negligently \nomits to take such order with any poisonous substance in his \npossession as is sufficient to guard against any probable danger to \nhuman life from such poisonous substance, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to six months or with fine \nwhich may extend to two thousand ringgit or with both.\n\nPenal Code                                            165 \n \nNegligent conduct with respect to any fire or combustible matter \n \n285. Whoever does, with fire or any combustible matter, any act so \nrashly or negligently as to endanger human life, or to be likely to cause \nhurt or injury to any other person, or knowingly or negligently omits \nto take such order with any fire or any combustible matter in his \npossession as is sufficient to guard against any probable danger to \nhuman life from such fire or combustible matter, shall be punished \nwith imprisonment for a term which may extend to six months or with \nfine which may extend to two thousand ringgit or with both. \n \n \nNegligent conduct with respect to any explosive substance \n \n286. Whoever does, with any explosive substance, any act  so rashly \nor negligently as to endanger human life, or to be likely to cause hurt \nor injury to any other person, or knowingly or negligently omits to take \nsuch order with any explosive substance in his possession as is \nsufficient to guard against any probable danger to human life from that \nsubstance, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may \nextend to six months or with fine which may extend to two thousand \nringgit or with both. \n \n \nNegligent conduct with respect to any machinery in the possession \nor under the charge of the offender \n \n287. Whoever does, with any machinery, any act so rashly or \nnegligently as to endanger human life, or to be likely to cause hurt or \ninjury to any other person, or knowingly or negligently omits to take \nsuch order with any machinery in his possession or under his care as is \nsufficient to guard  against any probable danger to human life from \nsuch machinery, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which \nmay extend to six months or with fine which may extend to two \nthousand ringgit or with both.\n\n166                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nNegligence with respect to pulling down or repairing buildings \n \n288. Whoever, in pulling down or repairing any building, knowingly \nor negligently omits to take such order with that building as is \nsufficient to guard against any probable danger to human life from the \nfall of that building, or of any part thereof, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to six months or with fine \nwhich may extend to two thousand ringgit or with both. \n \n \nNegligence with respect to any animal \n \n289. Whoever knowingly or negligently omits to take such order with \nany animal in his possession as is sufficient to guard against any \nprobable danger to human life, or any probable danger of grievous hurt \nfrom such animal, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term \nwhich may extend to six months or with fine which may extend to two \nthousand ringgit or with both. \n \n \nPunishment for public nuisance \n \n290. Whoever commits a public nuisance in any case not otherwise \npunishable by this Code, shall be punished with fine which may extend \nto four hundred ringgit. \n \n \nContinuance of nuisance after injunction to discontinue \n \n291. Whoever repeats or continues a public nuisance, having been \nenjoined by any public servant who has lawful authority to issue such \ninjunction not to repeat or continue such nuisance, shall be punished \nwith imprisonment for a term which may extend to six months or with \nfine or with both. \n \n \nSale, etc., of obscene books, etc. \n \n292. \nWhoever\u2014\n\nPenal Code                                            167 \n \n \n(a) sells, lets to hire, distributes, publicly exhibits or in any \nmanner puts into circulation, or for purposes of sale, hire, \ndistribution, public exhibition or circulation makes, \nproduces or has in his possession any obscene book, \npamphlet, paper, drawing, painting, representation or \nfigure or any other obscene object or document \nwhatsoever; \n \n(b) imports, exports or conveys any obscene object or \ndocument for any of the purposes aforesaid, or knowing or \nhaving reason to believe that such object or document will \nbe sold, let to hire, distributed or publicly exhibited or in \nany manner put into circulation;  \n \n(c) takes part in or receives profits from any business in the \ncourse of which he knows or has reason to believe that any \nsuch obscene objects or documents are for any of the \npurposes aforesaid, made, produced, purchased, kept, \nimported, exported, conveyed, publicly exhibited or in any \nmanner put into circulation; \n \n(d) advertises or makes known by any means whatsoever that \nany person is engaged or is ready to engage in any act \nwhich is an offence under this section, or that any such \nobscene object or document can be procured from or \nthrough any person; or \n \n(e) offers, or attempts to do any act which is an offence under \nthis section, \n \nshall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to \nthree years or with fine or with both. \n \nException\u2014This section does not extend to any book, pamphlet, writing, \ndrawing, or painting kept or used bona fide for religious purposes or any \nrepresentation sculptured, engraved, painted or otherwise represented on or in \nany temple, or on any car used for the conveyance of idols, or kept or used for \nany religious purpose.\n\n168                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nSale, etc., of obscene objects or documents to young person \n \n293. Whoever sells, lets to hire, distributes, exhibits or circulates to \nany person under the age of twenty years any such obscene object or \ndocument as is referred to in the last preceding section, or offers or \nattempts so to do, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term \nwhich may extend to five years or with fine or with both. \n \n \nObscene songs \n \n294. Whoever, to the annoyance of others\u2014 \n \n(a) does any obscene act in any public place; or \n \n(b) sings, recites or utters any obscene song, ballad or words \nin or near any public place, \n \nshall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to \nthree months or with fine or with both. \n \n \nCHAPTER XV \n \nOFFENCES RELATING TO RELIGION \n \nInjuring or defiling a place of worship with intent to insult the \nreligion of any class \n \n295. Whoever destroys, damages or defiles any place of worship, or \nany object held sacred by any class of persons, with the intention of \nthereby insulting the religion of any class of persons, or with the \nknowledge that any class of persons is likely to consider such \ndestruction, damage or defilement as an insult to their religion, shall \nbe punished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to two \nyears or with fine or with both.\n\nPenal Code                                            169 \n \nDisturbing a religious assembly \n \n296. Whoever voluntarily causes disturbance to any assembly \nlawfully engaged in the performance of religious worship or religious \nceremonies, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which \nmay extend to one year or with fine or with both. \n \n \nTrespassing on burial places, etc. \n \n297. Whoever, with the intention of wounding the feelings of any \nperson, or of insulting the religion of any person, or with the knowledge \nthat the feelings of any person are likely to be wounded, or that the religion \nof any person is likely to be insulted thereby, commits any trespass in any \nplace of worship or on any place of sepulture or any place set apart for the \nperformance of funeral rites, or as a depository for the remains of the dead, \nor offers any indignity to any human corpse, or causes disturbance to any \nperson assembled for the performance of funeral ceremonies, shall be \npunished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to one year or \nwith fine or with both. \n \n \nUttering words, etc., with deliberate intent to wound the religious \nfeelings of any person \n \n298. Whoever, with deliberate intention of wounding the religious \nfeelings of any person, utters any word or makes any sound in the \nhearing of that person, or makes any gesture in the sight of that person, \nor places any object in the sight of that person, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to one year or with fine or \nwith both. \n \n \nCausing, etc., disharmony, disunity, or feelings of enmity, hatred \nor ill will, or prejudicing, etc., the maintenance of harmony or \nunity, on grounds of religion \n \n298A. (1)  Whoever by words, either spoken or written, or by signs, or \nby visible representations, or by any act, activity or conduct, or by\n\n170                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \norganizing, promoting or arranging, or assisting in organizing, promoting \nor arranging, any activity, or otherwise in any other manner\u2014 \n \n(a) causes, or attempts to cause, or is likely to cause \ndisharmony, disunity, or feelings of enmity, hatred or ill \nwill; or \n \n(b) prejudices, or attempts to prejudice, or is likely to \nprejudice, the maintenance of harmony or unity, \n \non grounds of religion, between persons or groups of persons professing \nthe same or different religions, shall be punished with imprisonment for a \nterm of not less than two years and not more than five years. \n \n(2) Sections 173A and 294 of the Criminal Procedure Code shall not \napply in respect of an offence under subsection (1). \n \n(3) Where any person alleges or imputes in any manner specified in \nsubsection (1)\u2014 \n \n(a) that any other person, or any class, group or description of \npersons, professing any particular religion\u2014 \n \n(i) has ceased to profess that religion; \n \n(ii) should not be accepted, or cannot be accepted, as \nprofessing that religion; or \n \n(iii) does not believe, follow, profess, or belong to, that \nreligion; or \n \n(b) that anything lawfully done by any religious official \nappointed, or by any religious authority established, \nconstituted or appointed, by or under any written law, in \nthe exercise of any power, or in the discharge of any duty, \nor in the performance of any function, of a religious \ncharacter, by virtue of being so appointed, established or \nconstituted, is not acceptable to such person, or should not \nbe accepted by any other person or persons, or does not\n\nPenal Code                                            171 \n \naccord with or fulfil the requirements of that religion, or is \notherwise wrong or improper, \n \nhe shall be presumed to have contravened the provisions of  \nsubsection (1) by having acted in a manner likely to cause disharmony, \ndisunity or feelings of enmity, hatred or ill will, or likely to prejudice the \nmaintenance of harmony or unity, between persons or groups of persons \nprofessing the religion referred to in the allegation or imputation. \n \n(4) (a) Where, on any ground of a religious character, any person \nprofessing any particular religion uses for burial or cremation of any \nhuman corpse a place other than one which is lawfully used for such \npurpose by persons professing that religion, he shall be presumed to have \ncontravened the provisions of subsection (1) by having acted in a manner \nlikely to cause disharmony, disunity or feelings of enmity, hatred or ill \nwill, or likely to prejudice the maintenance of harmony or unity, between \npersons or groups of persons professing that religion. \n \n(b) Where any person, on any ground of a religious character, \ncounsels, advises, instigates, urges, pleads with, or appeals or \npropagates to, or in any manner or by any means call upon, whether \ndirectly or indirectly, any other person or persons professing any \nparticular religion\u2014 \n \n(i) to use for burial or cremation of any human corpse \na place other than one which is lawfully used for \nsuch purpose by persons professing that religion; \n \n(ii) not to use for burial or cremation of any human \ncorpse any place which is lawfully used for such \npurpose by persons professing that religion; or \n \n(iii) not to use for worship any place which is lawfully \nused for such purpose by persons professing that \nreligion, \n \nhe shall be presumed to have contravened the provisions of  \nsubsection (1) by having acted in a manner likely to cause disharmony, \ndisunity or feelings of enmity, hatred or ill will, or likely to prejudice\n\n172                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nthe maintenance of harmony or unity, between persons or groups of \npersons professing that religion or different religions. \n \n(5) Where any person who is not a religious official appointed, or a \nreligious authority established, constituted or appointed, by or under \nany written law purports to exercise any power, or to discharge any \nduty, or to perform any function, of a religious character, being a \npower, duty or function which can be lawfully exercised, discharged \nor performed only by a religious official appointed, or a religious \nauthority  established, constituted or appointed, by or under any written \nlaw, he shall be presumed to have contravened the provisions of \nsubsection (1) by having acted in a  manner likely to cause disharmony, \ndisunity or feelings of enmity, hatred or ill will, or likely to prejudice \nthe maintenance of harmony or unity, between persons or groups of \npersons professing the same or different religions. \n \n(6) The foregoing provisions of this section shall not apply to\u2014 \n \n(a) anything done by any religious authority established, \nconstituted or appointed by or under any written law and \nconferred by written law with power to give or issue any \nruling or decision on any matter pertaining to the religion \nin respect of which the authority is established, constituted \nor appointed; or \n \n(b) anything done by any person which is in pursuance of, or \nwhich accords with, any ruling or decision given or issued \nby such religious authority, whether or not such ruling or \ndecision is in writing, and if in writing, whether or not it is \npublished in the Gazette. \n \n(7) It shall not be a defence to any charge under this section to assert \nthat what the offender is charged with doing was done in any honest \nbelief in, or in any honest interpretation of, any precept, tenet or \nteaching of any religion. \n \n(8) If in any proceedings under this section any question arises with \nregard to the interpretation of any aspect of, or any matter in relation \nto, any religion, the Court shall accept the interpretation given by any\n\nPenal Code                                            173 \n \nreligious authority referred to in subsection (6), being a religious \nauthority in respect of that religion. \n \n \nCHAPTER XVI \n \nOFFENCES AFFECTING THE HUMAN BODY \n \nOffences Affecting Life \n \nCulpable homicide \n \n299. Whoever causes death by doing an act with the intention of \ncausing death, or with the intention of causing such bodily injury as is \nlikely to cause death, or with the knowledge that he is likely by such \nact to cause death, commits the offence of culpable homicide. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a)  A lays sticks and turf over a pit, with the intention of thereby causing \ndeath, or with the knowledge that death is likely to be thereby caused. Z, \nbelieving the ground to be firm, treads on it, falls in and is killed. A has \ncommitted the offence of culpable homicide. \n \n(b) A knows Z to be behind a bush. B does not know it. A, intending to \ncause, or knowing it to be likely to cause Z\u2019s death, induces B to fire at the bush. \nB fires and kills Z. Here B may be guilty of no offence, but A has committed the \noffence of culpable homicide. \n \n(c) A, by shooting at a fowl with intent to kill and steal it, kills B, who is \nbehind a bush; A not knowing that he was there. Here, although A was doing an \nunlawful act, he was not guilty of culpable homicide, as he did not intend to kill \nB, or to cause death by doing an act that he knew was likely to cause death. \n \nExplanation 1\u2014A person who causes bodily injury to another who is \nlabouring under a disorder, disease, or bodily infirmity, and thereby accelerates \nthe death of that other, shall be deemed to have caused his death. \n \nExplanation 2\u2014Where death is caused by bodily injury, the person who \ncauses such bodily injury shall be deemed to have caused the death, although by \nresorting to proper remedies and skilful treatment the death might have been \nprevented.\n\n174                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nExplanation 3\u2014The causing of the death of a child in the mother\u2019s womb \nis not homicide. But it may amount to culpable homicide to cause the death of a \nliving child, if any part of that child has been brought forth, though the child \nmay not have breathed or been completely born. \n \n \nMurder \n \n300. Except in the cases hereinafter excepted, culpable homicide is \nmurder\u2014 \n \n(a) if the act by which the death is caused is done with the \nintention of causing death; \n \n(b) if it is done with the intention of causing such bodily injury \nas the offender knows to be likely to cause the death of the \nperson to whom the harm is caused; \n \n(c) if it is done with the intention of causing bodily injury to \nany person, and the bodily injury intended to be inflicted \nis sufficient in the ordinary course of nature to cause death; \nor \n \n(d) if the person committing the act knows that it is so \nimminently dangerous that it must in all probability cause \ndeath, or such bodily injury as is likely to cause death, and \ncommits such act without any excuse for incurring the risk \nof causing death, or such injury as aforesaid. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a) A shoots Z with the intention of killing him. Z dies in consequence.  A \ncommits murder. \n \n(b) A, knowing that Z is labouring under such a disease that a blow is likely \nto cause his death, strikes him with the intention of causing bodily injury. Z dies \nin consequence of the blow. A is guilty of murder, although the blow might not \nhave been sufficient in the ordinary course of nature to cause the death of a \nperson in a sound state of health. But if A, not knowing that Z is labouring under \nany disease, gives him such a blow as would not in the ordinary course of nature \nkill a person in a sound state of health, here A, although he may intend to cause\n\nPenal Code                                            175 \n \nbodily injury, is not guilty of murder, if he did not intend to cause death, or such \nbodily injury as in the ordinary course of nature would cause death. \n \n(c) \nA intentionally gives Z a sword-cut or club-wound sufficient to cause \nthe death of a man in the ordinary course of nature. Z dies in consequence. Here \nA is guilty of murder, although he may not have intended to cause Z\u2019s death. \n \n(d) A, without any excuse, fires a loaded cannon into a crowd of persons \nand kills one of them. A is guilty of murder, although he may not have had a \npremeditated design to kill any particular individual. \n \nException 1\u2014Culpable homicide is not murder if the offender, whilst \ndeprived of the power of self control by grave and sudden provocation, causes \nthe death of the person who gave the provocation, or causes the death of any \nother person by mistake or accident. \n \nThe above exception is subject to the following provisos: \n \n(a)  that the provocation is not sought or voluntarily provoked by the \noffender as an excuse for killing or doing harm to any person; \n \n(b) that the provocation is not given by anything done in obedience to the \nlaw, or by a public servant in the lawful exercise of the powers of such \npublic servant; \n \n(c)  that the provocation is not given by anything done in the lawful \nexercise of the right of private defence. \n \nExplanation\u2014Whether the provocation was grave and sudden enough to \nprevent the offence from amounting to murder, is a question of fact. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a) A, under the influence of passion excited by a provocation given by Z, \nintentionally kills Y, Z\u2019s child. This is murder, inasmuch as the provocation \nwas not given by the child, and the death of the child was not caused by \naccident or misfortune in doing an act caused by the provocation. \n \n(b) Y gives grave and sudden provocation to A. A, on this provocation, fires a \npistol at Y, neither intending nor knowing himself to be likely to kill Z, who \nis near him, but out of sight.  A kills Z. Here A has not committed murder, \nbut merely culpable homicide. \n \n(c) A is lawfully arrested by Z, a bailiff. A is excited to sudden and violent \npassion by the arrest, and kills Z. This is murder, inasmuch as the \nprovocation was given by a thing done by a public servant in the exercise \nof his powers.\n\n176                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \n \n (d) A appears as a witness before Z, a Magistrate. Z says that he does not believe \na word of A\u2019s deposition, and that A has perjured himself. A is moved to \nsudden passion by these words, and kills Z. This is murder. \n \n(e) A attempts to pull Z\u2019s nose. Z, in the exercise of the right of private defence, \nlays hold of A to prevent him from doing so. A is moved to sudden and \nviolent passion in consequence, and kills Z. This is murder, inasmuch as the \nprovocation was given by a thing done in the exercise of the right of private \ndefence. \n \n(f) Z strikes B. B is by this provocation excited to violent rage. A, a bystander, \nintending to take advantage of B\u2019s rage, and to cause him to kill Z, puts a \nknife into B\u2019s hand for that purpose. B kills Z with the knife.  Here  B  may  \nhave  committed  only  culpable  homicide,  but  A  is guilty of murder. \n \nException  2\u2014Culpable  homicide  is  not  murder  if  the  offender,  in the \nexercise in good faith of the right of private defence of person or property, \nexceeds the power given to him by law, and causes the death of  the person  \nagainst whom he  is exercising such right of defence, without premeditation  and  \nwithout any intention of doing more harm than is necessary for the purpose of \nsuch defence. \n \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nZ attempts to horsewhip A, not in such a manner as to cause grievous hurt \nto A.  A draws out a pistol. Z persists in the assault. A, believing in good faith \nthat he can by no other means prevent himself from being horsewhipped, shoots \nZ dead. A has not committed murder, but only culpable homicide. \n \nException 3\u2014Culpable homicide is not murder if the offender, being a \npublic servant, or aiding a public servant acting for the advancement of public \njustice, exceeds the powers given to him by law, and causes death by doing an \nact which he, in good faith, believes to be lawful and necessary for the due \ndischarge of his duty as such public servant, and without ill will towards the \nperson whose death is caused. \n \nException 4\u2014Culpable homicide is not murder if it is committed without \npremeditation in a sudden fight in the heat of passion upon a sudden quarrel, and \nwithout the offender having taken undue advantage or acted in a cruel or unusual \nmanner. \n \nExplanation\u2014It is immaterial in such cases which party offers the \nprovocation or commits the first assault.\n\nPenal Code                                            177 \n \nException 5\u2014Culpable homicide is not murder when the person whose \ndeath is caused, being above the age of eighteen years, suffers death, or takes \nthe risk of death with his own consent. \n \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nA, by instigation, voluntarily causes Z, a person under eighteen years of age, \nto commit suicide. Here, on account of Z\u2019s youth, he was incapable of giving \nconsent to his own death. A has therefore abetted murder. \n \n \nCulpable homicide by causing the death of a person other than the \nperson whose death was intended \n \n301. If a person, by doing anything which he intends or knows to be \nlikely to cause death, commits culpable homicide by causing the death \nof any person whose death he neither intends nor knows himself to be \nlikely to cause, the culpable homicide committed by the offender is of \nthe description of which it would have been if he had caused the death \nof the person whose death he intended or knew himself to be likely to \ncause. \n \n \nPunishment for murder \n \n302. Whoever commits murder shall be punished with death. \n \n \n303. (There is no s. 303). \n \n \nPunishment for culpable homicide not amounting to murder \n \n304. Whoever commits culpable homicide not amounting to murder \nshall be punished\u2014 \n \n(a) with imprisonment for a term which may extend to thirty \nyears, and shall also be liable to fine, if the act by which the \ndeath is caused is done with the intention of causing death,\n\n178                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nor of causing such bodily injury as is likely to cause death; \nor \n \n(b) with imprisonment for a term which may extend to ten \nyears or with fine or with both, if the act is done with the \nknowledge that it is likely to cause death, but without any \nintention to cause death, or to cause such bodily injury as \nis likely to cause death. \n \n \nCausing death by negligence \n \n304A. Whoever causes the death of any person, by doing any rash or \nnegligence act not amounting to culpable homicide, shall be punished \nwith imprisonment for a term which may extend to two years or with \nfine or with both. \n \n \nAbetment of suicide of child or insane person \n \n305. If any person under eighteen years of age, any insane person, \nany delirious person, any idiot, or any person in a state of intoxication, \ncommits suicide, whoever abets the commission of such suicide shall \nbe punished with death or imprisonment for a term which may extend \nto twenty years, and shall also be liable to fine. \n \n \nAbetment of suicide \n \n306. If any person commits suicide, whoever abets the commission \nof such suicide shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which \nmay extend to ten years, and shall also be liable to fine. \n \n \nAttempt to murder \n \n307. (1) Whoever does any act with such intention or knowledge \nand under such circumstances, that if he by that act caused death he \nwould be guilty of murder, shall be punished with imprisonment for a\n\nPenal Code                                            179 \n \nterm which may extend to ten years, and shall also be liable to fine; \nand if hurt is caused to any person by such act, the offender shall be \nliable to imprisonment for a term which may extend to twenty years. \n \n(2) When any person offending under this section is under sentence \nof imprisonment for life or for a term of twenty years, he may, if hurt \nis caused, be punished with death. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a) A shoots at Z with intention to kill him, under such circumstances that, \nif death ensued, A would be guilty of murder. A is liable to punishment under \nthis section. \n \n(b) A, with the intention of causing the death of a child of tender years, \nexposes it in a desert place. A has committed the offence defined by this section, \nthough the death of the child does not ensue. \n \n(c)  A, intending to murder Z, buys a gun and loads it. A has not yet \ncommitted the offence. A fires the gun at Z. He has committed the offence \ndefined in this section; and if by such firing he wounds Z, he is liable to the \npunishment by the latter part of this section. \n \n(d) A, intending to murder Z by poison, purchases poison and mixes the \nsame with food which remains in A\u2019s keeping; A has not yet committed the \noffence defined in this section.  A places the food on Z\u2019s table or delivers it to \nZ\u2019s servants to place it on Z\u2019s table. A has committed the offence defined in this \nsection. \n \n \nAttempt to commit culpable homicide \n \n308. Whoever does any act with such intention or knowledge and \nunder such circumstances that if he by that act caused death he would \nbe guilty of culpable homicide not amounting to murder, shall be \npunished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to three \nyears or with fine or with both; and if hurt is caused to any person by \nsuch act, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may \nextend to seven years or with fine or with both.\n\n180                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nA, on grave and sudden provocation, fires a pistol at Z, under such \ncircumstances that if he thereby caused death he would be guilty of culpable \nhomicide not amounting to murder. A has committed the offence defined in this \nsection. \n \n \nAttempt to commit suicide \n \n309. Whoever attempts to commit suicide, and does any act towards \nthe commission of such offence, shall be punished with imprisonment \nfor a term which may extend to one year or with fine or with both. \n \n \nInfanticide \n \n309A. When any woman by any wilful act or omission causes the \ndeath of her newly-born child, but at the time of the act or omission \nshe had not fully recovered from the effect of giving birth to such child, \nand by reason thereof the balance of her mind was then disturbed, she \nshall, notwithstanding that the circumstances were such that but for \nthis section the offence would have amounted to murder, be guilty of \nthe offence of infanticide. \n \n \nPunishment for infanticide \n \n309B. Whoever commits the offence of infanticide shall be punished \nat the discretion of the Court, with imprisonment for a term which may \nextend to twenty years, and shall also be liable to fine. \n \n \n310\u2013311. \n(There are no ss. 310\u2013311).\n\nPenal Code                                            181 \n \nCausing Miscarriage; Injuries to Unborn Children; Exposure \nof Infants; and Concealment of Births \n \n \nCausing miscarriage \n \n312. Whoever voluntarily causes a woman with child to miscarry \nshall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to \nthree years or with fine or with both; and if the woman is quick with \nchild, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may \nextend to seven years, and shall also be liable to fine. \n \n \nExplanation\u2014A woman who causes herself to miscarry is within the \nmeaning of this section. \n \nException\u2014This section does not extend to a medical practitioner registered \nunder the Medical Act 1971 [Act 50] who terminates the pregnancy of a woman \nif such medical practitioner is of the opinion, formed in good faith, that the \ncontinuance of the pregnancy would involve risk to the life of the pregnant \nwoman, or injury to the mental or physical health of the pregnant woman, greater \nthan if the pregnancy were terminated. \n \n \nCausing miscarriage without woman\u2019s consent \n \n313. Whoever commits the offence defined in section 312, without \nthe consent of the woman, whether the woman is quick with child or \nnot, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may extend \nto twenty years, and shall also be liable to fine. \n \n \nDeath caused by act done with intent to cause miscarriage. If act \ndone without woman\u2019s consent  \n \n314. Whoever, with intent to cause the miscarriage of a woman with \nchild, does any act which causes the death of such woman, shall be \npunished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to ten years, \nand shall also be liable to fine; and if the act is done without the consent \nof the woman, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which \nmay extend to twenty years.\n\n182                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \n \nExplanation\u2014It is not essential to this offence that the offender should \nknow that the act is likely to cause death. \n \n \nAct done with intent to prevent a child being born alive or to cause \nit to die after birth \n \n315. Whoever before the birth of any child does any act with the \nintention of thereby preventing that child from being born alive, or \ncausing it to die after its birth, and does by such act prevent that child \nfrom being born alive, or causes it to die after its birth, shall, if such \nact is not caused in good faith for the purpose of saving the life of the \nmother, be punished with imprisonment for a term which may extend \nto ten years or with fine or with both. \n \n \nCausing death of a quick unborn child by an act amounting to \nculpable homicide \n \n316. Whoever does any act under such circumstances that if he \nthereby caused death he would be guilty of culpable homicide, and \ndoes by such act cause the death of a quick unborn child, shall be \npunished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to ten years, \nand shall also be liable to fine. \n \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nA, knowing that he is likely to cause the death of a pregnant woman, does \nan act which, if it caused the death of the woman, would amount to culpable \nhomicide. The woman is injured, but does not die; but the death of an unborn \nquick child with which she is pregnant is thereby caused. A is guilty of the \noffence defined in this section.\n\nPenal Code                                            183 \n \nExposure and abandonment of a child under twelve years by \nparent or person having care of it \n \n317. Whoever, being the father or mother of a child under the age of \ntwelve years, or having the care of such child, exposes or leaves such \nchild in any place with the intention of wholly abandoning such child, \nshall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to \nseven years or with fine or with both. \n \nExplanation\u2014This section is not intended to prevent the trial of the offender  \nfor  murder  or  culpable  homicide,  as  the  case  may  be,  if  the child dies in \nconsequence of the exposure. \n \n \nConcealment of birth by secret disposal of dead body \n \n318. Whoever by secretly burying or otherwise disposing of the dead \nbody of a child, whether such child dies before or after or during its \nbirth, intentionally conceals or endeavours to conceal the birth of such \nchild shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may \nextend to two years or with fine or with both. \n \n \nHurt \n \nHurt \n \n319. Whoever causes bodily pain, disease or infirmity to any person \nis said to cause hurt. \n \n \nGrievous hurt \n \n320. The following kinds of hurt only are designated as \u201cgrievous\u201d: \n \n(a) emasculation; \n \n(b) permanent privation of the sight of either eye; \n \n(c) permanent privation of the hearing of either ear;\n\n184                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \n \n(d)  privation of any member or joint; \n \n(e) destruction or permanent impairing of the powers of any \nmember or joint; \n \n(f)  permanent disfiguration of the head or face; \n \n(g) fracture or dislocation of a bone; \n \n(h) any hurt which endangers life, or which causes the sufferer \nto be, during the space of ten days, in severe bodily pain, \nor unable to follow his ordinary pursuits. \n \n \nVoluntarily causing hurt \n \n321. Whoever does any act with the intention of thereby causing hurt \nto any person, or with the knowledge that he is likely thereby to cause \nhurt to any person, and does thereby cause hurt to any person, is said \n\u201cvoluntarily to cause hurt\u201d. \n \n \nVoluntarily causing grievous hurt \n \n322. Whoever voluntarily causes hurt, if the hurt which he intends to \ncause or knows himself to be likely to cause is grievous hurt, and if the \nhurt which he causes is grievous hurt, is said \u201cvoluntarily to cause \ngrievous hurt\u201d. \n \nExplanation\u2014A person is not said voluntarily to cause grievous hurt except \nwhen he both causes grievous hurt and intends or knows himself to be likely to \ncause grievous hurt. But he is said voluntarily to cause grievous hurt if, intending \nor knowing himself to be likely to cause grievous hurt of one kind, he actually \ncauses grievous hurt of another kind.\n\nPenal Code                                            185 \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nA, intending or knowing himself to be likely permanently to disfigure Z\u2019s \nface, gives Z a blow which does not permanently disfigure Z\u2019s face, but which \ncauses Z to suffer severe bodily pain for the space of ten days. A has voluntarily \ncaused grievous hurt. \n \n \nPunishment for voluntarily causing hurt \n \n323. Whoever, except in the case provided for by section 334, \nvoluntarily causes hurt, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term \nwhich may extend to one year or with fine which may extend to two \nthousand ringgit or with both. \n \n \nVoluntarily causing hurt by dangerous weapons or means \n \n324. Whoever, except in the case provided for by section 334, \nvoluntarily causes hurt by means of any instrument for shooting, \nstabbing or cutting, or any instrument which, used as a weapon of \noffence, is likely to cause death, or any scheduled weapon as specified \nunder the Corrosive and Explosive Substances and Offensive Weapons \nAct 1958, or by means of fire or any heated substance, or by means of \nany poison or any corrosive substance, or by means of any explosive \nsubstance, or by means of any substance which it is deleterious to the \nhuman body to inhale, to swallow, or to receive into the blood, or by \nmeans of any  animal, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term \nwhich may extend to ten years or with fine or with whipping or with \nany two of such  punishments. \n \n \nPunishment for voluntarily causing grievous hurt \n \n325. Whoever, except in the case provided by section 335, \nvoluntarily causes grievous hurt, shall be punished with imprisonment \nfor a term which may extend to seven years, and shall also be liable to \nfine.\n\n186                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nVoluntarily causing grievous hurt by dangerous weapons or means \n \n326. Whoever, except in the case provided by section 335, \nvoluntarily causes grievous hurt by means of any instrument for \nshooting, stabbing or cutting, or any instrument which, used as a \nweapon of offence, is likely to cause death, or any scheduled weapon \nas specified under the Corrosive and Explosive Substances and \nOffensive Weapons Act 1958, or by means of fire or any heated \nsubstance, or by means of any poison or any corrosive substance, or by \nmeans of any explosive substance, or by means of any substance which \nit is deleterious to the human body to inhale, to swallow, or to receive \ninto the blood, or by means of any animal, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to twenty years, and shall \nalso be liable to fine or to whipping. \n \n \nPunishment for causing hurt to spouse, former spouse, etc. \n \n326A. (1) Whoever causes hurt to his spouse or former spouse, a \nchild, an incapacitated adult or other member of the family and \ncommits an offence under section 323, 324, 325, 326, 334 or 335 shall \nbe punished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to twice \nof the maximum term for which he would have been liable on \nconviction for that offence under the relevant section notwithstanding \nany other punishment provided for that offence. \n \n(2) For the purpose of this section, \u201cspouse\u201d, \u201cchild\u201d, \u201cincapacitated \nadult\u201d and \u201cother member of the family\u201d have the meanings assigned \nto them in section 2 of the Domestic Violence Act 1994 [Act 521]. \n \n \nVoluntarily causing hurt to extort property or to constrain to an \nillegal act \n \n327. Whoever, voluntarily causes hurt for the purpose of extorting \nfrom the sufferer, or from any person interested in the sufferer, any \nproperty or valuable security, or of constraining the sufferer, or any \nperson interested in such sufferer, to do anything which is illegal, or \nwhich may facilitate the commission of an offence, shall be punished\n\nPenal Code                                            187 \n \nwith imprisonment for a term which may extend to ten years, and shall \nalso be liable to fine or to whipping. \n \n \nCausing hurt by means of poison, etc., with intent to commit an \noffence \n \n328. Whoever administers to, or causes to be taken by any person, \nany poison or any stupefying, intoxicating, or unwholesome drug or \nother thing, with intent to cause hurt to such person, or with intent to \ncommit or to facilitate the commission of an offence, or knowing it to \nbe likely that he will thereby cause hurt, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to ten years, and shall also \nbe liable to fine. \n \n \nVoluntarily causing grievous hurt to extort property, or to \nconstrain to an illegal act \n \n329. Whoever voluntarily causes grievous hurt for the purpose of \nextorting from the sufferer, or from any person interested in the \nsufferer, any property or valuable security, or of constraining the \nsufferer, or any person interested in such sufferer, to do anything which \nis illegal or which may facilitate the commission of an offence, shall \nbe punished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to twenty \nyears, and shall also be liable to fine or to whipping. \n \n \nVoluntarily causing hurt to extort confession or to compel \nrestoration of property \n \n330. Whoever voluntarily causes hurt for the purpose of extorting \nfrom the  sufferer, or from any person interested in the sufferer, any \nconfession or any information which may lead to the detection of an \noffence or misconduct, or for the purpose of constraining the sufferer, \nor any person interested in the sufferer, to restore or to cause the \nrestoration of any property or valuable security or to satisfy any claim \nor demand, or to give information which may lead to the restoration of \nany property or valuable security, shall be punished with imprisonment\n\n188                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nfor a term which may extend to seven years, and shall also be liable to \nfine. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a)  A, a police officer, tortures Z in order to induce Z to confess that he \ncommitted a crime. A is guilty of an offence under this section. \n \n(b)  A, a police officer, tortures B to induce him to point out where certain \nstolen property is deposited. A is guilty of an offence under this section. \n \n(c) A, a revenue officer, tortures Z in order to compel him to confess to a \npretended offence against the excise laws. A is guilty of an offence under this \nsection. \n \n \nVoluntarily causing grievous hurt to extort confession or to compel \nrestoration of property \n \n331. Whoever voluntarily causes grievous hurt for the purpose of \nextorting from the sufferer, or from any person interested in the \nsufferer, any confession or any information which may lead to the \ndetection of an offence or misconduct, or for the purpose of \nconstraining the sufferer, or any person interested in the sufferer, to \nrestore or to cause the restoration of any property or valuable security, \nor to satisfy any claim or demand, or to give information which may \nlead to the restoration of any property or valuable security, shall be \npunished with imprisonment for a term which may extend  to ten years, \nand shall also be liable to fine. \n \n \nVoluntarily causing hurt to deter public servant from his duty \n \n332. Whoever voluntarily causes hurt to any person being a public \nservant in the discharge of his duty as such public servant, or with \nintent to prevent or deter that person or any other public servant from \ndischarging his duty as such public servant, or in consequence of \nanything done or attempted to be done by that person in the lawful \ndischarge of his duty as such public servant, shall be punished with\n\nPenal Code                                            189 \n \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to three years or with fine \nor with both. \n \n \nVoluntarily causing grievous hurt to deter public servant from his \nduty \n \n333. Whoever voluntarily causes grievous hurt to any person being a \npublic servant in the discharge of his duty as such public servant, or \nwith intent to prevent or deter that person or any other public servant \nfrom discharging his duty as such public servant, or in consequence of \nanything done or attempted to be done by that person in the lawful \ndischarge of his duty as such public servant, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to ten years, and  shall also \nbe liable to fine. \n \n \nVoluntarily causing hurt on provocation \n \n334. Whoever voluntarily causes hurt on grave and sudden \nprovocation, if he neither intends nor knows himself to be likely to \ncause hurt to any person other than the person who gave the \nprovocation, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which \nmay extend to one month or with fine which may extend to one \nthousand ringgit or with both. \n \n \nCausing grievous hurt on provocation \n \n335. Whoever voluntarily causes grievous hurt on grave and sudden \nprovocation, if he neither intends nor knows himself to be likely to \ncause grievous hurt to any person other than the person who gave the \nprovocation, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which \nmay extend to four years or with fine which may extend to four \nthousand ringgit or with both. \n \nExplanation\u2014The last two sections are subject to the same provisos as \nException 1 of section 300.\n\n190                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nPunishment for act which endangers life or the personal safety of \nothers \n \n336. Whoever does any act so rashly or negligently as to endanger \nhuman life or the personal safety of others, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to three months or with \nfine which may extend to five hundred ringgit or with both. \n \n \nCausing hurt by an act which endangers life or the personal safety \nof others \n \n337. Whoever causes hurt to any person by doing any act so rashly \nor negligently as to endanger human life or the personal safety of \nothers, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may \nextend to six months or with fine which may extend to one thousand \nringgit or with both. \n \n \nCausing grievous hurt by an act which endangers life or the \npersonal safety of others \n \n338. Whoever causes grievous hurt to any person by doing any act so \nrashly or negligently as to endanger human life or the personal safety \nof others, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may \nextend to two years or with fine which may extend to two thousand \nringgit or with both. \n \n \nWrongful Restraints and Wrongful Confinement \n \nWrongful restraint \n \n339. Whoever voluntarily obstructs any person, so as to prevent that \nperson from proceeding in any direction in which that person has a \nright to proceed, is said wrongfully to restrain that person.\n\nPenal Code                                            191 \n \nException\u2014The obstruction of a private way over land or water which a \nperson in good faith believes himself to have a lawful right to obstruct, is not an \noffence within the meaning of this section. \n \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nA obstructs a path along which Z has a right to pass, A not believing in good \nfaith that he has a right to stop the path. Z is thereby prevented from passing. A \nwrongfully restrains Z. \n \n \nWrongful confinement \n \n340.  Whoever wrongfully restrains any person in such a manner as to \nprevent that person from proceeding beyond certain circumscribing \nlimits, is said \u201cwrongfully to confine\u201d that person. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a) A causes Z to go within a walled space, and locks Z in. Z is thus \nprevented from proceeding in any direction beyond the circumscribing line of \nwall. A wrongfully confines Z. \n \n(b) A places men with firearms at the outlets of a building and tells Z that \nthey will fire at Z if Z attempts to leave the building. A wrongfully confines Z. \n \n \nPunishment for wrongful restraint \n \n341.  Whoever wrongfully restrains any person shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to one month or with fine \nwhich may extend to one thousand ringgit or with both. \n \n \nPunishment for wrongful confinement \n \n342. Whoever wrongfully confines any person shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to one year or with fine \nwhich may extend to two thousand ringgit or with both.\n\n192                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nWrongful confinement for three or more days \n \n343. Whoever wrongfully confines any person for three days or \nmore, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may \nextend to two years or with fine or with both. \n \n \nWrongful confinement for ten or more days \n \n344. Whoever wrongfully confines any person for ten days or more, \nshall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to \nthree years, and shall also be liable to fine. \n \n \nWrongful confinement of person for whose liberation a writ has \nbeen issued \n \n345. Whoever keeps any person in wrongful confinement, knowing \nthat a writ for the liberation of that person has been duly issued, shall \nbe punished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to two \nyears, in addition to any term of imprisonment to which he may be \nliable under any other section of this Code. \n \n \nWrongful confinement in secret \n \n346. Whoever wrongfully confines any person in such a manner as \nto  indicate an intention that the confinement of such person may not \nbe known to any person interested in the person so confined, or to any \npublic servant, or that the place of such confinement may not be known \nto or discovered by any such person or public servant as hereinbefore \nmentioned, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may \nextend to two years, in addition to any other punishment to which he \nmay be liable for such wrongful confinement.\n\nPenal Code                                            193 \n \nWrongful confinement for the purpose of extorting property or \nconstraining to an illegal act \n \n347. Whoever wrongfully confines any person for the purpose of \nextorting from the person confined, or from any person interested in \nthe person confined, any property or valuable security, or of \nconstraining the person confined, or any person interested in such \nperson, to do anything illegal or to give any information which may \nfacilitate the commission of an offence, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to three years, and shall \nalso be liable to fine. \n \n \nWrongful confinement for the purpose of extorting confession or \nof compelling restoration of property \n \n348. Whoever wrongfully confines any person for the purpose of \nextorting from the person confined, or from any person interested in \nthe person confined, any confession or any information which may \nlead to the detection of an offence or misconduct; or for the purpose of \nconstraining the person confined, or any person interested in the person \nconfined, to restore, or to cause the restoration of any property or \nvaluable security, or to satisfy any claim or demand, or to give \ninformation which may lead to the restoration of any property or \nvaluable security, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term \nwhich may extend to three years, and shall also be liable to fine. \n \n \nCriminal Force and Assault \n \nForce \n \n349. A person is said to use force to another if he causes motion, \nchange of motion, or cessation of motion to that other, or if he causes \nto any substance such motion, or change of motion, or cessation of \nmotion as brings that substance into contact with any part of that \nother\u2019s body, or with anything which that other is wearing or carrying, \nor with anything so situated that such contact affects that other\u2019s sense \nof feeling:\n\n194                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nProvided that the person causing the motion, or change of motion, or \ncessation of motion, causes that motion, change of motion, or cessation \nof motion in one of the three ways hereinafter described\u2014 \n \n(a) by his own bodily power; \n \n(b) by disposing any substance in such a manner that the \nmotion, or change or cessation of motion, takes place \nwithout any further act on his part, or on the part of any \nother person; \n \n(c) by inducing any animal to move, to change its motion, or \nto cease to move. \n \n \nCriminal force \n \n350. Whoever intentionally uses force to any person, without that \nperson\u2019s consent, in order to cause the committing of any offence, or \nintending by the use of such force illegally to cause, or knowing it to \nbe likely that by the use of such force he will illegally cause injury, \nfear, or annoyance to the person to whom the force is used, is said to \nuse criminal force to that other. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a) Z is sitting in a moored boat on a river. A unfastens the moorings, and \nthus intentionally causes the boat to drift down the stream. Here A intentionally \ncauses motion to Z, and he does this by disposing substances in such a manner \nthat the motion is produced without any other act on any person\u2019s part. A has \ntherefore intentionally used force to Z; and if he has done so without Z\u2019s consent, \nin order to the committing of any offence, or intending or knowing it to be likely \nthat this use of force will cause injury, fear or annoyance to Z. A has used \ncriminal force to Z. \n \n(b) Z is riding in a chariot. A lashes Z\u2019s horses, and thereby causes them to \nquicken their pace. Here A has caused change of motion to Z by inducing the \nanimals to change their motion. A has therefore used force to Z; and if A has \ndone this without Z\u2019s consent, intending or knowing it to be likely that he may \nthereby injure, frighten or annoy Z, A has committed criminal force to Z.\n\nPenal Code                                            195 \n \n(c)  Z is riding in a carriage. A, intending to rob Z, seizes the horse and stops \nthe carriage. Here A has caused cessation of motion to Z, and he has done this \nby his own bodily power. A has therefore used force to Z; and as A has acted \nthus intentionally without Z\u2019s consent, in order to the commission of an offence, \nA has used criminal force to Z. \n \n(d) A intentionally pushes against Z in the street. Here A has by his own \nbodily power moved his own person so as to bring it into contact with Z.  He  \nhas  therefore  intentionally  used  force  to  Z,  and  if  he  has done so without \nZ\u2019s consent, intending or knowing it to be likely that he may thereby injure, \nfrighten or annoy Z, he has used criminal force to Z. \n \n(e) A throws a stone, intending or knowing it to be likely that the stone will be \nthus brought into contact with Z, or with Z\u2019s clothes, or with something carried  by \nZ, or that it will strike water and dash up the water against Z\u2019s clothes, or something \ncarried by Z. Here if the throwing of the stone produces the effect of causing any \nsubstance to come into contact with Z, or Z\u2019s clothes, A has used force to Z; and if \nhe did so without Z\u2019s consent, intending thereby to injure, frighten or annoy Z, he \nhas used criminal force to Z. \n \n(f) A intentionally pulls up a woman\u2019s veil.  Here A intentionally uses force \nto her; and if he does so without her consent, intending or knowing it to be likely \nthat he may thereby injure, frighten or annoy her, he has used criminal force to \nher. \n \n(g) Z is bathing. A pours into the bath water which he knows to be boiling. \nHere A intentionally by his own bodily power causes such motion in the boiling \nwater as brings that water into contact with Z, or with other water so situated \nthat such contact must affect Z\u2019s sense of feeling; A has therefore intentionally \nused force to Z; and if he has done this without Z\u2019s consent, intending or knowing \nit to be likely that he may thereby cause injury, fear or annoyance to Z, A has \nused criminal force. \n \n(h) A incites a dog to spring upon Z, without Z\u2019s consent. Here, if A intends \nto cause injury, fear or annoyance to Z, he uses criminal force to Z. \n \n(i)  A, a head teacher, in the reasonable exercise of his discretion as head \nteacher, canes B, one of his scholars. A does not use criminal force to B because, \nalthough A intends to cause fear and annoyance, he does not use force illegally. \n \n \nAssault \n \n351. Whoever makes any gesture or any preparation, intending or \nknowing it to be likely that such gesture or preparation will cause any \nperson present to apprehend that he who makes that gesture or\n\n196                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \npreparation is about to use criminal force to that person, is said to \ncommit an assault. \n \n \nExplanation\u2014Mere words do not amount to an assault.  But  the words \nwhich a person uses may give to his gestures or preparation such a  meaning  as  \nmay  make  those  gestures  or  preparations  amount  to  an assault. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a) A shakes his fist at Z, intending or knowing it to be likely that he may \nthereby cause Z to believe that A is about to strike Z. A has committed an assault. \n \n(b) A  begins  to  unloose  the  muzzle  of  a  ferocious  dog,  intending or \nknowing it to be likely that he may thereby cause Z to believe that he is about to \ncause the dog to attack Z. A has committed an assault upon Z. \n \n(c)  A takes up a stick, saying to Z, \u201cI will give you a beating\u201d. Here, though the \nwords used by A could in no case amount to an assault, and though the mere gesture, \nunaccompanied by any other circumstances might not amount to an assault, the \ngesture explained by the words may amount to an assault. \n \n \nPunishment for using criminal force otherwise than on grave \nprovocation \n \n352. Whoever assaults or uses criminal force to any person otherwise than \non grave and sudden provocation given by that person, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to three months or with fine \nwhich may extend to one thousand ringgit or with both. \n \nExplanation\u2014Grave and sudden provocation will not mitigate the \npunishment for an offence under this section, if the provocation is sought or \nvoluntarily provoked by the offender as an excuse for the offence; \n \nif the provocation is given by anything done in obedience to the law or by a \npublic servant in the lawful exercise of the powers of such public servant; or \n \nif the provocation is given by anything done in the lawful exercise of the \nright of private defence. \n \nWhether the provocation was grave and sudden enough to mitigate the \noffence, is a question of fact.\n\nPenal Code                                            197 \n \n \nPunishment for using criminal force by spouse \n \n352A. Whoever, during the subsistence of a valid marriage, assaults \nor uses criminal force on his spouse shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to six months, or with fine \nwhich may extend to two thousand ringgit, or with both. \n \n \nUsing criminal force to deter a public servant from discharge of \nhis duty \n \n353. Whoever assaults or uses criminal force to any person being a \npublic servant in the execution of his duty as such public servant, or \nwith intent to prevent or deter that person from discharging his duty as \nsuch public servant, or in consequence of anything done or attempted \nto be done by such person in the lawful discharge of his duty as such \npublic servant, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which \nmay extend to two years or with fine or with both. \n \n \nAssault or use of criminal force to a person with intent to outrage \nmodesty \n \n354. Whoever assaults or uses criminal force to any person, intending \nto outrage or knowing it to be likely that he will thereby outrage the \nmodesty of that person, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term \nwhich may extend to ten years or with fine or with whipping or with \nany two of such punishments. \n \n \nAssault or criminal force with intent to dishonour a person, \notherwise than on grave provocation \n \n355. Whoever assaults or uses criminal force to any person, intending \nthereby to dishonour that person, otherwise than on grave and sudden \nprovocation given by that person, shall be punished with imprisonment \nfor a term which may extend to two years or with fine or with both.\n\n198                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nAssault or criminal force in attempt to commit theft of property \ncarried by a person \n \n356. Whoever assaults or uses criminal force to any person, in \nattempting to commit theft on any property which that person is then \nwearing or carrying, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term \nwhich may extend to two years or with fine or with whipping or any \ntwo of such punishments. \n \n \nAssault or criminal force in attempt wrongfully to confine a person \n \n357. Whoever assaults or uses criminal force to any person, in \nattempting wrongfully to confine that person, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to one year or with fine \nwhich may extend to two thousand ringgit or with both. \n \n \nAssaulting or using criminal force on grave provocation \n \n358. Whoever assaults or uses criminal force to any person on grave \nand sudden provocation given by that person, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to one month or with fine \nwhich may extend to four hundred ringgit or with both. \n \nExplanation\u2014The last section is subject to the same explanation as  \nsection 352. \n \nKidnapping, Abduction, Slavery and Forced Labour \n \n \nKidnapping \n \n359. Kidnapping is of two kinds: kidnapping from Malaysia and \nkidnapping from lawful guardianship.\n\nPenal Code                                            199 \n \nKidnapping from Malaysia \n \n360. Whoever conveys any person beyond the limits of Malaysia \nwithout the consent of that person, or of some person legally \nauthorized to consent on behalf of that person, is said to kidnap that \nperson from Malaysia. \n \n \nKidnapping from lawful guardianship \n \n361. Whoever takes or entices any minor under fourteen years of age \nif a male, or under sixteen years of age if a female, or any person of \nunsound mind, out of the keeping of the lawful guardian of such minor \nor person of unsound mind, without the consent of such guardian, is \nsaid to kidnap such minor or person from lawful guardianship. \n \nExplanation\u2014The words \u201clawful guardian\u201d in this section include any \nperson lawfully entrusted with the care or custody of such minor or other person. \n \nException\u2014This section does not extend to the act of any person who in \ngood faith believes himself to be the father of an illegitimate child or who in \ngood faith believes himself to be entitled to the lawful custody of such child, \nunless such act is committed for an immoral or unlawful purpose. \n \n \nAbduction \n \n362. Whoever by force compels or by any deceitful means induces \nany person to go from any place, is said to abduct that person. \n \n \nPunishment for kidnapping \n \n363. Whoever kidnaps any person from Malaysia or from lawful \nguardianship, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which \nmay extend to seven years, and shall also be liable to fine.\n\n200                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nKidnapping or abducting in order to murder \n \n364. Whoever kidnaps or abducts any person in order that such \nperson may be murdered, or may be so disposed of as to be put in \ndanger of being murdered, shall be punished with death or \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to thirty years and shall, if \nhe is not sentenced to death, also be liable to whipping. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a) A kidnaps Z from Malaysia intending or knowing it to be likely that Z \nmay be sacrificed to an idol. A has committed the offence defined in this section. \n \n(b) A forcibly carries or entices B away from his home in order that B may \nbe murdered. A has committed the offence defined in this section. \n \n \nKidnapping or abducting with intent secretly and wrongfully to \nconfine a person \n \n365. Whoever kidnaps or abducts any person with intent to cause that \nperson to be secretly and wrongfully confined, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to seven years, and shall \nalso be liable to fine. \n \n \nKidnapping or abducting a woman to compel her marriage, etc. \n \n366. Whoever kidnaps or abducts any woman with intent that she \nmay be compelled, or knowing it to be likely that she will be compelled \nto marry any person against her will, or in order that she may be forced \nor seduced to illicit intercourse, or to a life of prostitution, or knowing \nit to be likely that she will be forced or seduced to illicit intercourse, \nor to a life of prostitution, shall be punished with imprisonment for a \nterm which may extend to ten years, and shall also be liable to fine.\n\nPenal Code                                            201 \n \nKidnapping or abducting in order to subject a person to grievous \nhurt, slavery, etc. \n \n367. Whoever kidnaps or abducts any person in order that such \nperson may be subjected, or may be so disposed of as to be put in \ndanger of being subjected to grievous hurt or slavery, or to the \nunnatural lust of any person, or knowing it to be likely that such person \nwill be so subjected or disposed of, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to ten years, and shall also \nbe liable to fine. \n \n \nWrongfully concealing or keeping in confinement a kidnapped \nperson \n \n368. Whoever, knowing that any person has been kidnapped or has \nbeen abducted, wrongfully conceals or keeps such person in \nconfinement, shall be punished in the same manner as if he had \nkidnapped or abducted such person with the same intention or \nknowledge or for the same purpose as that with or for which he \nconceals or detains such person in confinement. \n \n \nKidnapping or abducting child under ten years with intent to steal \nmovable property from the person of such child \n \n369. Whoever kidnaps or abducts any child under the age of ten \nyears, with the intention of taking dishonestly any movable property \nfrom the person of such child, shall be punished with imprisonment for \na term which may extend to seven years, and shall also be liable to fine. \n \n \nBuying or disposing of any person as a slave \n \n370. Whoever imports, exports, removes, buys, sells or disposes of \nany person as a slave, or accepts, receives or detains against his will \nany person as a slave, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term \nwhich may extend to seven years, and shall also be liable to fine.\n\n202                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nHabitual dealing in slaves \n \n371. Whoever habitually imports, exports, removes, buys, sells, \ntraffics, or deals in slaves, shall be punished with imprisonment for a \nterm which may extend to twenty years, and shall also be liable to fine. \n \n \nExploiting any person for purposes of prostitution \n \n372. \n(1) \nWhoever\u2014 \n \n(a) sells, lets for hire or otherwise disposes of, or procures, \nbuys or hires or otherwise obtains possession of, any person \nwith such intention that the person is to be employed or \nused for the purpose of prostitution or of having sexual \nintercourse with any other person, either within or outside \nMalaysia, or knowing or having reason to believe that the \nperson will be so employed or used; \n \n(b) by or under any false pretence, false representation, or \nfraudulent or deceitful means made or used, either within \nor outside Malaysia, brings or assists in bringing into, or \ntakes out or assists in taking out of, Malaysia, any person \nwith such intention that the person is to be employed or \nused for the purpose of prostitution or of having  sexual \nintercourse with any other person, either within or outside \nMalaysia, or knowing or having reason to believe that the \nperson will be so employed or used; \n \n(c) receives or harbours any person\u2014 \n \n(i) who has been sold, let for hire or otherwise \ndisposed of, or who has been procured, purchased, \nhired or otherwise obtained possession of in the \ncircumstances as set out in paragraph (a); or \n \n(ii) who has been brought into or taken out of \nMalaysia in the circumstances as set out in \nparagraph (b),\n\nPenal Code                                            203 \n \n \nknowing or having reason to believe that the person is to \nbe employed or used for the purpose of prostitution or of \nhaving sexual intercourse with any other person, either \nwithin or outside Malaysia, and with intent to aid such \npurpose; \n \n(d) wrongfully restrains any person in any place with such \nintention that the person will be used or employed for the \npurpose of prostitution or of having sexual intercourse with \nany other person; \n \n(e) by means of any advertisement or other notice published in \nany manner or displayed in any place for prostitution \nservice or a service which a reasonable person would \nunderstand it to be a prostitution service, offers any person \nfor the purpose of prostitution or seeks information for that \npurpose or accepts such advertisement or notice for \npublication or display; \n \n(f) acts as an intermediary on behalf of another or exercises \ncontrol or influence over the movements of another in such \na manner as to show that the person is aiding or abetting or \ncontrolling the prostitution of that other, \n \nshall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to \nfifteen years and with whipping, and shall also be liable to fine. \n \n(2) For the purpose of paragraph (1)(d), it shall be presumed until \nthe contrary is proved that a person wrongfully restrains a person if \nhe\u2014 \n(a) withholds from that person wearing apparel or any other \nproperty belonging to that person or wearing apparel \ncommonly or last used by that person; \n \n(b) threatens that person to whom wearing apparel or any other \nproperty has been let or hired out or supplied to with legal \nproceedings if he takes away such wearing apparel or \nproperty;\n\n204                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \n(c) threatens that person with legal proceedings for the \nrecovery of any debt or alleged debt or uses any other threat \nwhatsoever; or \n \n(d) without any lawful authority, detains that person\u2019s identity \ncard issued under the law relating to national registration \nor that person\u2019s passport. \n \n(3) In this section and in sections 372A and 372B, \u201cprostitution\u201d \nmeans the act of a person offering that person\u2019s body for sexual \ngratification for hire whether in money or in kind; and \u201cprostitute\u201d \nshall be construed accordingly. \n \n \nPersons living on or trading in prostitution \n \n372A. (1) \nWhoever knowingly lives wholly or in part on the \nearnings of the prostitution of another person shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to fifteen years and with \nwhipping, and shall also be liable to fine. \n \n(2) Where any person is proved to have exercised control, direction \nor influence over the movements of a prostitute in such a manner as to \nshow that that person is aiding, abetting or compelling the prostitution \nof the prostitute with any other person or generally that person shall, \nin the absence of any proof to the contrary, be deemed to be knowingly \nliving on the earnings of prostitution. \n \n \nSoliciting for purpose of prostitution \n \n372B. Whoever solicits or importunes for the purpose of prostitution \nor any immoral purpose in any place shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term not exceeding one year or with fine or with \nboth.\n\nPenal Code                                            205 \n \nSuppression of brothels \n \n373. \n(1) \nWhoever\u2014 \n \n(a) keeps, manages or assists in the management of a brothel; \n \n(b) being the owner of any place or the agent of such owner, or \nbeing the occupier of any place, lets the place or any part \nthereof with the knowledge that such place or part is to be \nused as a brothel or permits such place or part to be used as \na brothel or is wilfully a party to the continued use of such \nplace or part as a brothel, \n \nshall be punished with imprisonment which may extend to fifteen \nyears, and shall also be liable to fine. \n \n(2) In this section, \u201cbrothel\u201d means any place occupied or used by \nany two or more persons whether at the same time or at different times \nfor purposes of prostitution. \n \n \n373A. (Deleted by Act A1131). \n \n \nUnlawful compulsory labour \n \n374. Whoever unlawfully compels any person to labour against the \nwill of that person, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term \nwhich may extend to one year or with fine or with both. \n \n \nHostage-Taking \n \nHostage-taking \n \n374A. Whoever seizes or detains and threatens to kill, to injure or to \ncontinue to detain another person (\u201cthe hostage\u201d) to compel the \nGovernment of Malaysia or the Government of any State in Malaysia, \nany other government, or any international organization or any other \nperson or group of persons to do or refrain from doing any act as an\n\n206                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nexplicit or implicit condition for the release of the hostage shall be \npunished\u2014 \n \n(a) if the act results in death, with death; and \n \n(b) in any other case, with imprisonment for a term of not less \nthan seven years but not exceeding thirty years, and shall \nalso be liable to fine. \n \n \nRape \n \nRape \n \n375. \nA man is said to commit \u201crape\u201d who, except in the case \nhereinafter excepted, has sexual intercourse with a woman under \ncircumstances falling under any of the following descriptions: \n \n(a) against her will; \n \n(b) without her consent; \n \n(c) with her consent, when her consent has been obtained by \nputting her in fear of death or hurt to herself or any other \nperson, or obtained under a misconception of fact and the \nman knows or has reason to believe that the consent was \ngiven in consequence of such misconception; \n \n(d) with her consent, when the man knows that he is not her \nhusband, and her consent is given because she believes that \nhe is another man to whom she is or believes herself to be \nlawfully married or to whom she would consent; \n \n(e) with her consent, when, at the time of giving such consent, \nshe is unable to understand the nature and consequences of \nthat to which she gives consent;\n\nPenal Code                                            207 \n \n(f) with her consent, when the consent is obtained by using his \nposition of authority over her or because of professional \nrelationship or other relationship of trust in relation to her; \n \n(g) with or without her consent, when she is under sixteen \nyears of age. \n \nExplanation\u2014Penetration is sufficient to constitute the sexual intercourse \nnecessary to the offence of rape. \n \nException\u2014Sexual intercourse by a man with his own wife by a marriage \nwhich is valid under any written law for the time being in force, or is recognized \nin Malaysia as valid, is not rape. \n \nExplanation 1\u2014A woman\u2014 \n \n(a) living separately from her husband under a decree of judicial separation \nor a decree nisi not made absolute; or \n \n(b) who has obtained an injunction restraining her husband from having \nsexual intercourse with her, \n \nshall be deemed not to be his wife for the purposes of this section. \n \nExplanation 2\u2014A Muslim woman living separately from her husband \nduring the period of \u2018iddah, which shall be calculated in accordance with Hukum \nSyara\u2019, shall be deemed not to be his wife for the purposes of this section. \n \n \nHusband causing hurt in order to have sexual intercourse \n \n375A. Any man who during the subsistence of a valid marriage causes \nhurt or fear of death or hurt to his wife or any other person in order to \nhave sexual intercourse with his wife shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to five years. \n \n \nGang rape \n \n375B. Whoever commits gang rape shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term of not less than ten years and not more than \nthirty years.\n\n208                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nExplanation\u2014Where a woman is raped by one or more in a group of \npersons acting in furtherance of their common intention, each of the persons \nshall be deemed to have committed gang rape within the meaning of this section. \n \n \nPunishment for rape \n \n376. (1) Subject to subsections (2), (3) and (4), whoever commits \nrape shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may extend \nto twenty years, and shall also be punished with whipping. \n \n(2) Whoever commits rape on a woman under any of the following \ncircumstances: \n \n(a) at the time of, or immediately before or after the \ncommission of the offence, causes hurt to her or to any \nother person;
