\n \n(b) at the time of, or immediately before or after the \ncommission of the offence, puts her in fear of death or hurt \nto herself or any other person; \n \n(c) the offence was committed in the company of or in the \npresence of any other person; \n \n(d) without her consent, when she is under sixteen years of age; \n \n(e) with or without her consent, when she is under twelve years \nof age; \n \n(f) with her consent, when the consent is obtained by using his \nposition of authority over her or because of professional \nrelationship or other relationship of trust in relation to her; \n \n(g) at the time of the offence the woman was pregnant; \n \n(h) when by reason or on occasion of the rape, the woman \nbecomes insane;\n\nPenal Code                                            209 \n \n(i) when he knows that he is afflicted with the Human \nImmuno-Deficiency \nVirus \n(HIV)/Acquired \nImmune \nDeficiency Syndrome (AIDS) or any other sexually \ntransmissible disease and the virus or disease is or may be \ntransmitted to the woman; \n \n(j) when by reason or on occasion of the rape, the woman \ncommits suicide; or \n \n(k) when he knew of the mental disability, emotional disorder \nor physical handicap of the woman at the time of the \ncommission of the crime, \n \nshall be punished with imprisonment for a term of not less than ten \nyears and not more than thirty years and shall also be punished with \nwhipping. \n \n(3) Whoever commits rape on a woman whose relationship to him \nis such that he is not permitted under the law, religion, custom or usage, \nto marry her, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term of not \nless than eight years and not more than thirty years, and shall also be \npunished with whipping of not less than ten strokes. \n \n(4) Whoever whilst committing or attempting to commit rape \ncauses the death of the woman on whom the rape is committed or \nattempted shall be punished with death or imprisonment for a term of \nnot less than fifteen years and not more than thirty years, and shall also \nbe punished with whipping of not less than ten strokes. \n \n \nIncest \n \nIncest \n \n376A. A person is said to commit incest if he or she has sexual \nintercourse with another person whose relationship to him or her is \nsuch that he or she is not permitted, under the law, religion, custom or \nusage applicable to him or her, to marry that other person.\n\n210                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nPunishment for incest \n \n376B. (1) Whoever commits incest shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term of not less than ten years and not more than \nthirty years, and shall also be punished with whipping. \n \n(2) It shall be a defence to a charge against a person under this \nsection if it is proved\u2014 \n \n(a) that he or she did not know that the person with whom he \nor she had sexual intercourse was a person whose \nrelationship to him or her was such that he or she was not \npermitted under the law, religion, custom or usage \napplicable to him or her to marry that person; or \n \n(b) that the act of sexual intercourse was done without his or \nher consent. \n \n \nExplanation\u2014A person who is under sixteen years of age, if female, or \nunder thirteen years of age, if male, shall be deemed to be incapable of giving \nconsent. \n \n \nUnnatural Offences \n \nBuggery with an animal \n \n377. Whoever voluntarily has carnal intercourse with an animal shall \nbe punished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to twenty \nyears, and shall also be liable to fine or to whipping. \n \nExplanation\u2014Penetration is sufficient to constitute the carnal intercourse \nnecessary to the offence described in this section.\n\nPenal Code                                            211 \n \nCarnal intercourse against the order of nature \n \n377A. Any person who has sexual connection with another person by \nthe introduction of the penis into the anus or mouth of the other person \nis said to commit carnal intercourse against the order of nature. \n \n \nExplanation\u2014Penetration is sufficient to constitute the sexual connection \nnecessary to the offence described in this section. \n \n \nPunishment for committing carnal intercourse against the order \nof nature \n \n377B. Whoever voluntarily commits carnal intercourse against the \norder of nature shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which \nmay extend to twenty years, and shall also be punished with whipping. \n \n \nCommitting carnal intercourse against the order of nature without \nconsent, etc. \n \n377C. Whoever voluntarily commits carnal intercourse against the \norder of nature on another person without the consent, or against the \nwill, of the other person, or by putting the other person in fear of death \nor hurt to the person or any other person, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term of not less than five years and not more than \ntwenty years, and shall also be punished with whipping. \n \n \nSexual connection by object, etc. \n \n377CA. Any person who has sexual connection with another person by \nthe introduction of any object or any part of the body, except the penis \ninto the vagina or anus of the other person without the other person\u2019s \nconsent shall be punished with imprisonment for a term of not less than \nfive years and not more than thirty years, and shall also be liable to \nwhipping.\n\n212                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nException\u2014This section does not extend to where the introduction of any \nobject into the vagina or anus of any person is carried out for medical or law \nenforcement purposes. \n \n \nOutrages on decency \n \n377D. Any person who, in public or private, commits, or abets the \ncommission of, or procures or attempts to procure the commission by any \nperson of, any act of gross indecency with another person, shall be \npunished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to two years. \n \n \nInciting a child to an act of gross indecency \n \n377E. Any person who incites a child under the age of fourteen years \nto any act of gross indecency with him or another person shall be \npunished with imprisonment for a term of not less than three years and \nnot more than fifteen years, and shall also be punished with whipping. \n \n \nCHAPTER XVII \n \nOFFENCES AGAINST PROPERTY \n \nTheft \n \n \nTheft \n \n378. Whoever, intending to take dishonestly any movable property \nout of the possession of any person without that person\u2019s consent, \nmoves that property  in  order to such taking, is said to commit theft. \n \n Explanation 1\u2014A thing so long as it is attached to the earth, not being \nmovable property, is not the subject of theft; but it becomes capable of being the \nsubject of theft as soon as it is severed from the earth. \n \nExplanation 2\u2014A moving, effected by the same act which effects the \nseverance, may be a theft.\n\nPenal Code                                            213 \n \nExplanation 3\u2014A person is said to cause a thing to move by removing an \nobstacle which prevented it from moving, or by separating it from any other \nthing, as well as by actually moving it. \n \nExplanation  4\u2014A person, who by any means causes an animal to move, is \nsaid to move that animal, and to move everything which in consequence of the \nmotion so caused is moved by that animal. \n \nExplanation 5\u2014The consent mentioned in the definition may be express or \nimplied, and may be given either by the person in possession, or by any person \nhaving for that purpose authority either express or implied. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a) A cuts down a tree on Z\u2019s ground, with the intention of dishonestly \ntaking the tree out of Z\u2019s possession without Z\u2019s consent. Here, as soon as  A  has  \nsevered  the  tree  in  order  to  such  taking,  he  has  committed theft. \n \n(b) A puts a bait for dogs in his pocket, and thus induces Z\u2019s dog to follow \nit. Here, if A\u2019s intention be dishonestly to take the dog out of Z\u2019s possession \nwithout Z\u2019s consent, A has committed theft as soon as Z\u2019s dog has begun to \nfollow A. \n \n(c) A meets a bullock carrying a box of treasure. He drives the bullock in a \ncertain direction, in order that he may dishonestly take the treasure. As soon as \nthe bullock begins to move, A has committed theft of the treasure. \n \n(d) A, being Z\u2019s servant and entrusted by Z with the care of Z\u2019s plate, \ndishonestly runs away with the plate without Z\u2019s consent. A has committed theft. \n \n(e) Z, going on a journey, entrusts his plate to A, the keeper of a warehouse, \ntill Z shall return. A carries the plate to a goldsmith and sells it. Here the plate \nwas not in Z\u2019s possession. It could not, therefore, be taken out of Z\u2019s possession, \nand A has not committed theft, though he may have committed criminal breach \nof trust. \n \n(f) A finds a ring belonging to Z on a table in the house which he occupies. \nHere the ring is in Z\u2019s possession, and if A dishonestly removes it, A commits \ntheft. \n \n(g) A finds a ring lying on the high road, not in the possession of any \nperson.  A  by  taking  it  commits  no  theft,  though  he  may  commit criminal \nmisappropriation of property. \n \n(h) A sees a ring belonging to Z lying on a table in Z\u2019s house. Not venturing \nto misappropriate the ring immediately for fear of search and detection, A hides \nthe ring in a place where it is highly improbable that it will ever be found by Z,\n\n214                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nwith the intention of taking the ring from the hiding place and selling it when \nthe loss is forgotten. Here A, at the time of first moving the ring, commits theft. \n \n(i) A delivers his watch to Z, a jeweller, to be regulated. Z carries it to his \nshop. A, not owing to the jeweller any debt for which the jeweller might lawfully \ndetain the watch as a security, enters the shop openly, take his watch by force \nout of Z\u2019s hand, and carries it away. Here A, though he may have committed \ncriminal trespass and assault, has not committed theft, inasmuch as what he did \nwas not done dishonestly. \n \n(j)  If A owes money to Z for repairing the watch, and if Z retains the  watch  \nlawfully  as  a  security  for  the  debt,  and  A  takes  the  watch out of Z\u2019s \npossession, with the intention of depriving Z of the property as a security for his \ndebt, he commits theft, inasmuch as he takes it dishonestly. \n \n(k)  Again, if A having pawned his watch to Z, takes it out of Z\u2019s possession \nwithout Z\u2019s consent, not having paid what he borrowed on the watch, he commits \ntheft, though the watch is his own property, inasmuch as he takes it dishonestly. \n \n(l) A takes an article belonging to Z out of Z\u2019s possession, without Z\u2019s  \nconsent,  with  the  intention  of  keeping  it  until  he  obtains  money from Z as \na reward for its restoration. Here A takes dishonestly; A has therefore committed \ntheft. \n \n(m) A, being on friendly terms with Z, goes into Z\u2019s library in Z\u2019s absence \nand takes away a book, without Z\u2019s express consent, for the purpose  merely  of  \nreading  it,  and  with  the  intention  of  returning  it. Here, it is probable that A \nmay have conceived that he had Z\u2019s implied consent to use Z\u2019s book. If this was \nA\u2019s impression, A has not committed theft. \n \n(n) A asks charity from Z\u2019s wife. She gives A money, food and clothes, \nwhich A, knows to belong to Z, her husband. Here it is probable that A may \nconceive that Z\u2019s wife is authorized to give away alms. If this was A\u2019s \nimpression, A has not committed theft. \n \n(o) A is the paramour of Z\u2019s wife.  She gives A valuable property, which A \nknows to belong to her husband Z, and to be such property as she has no authority \nfrom Z to give. If A takes the property dishonestly, he commits theft. \n \n(p) A in good faith, believing property belonging to Z to be A\u2019s own \nproperty, takes that property out of B\u2019s possession. Here, as A does not take \ndishonestly, he does not commit theft.\n\nPenal Code                                            215 \n \nPunishment for theft \n \n379.  Whoever commits theft shall be punished with imprisonment \nfor a term which may extend to seven years or with fine or with both, \nand for a second or subsequent offence shall be punished with \nimprisonment and shall also be liable to fine or to whipping. \n \n \nPunishment for theft of a motor vehicle \n \n379A. (1) Whoever commits theft of a motor vehicle or any \ncomponent part of a motor vehicle shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term of not less than one year and not more than \nseven years, and shall also be liable to fine. \n \n(2) In this section\u2014 \n \n\u201ccomponent part\u201d, in relation to a motor vehicle, includes any tyre, \naccessory or equipment; \n \n\u201cmotor vehicle\u201d means a mechanically propelled vehicle intended or \nadapted for use on roads, and includes a trailer drawn by a motor \nvehicle. \n \n \nTheft in dwelling house, etc. \n \n380. Whoever commits theft in any building, tent, or vessel, which \nbuilding, tent, or vessel is used as a human dwelling, or for the custody \nof property, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may \nextend to ten years, and shall also be liable to fine, and for a second or \nsubsequent offence, shall be punished with imprisonment and shall \nalso be liable to fine or to whipping. \n \n \nTheft by clerk or servant of property in possession of master \n \n381. Whoever, being a clerk or servant, or being employed in the \ncapacity of a clerk or servant, commits theft in respect of any property \nin the possession of his master or employer, shall be punished with\n\n216                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to seven years, and shall \nalso be liable to fine. \n \n \nTheft after preparation made for causing death or hurt in order to \ncommit theft \n \n382. Whoever commits theft, having made preparation for causing \ndeath or hurt or restraint, or fear of death or of hurt or of restraint, to \nany person in order to commit such theft, or in order to effect his escape \nafter committing such theft, or in order to retain property taken by such \ntheft, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may \nextend to ten years, and shall also be liable to fine or to whipping. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a) A commits theft of property in Z\u2019s possession; and, while committing \nthis  theft,  he  has  a  loaded  pistol  under  his  garment,  having  provided this \npistol for the purpose of hurting Z in case Z should resist. A has committed the \noffence defined in this section. \n \n(b) A  picks  Z\u2019s  pocket,  having  posted  several  of  his  companions near \nhim, in order that they may restrain Z, if Z should perceive what is passing and \nshould resist, or should attempt to apprehend A. A has committed the offence \ndefined in this section. \n \n \nPersons convicted of an offence against section 379, 380 or 382 \ncommitting subsequent offence against such sections \n \n382A. Whoever, having been convicted of an offence under  \nsection 379, 380 or 382 subsequently commits an offence under any \nother of the said three sections, shall be deemed to have committed a \nsecond offence under the section under which he has been \nsubsequently convicted.\n\nPenal Code                                            217 \n \nExtortion \n \nExtortion \n \n383. Whoever intentionally puts any person in fear of any injury to \nthat person or to any other, and thereby dishonestly induces the person \nso put in fear to deliver to any person any property or valuable security, \nor anything signed or sealed which may be converted into a valuable \nsecurity, commits \u201cextortion\u201d. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a)  A threatens to publish a defamatory libel concerning Z, unless Z gives \nhim money. He thus induces Z to give him money. A has committed extortion. \n \n(b) A threatens Z that he will keep Z\u2019s child in wrongful confinement, \nunless Z will sign and deliver to A a promissory note binding Z to pay certain \nmoneys to A. Z signs and delivers the note. A has committed extortion. \n \n(c) A threatens to send men to plough up Z\u2019s field, unless Z will sign and \ndeliver to B a bond, binding Z under a penalty to deliver certain produce to B, \nand thereby induces Z to sign and deliver the bond. A has committed extortion. \n \n(d) A, by putting Z in fear of grievous hurt, dishonestly induces Z to sign \nor affix his seal to a blank paper and deliver it to A. Z signs and delivers the \npaper to A. Here, as the paper so signed may be converted into a valuable \nsecurity, A has committed extortion. \n \n \nPunishment for extortion \n \n384. Whoever \ncommits \nextortion \nshall \nbe \npunished \nwith \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to ten years or with fine or \nwith whipping or with any two of such punishments. \n \n \nPutting person in fear of injury in order to commit extortion \n \n385. Whoever, in order to commit extortion, puts any person in fear, \nor attempts to put any person in fear of any injury, shall be punished \nwith imprisonment for a term which may extend to seven years or with \nfine or with whipping or with any two of such punishments.\n\n218                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \n \n \nExtortion by putting a person in fear of death or grievous hurt \n \n386. Whoever commits extortion by putting any person in fear of \ndeath or of grievous hurt to that person or to any other, shall be \npunished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to fourteen \nyears, and shall also be liable to fine or to whipping. \n \n \nPutting person in fear of death or of grievous hurt in order to \ncommit extortion \n \n387. Whoever, in order to commit extortion, puts or attempts to put \nany person in fear of death or of grievous hurt to that person or to any \nother, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may \nextend to ten years, and shall also be liable to fine or to whipping. \n \n \nExtortion by threat of accusation of an offence punishable with \ndeath, or imprisonment, etc. \n \n388. Whoever commits extortion by putting any person in fear of  an  \naccusation against that person or any other, of having committed, or \nattempted to commit, any offence punishable with death, or with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to twenty years, or with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to ten years, or of having  \nattempted to induce any other person to commit such offence, shall be \npunished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to ten years, \nand shall also be liable to fine or to whipping; and if the offence is one \npunishable under sections 377, 377B and 377C, may be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to twenty years. \n \n \nPutting person in fear of accusation of offence, in order to commit \nextortion \n \n389. Whoever, in order to commit extortion puts or attempts to put \nany person in fear of an accusation against that person or any other, of\n\nPenal Code                                            219 \n \nhaving  committed, or attempted to commit, an offence punishable \nwith death, or with imprisonment for a term which may extend to \ntwenty years, or with imprisonment for a term which may extend to ten \nyears, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may \nextend to ten years, and shall also be liable to fine or to whipping; and \nif the offence is punishable under sections 377, 377B and 377C, may \nbe punished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to twenty \nyears. \n \n \nRobbery and Gang-Robbery \n \nRobbery \n \n390. (1) In all robbery there is either theft or extortion. \n \n(2) Theft is \u201crobbery\u201d, if, in order to commit theft, or in committing \nthe theft, or in carrying away or attempting to carry away property \nobtained by the theft, the offender, for that end, voluntarily causes or \nattempts to cause to any person death, or hurt, or wrongful restraint, or \nfear of instant death, or of instant hurt, or of instant wrongful restraint. \n \n(3) Extortion is \u201crobbery\u201d, if the offender, at the time of committing \nthe extortion, is in the presence of the person put in fear and commits \nthe extortion by putting that person in fear of instant death, of instant \nhurt, or of instant wrongful restraint to that person or to some other \nperson, and, by so putting in fear, induces the person so put in fear then \nand there to deliver up the thing extorted. \n \nExplanation\u2014The offender is said to be present if he is sufficiently near to \nput the other person in fear of instant death, of instant hurt, or of instant wrongful \nrestraint. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a)  A  holds  Z  down,  and  fraudulently  takes  Z\u2019s  money  and  jewels \nfrom Z\u2019s clothes, without Z\u2019s consent. Here A has committed theft, and, in order \nto commit that theft, has voluntarily caused wrongful restraint to Z. A has \ntherefore committed robbery.\n\n220                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \n(b)  A meets Z on the high road, shows a pistol, and demands Z\u2019s purse. Z, \nin consequence surrenders his purse. Here A has extorted the purse from Z by \nputting him in fear of instant hurt, and being at the time of committing the \nextortion in his presence, A has therefore committed robbery. \n \n(c)  A meets Z and Z\u2019s child on the high road. A takes the child, and \nthreatens  to  fling  it  down  a  precipice,  unless  Z  delivers  his  purse.  Z, in \nconsequence, delivers his purse. Here A has extorted the purse from Z, by \ncausing Z to be in fear of instant hurt to the child, who is there present. A has \ntherefore committed robbery on Z. \n \n(d) A obtains property from Z by saying\u2014\u201cYour child is in the hands of \nmy gang, and will be put to death unless you send us one thousand ringgit\u201d. This \nis extortion, and punishable as such; but it is not robbery, unless Z is put in fear \nof the instant death of his child. \n \n(e) Z is walking along a road.  A on a motorcycle snatches Z\u2019s handbag and \nin the process causes hurt to Z.  A  rides away with Z\u2019s handbag. A has therefore \ncommitted robbery. \n \n \nGang-robbery \n \n391. When two or more persons conjointly commit or attempt to \ncommit a robbery, or where the whole number of persons conjointly \ncommitting or attempting to commit a robbery, and of persons present \nand aiding such commission or attempt, amount to two or more, every \nperson so committing, attempting, or aiding, is said to commit \u201cgang-\nrobbery\u201d. \n \n \nPunishment for robbery \n \n392. Whoever commits robbery shall be punished with imprisonment \nfor a term which may extend to fourteen years, and he shall also be \nliable to fine or to whipping. \n \n \nAttempt to commit robbery \n \n393. Whoever attempts to commit robbery shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to seven years, and shall\n\nPenal Code                                            221 \n \nalso be liable to fine. \n \n \nVoluntarily causing hurt in committing robbery \n \n394. If any person, in committing or in attempting to commit robbery, \nvoluntarily causes hurt, such person, and any other person jointly \nconcerned in committing or attempting to commit such robbery, shall \nbe punished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to twenty \nyears, and shall also be liable to fine or to whipping. \n \n \nPunishment for gang-robbery \n \n395. Whoever commits gang-robbery shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to twenty years, and shall \nalso be liable to whipping. \n \n \nGang-robbery with murder \n \n396. If any one of two or more persons, who are conjointly \ncommitting gang-robbery, commits murder in so committing  \ngang-robbery, every one of those persons shall be punished with death \nor imprisonment for a term which may extend to thirty years, and, \nwhere the punishment is not death, shall also be liable to whipping. \n \n \nRobbery when armed or with attempt to cause death or grievous \nhurt \n \n397. If at the time of committing or attempting to commit robbery, \nthe offender is armed with or uses any deadly weapon, or causes \ngrievous hurt to any person, or attempts to cause death or grievous hurt \nto any person, such offender shall be liable to be whipped, in addition \nto any other punishment to which he may be liable under any other \nsection of this Code. \n \n \n398. (Deleted by F.M.S. En. 30 of 1938).\n\n222                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \n \nMaking preparation to commit gang-robbery \n \n399. Whoever makes any preparation for committing gang-robbery, \nshall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to \nten years, and shall also be liable to whipping. \n \n \nPunishment for belonging to gang of robbers \n \n400. Whoever shall belong to a gang of persons associated for the \npurpose of habitually committing gang-robbery, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to twenty years, and shall \nalso be liable to whipping. \n \n \nPunishment for belonging to wandering gang of thieves \n \n401. Whoever shall belong to any wandering or other gang of persons \nassociated for the purpose of habitually committing theft or robbery, \nand not being gang-robbers, shall be punished with imprisonment for \na term which may extend to seven years, and shall also be liable to fine \nor to whipping. \n \n \nAssembling for purpose of committing gang-robbery \n \n402. Whoever shall be one of two or more persons assembled for the \npurpose of committing gang-robbery, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to seven years, and shall \nalso be liable to fine or to whipping.\n\nPenal Code                                            223 \n \nCriminal Misappropriation of Property \n \n \nDefinition of \u201cagent\u201d, \u201ccompany\u201d, \u201cdirector\u201d and \u201cofficer\u201d \n \n402A. For the purposes of sections 403, 404, 405, 406, 407, 408, 409, \n409A, 409B, 415, 416, 417, 418, 419 and 420 of this Chapter, unless \nthe contrary appears from the context:  \n \n\u201cagent\u201d includes any corporation or other person acting or having \nbeen acting or desirous or intending to act for or on behalf of any \ncompany or other person whether as agent, partner, co-owner, clerk, \nservant, employee, banker, broker, auctioneer, architect, clerk of \nworks, engineer, advocate and solicitor, accountant, auditor, surveyor, \nbuyer, salesman, trustee executor, administrator, liquidator, trustee \nwithin the meaning of any Act relating to trusteeship or bankruptcy, \nreceiver, director, manager or other officer of any company, club, \npartnership or association or in any other capacity either alone or \njointly with any other person and whether in his own name or in the \nname of his principal or not; \n \n\u201ccompany\u201d means a company incorporated under any relevant law \nfor the time being in force or pursuant to any corresponding previous \nenactment and includes any statutory corporations; \n \n\u201cdirector\u201d includes any person occupying the position of director of \na company, by whatever name called, and includes a person who acts \nor issues directions or instructions in a manner in which directors of a \ncompany are accustomed to issue or act, and includes an alternate or \nsubstitute director, notwithstanding any defect in the appointment or \nqualification of such person; \n \n\u201cofficer\u201d in relation to a company includes\u2014 \n \n(a) any director, secretary or employee of the company; \n \n(b) a receiver and manager of any part of the undertaking of \nthe company appointed under a power contained in any \ninstrument;  and\n\n224                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \n(c) any liquidator of a company appointed in a voluntary \nwinding up, but does not include\u2014 \n \n(i) any receiver who is not also a manager; \n \n(ii) any receiver and manager appointed by the Court; \nor \n \n(iii) any liquidator appointed by the Court or by the \ncreditors. \n \n \nDishonest misappropriation of property \n \n403. Whoever dishonestly misappropriates, or converts to his own \nuse, or causes any other person to dispose of, any property, shall be \npunished with imprisonment for a term which shall not be less than six \nmonths and not more than five years and with whipping and shall also \nbe liable to fine. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a)  A takes property belonging to Z out of Z\u2019s possession, in good faith, \nbelieving, at the time when he takes it, that the property belongs to himself. A is \nnot guilty of theft; but if A, after discovering his mistake, dishonestly \nappropriates the property to his own use, he is guilty of an offence under this \nsection. \n \n(b) A,  being  on  friendly  terms  with  Z,  goes  into  Z\u2019s  house  in  Z\u2019s \nabsence and takes away a book without Z\u2019s express consent. Here, if A was under \nthe impression that he had Z\u2019s implied consent to take the book for the purpose \nof reading it, A has not committed theft. But if A afterwards sells the book for \nhis own benefit, he is guilty of an offence under this section. \n \n(c)  A and B being joint owners of a horse, A takes the horse out of B\u2019s \npossession, intending to use it.  Here, as A has a  right  to  use  the horse, he does \nnot dishonestly misappropriate it. But if A sells the horse and appropriates the \nwhole proceeds to his own use, he is guilty of an offence under this section. \n \nExplanation 1\u2014A dishonest misappropriation for a time only is a \nmisappropriation within the meaning of this section.\n\nPenal Code                                            225 \n \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nA finds a Government promissory note belonging to Z, bearing a blank \nendorsement. A, knowing that the note belongs to Z, pledges it with a banker as \na security for a loan, intending at a future time to restore it to Z. A has committed \nan offence under this section. \n \nExplanation 2\u2014A person who finds property not in the possession of any \nother person, and takes such property for the purpose of protecting it for, or of \nrestoring it to the owner, does not take or misappropriate it dishonestly, and is \nnot guilty of an offence; but he is guilty of the offence  above  defined,  if  he  \nappropriates  it  to  his  own  use,  when  he knows or has the means of \ndiscovering the owner, or before he has used reasonable means to discover and \ngive notice to the owner, and has kept the property a reasonable time to enable \nthe owner to claim it. \n \nWhat are reasonable means, or what is a reasonable time in such a case, is \na question of fact. \n \nIt is not necessary that the finder should know who is the owner of the \nproperty, or that any particular person is the owner of it; it is sufficient if, at the \ntime of appropriating it, he does not believe it to be his own property, or in good \nfaith believes that the real owner cannot be found. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a)  A  finds  a  ringgit  on  the  high  road,  not  knowing  to  whom  the \nringgit belongs. A picks up the ringgit. Here A has not committed the offence \ndefined in this section. \n \n(b) A finds a letter on the high road, containing a bank note. From the  \ndirection  and  contents  of  the  letter  he  learns  to  whom  the  note belongs. \nHe appropriates the note. He is guilty of an offence under this section. \n \n(c) A finds a cheque payable to bearer. He can form no conjecture as to the \nperson who has lost the cheque. But the name of the person who has drawn the \ncheque appears. A knows that this person can direct him to the person in whose \nfavour the cheque was drawn. A appropriates the cheque without attempting to \ndiscover the owner. He is guilty of an offence under this section. \n \n(d)  A sees Z drop his purse with money in it. A picks up the purse with the \nintention of restoring it to Z, but afterwards appropriates it to his own use. A has \ncommitted an offence under this section.\n\n226                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \n(e) A finds a purse with money, not knowing to whom it belongs; he \nafterwards discovers that it belongs to Z, and appropriates it to his own use. A is \nguilty of an offence under this section. \n \n(f)  A finds a valuable ring, not knowing to whom it belongs. A sells it \nimmediately without attempting to discover the owner. A is guilty of an offence \nunder this section. \n \n \nDishonest misappropriation of property possessed by a deceased \nperson at time of his death \n \n404. Whoever dishonestly misappropriates, or converts to his own \nuse or causes any other person to dispose of property, knowing that \nsuch property was in the possession of a deceased person at the time \nof that person\u2019s decease, and has not since been in the possession of \nany person legally entitled to such possession, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which shall not be less than six months and \nnot more than five years and with whipping, and shall also be liable to \nfine; and if the offender at the time of such person\u2019s decease was \nemployed by him as a clerk or servant,  the imprisonment shall not be \nless than one year and not more than ten  years and with whipping, and \nshall also be liable to fine. \n \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nZ dies in possession of furniture and money. His servant A, before the \nmoney comes into the possession of any person entitled to such possession, \ndishonestly misappropriates it. A has committed the offence defined in this \nsection. \n \n \nCriminal Breach of Trust \n \nCriminal breach of trust \n \n405. Whoever, being in any manner entrusted with property, or with \nany dominion over property either solely or jointly with any other \nperson dishonestly misappropriates, or converts to his own use, that \nproperty, or dishonestly uses or disposes of that property in violation\n\nPenal Code                                            227 \n \nof any direction of law prescribing the mode in which such trust is to \nbe  discharged, or of any legal contract, express or implied, which he \nhas made touching the discharge of such trust, or wilfully suffers any \nother person so to do, commits \u201ccriminal breach of trust\u201d. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a) A, being executor to the will of a deceased person, dishonestly disobeys \nthe law which directs him to divide the effects according to the will, and \nappropriates them to his own use. A has committed criminal breach of trust. \n \n(b) A, is a warehouse-keeper. Z, going on a journey, entrusts his furniture \nto A, under a contract that it shall be returned on payment of a stipulated sum for \nwarehouse room. A dishonestly sells the goods. A has committed criminal breach \nof trust. \n \n(c) A, residing in Kuala Lumpur, is agent for Z, residing in Penang. There \nis an express or implied contract between A and Z that all sums remitted by Z to \nA shall be invested by A according to Z\u2019s direction. Z remits five thousand ringgit \nto A, with directions to A to invest the same in Government securities. A \ndishonestly disobeys the directions, and employs the money in his own business. \nA has committed criminal breach of trust. \n \n(d) But if A, in the last illustration, not dishonestly, but in good faith, \nbelieving that it will be more for Z\u2019s advantage to hold shares in the Oriental \nBank, disobeys Z\u2019s directions, and buys shares in the Oriental Bank  for  Z,  \ninstead  of  buying  Government  securities,  here,  though  Z should suffer loss \nand should be entitled to bring a civil action against A on account of that loss, \nyet A, not having acted dishonestly, has not committed criminal breach of trust. \n \n(e) A, a collector of Government money, or a clerk in a Government office, \nis entrusted with public money, and is either directed by law, or bound by a \ncontract express or implied, with the Government, to pay into a certain treasury \nall the public money which he holds. A dishonestly appropriates the money. A \nhas committed criminal breach of trust. \n \n(f) A, a carrier, is entrusted by Z with property to be carried by land or by \nwater. A dishonestly misappropriates the property. A has committed criminal \nbreach of trust. \n \n \nExplanation\u2014Upon any prosecution for any offence of criminal breach of  \ntrust,  an  employer  who  deducts  the  employee\u2019s  contribution  from the  wages  \npayable  to  the  employee  for  credit  to  any  employee  fund, by  whatever \nname called, established by any law for the time being in force, shall be deemed \nto have been entrusted with the amount of the contribution so deducted by him\n\n228                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nand if he makes default in the payment of such contribution to the said fund in \nviolation of the said law, shall be deemed to have dishonestly used the amount \nof the said contribution in violation of a direction of law within the meaning of \nthis section. \n \n \nPunishment of criminal breach of trust \n \n406. Whoever commits criminal breach of trust shall be punished \nwith imprisonment for a term not exceeding ten years and with \nwhipping, and shall also be liable to fine. \n \n \nCriminal breach of trust by carrier, etc. \n \n407. Whoever, being entrusted with property as a carrier, wharfinger, \nor warehouse-keeper, commits criminal breach of trust in respect of \nsuch property, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which \nshall not be less than one year and not more than ten years and with \nwhipping, and shall also be liable to fine. \n \n \nCriminal breach of trust by clerk or servant \n \n408. Whoever, being a clerk or servant, or employed as a clerk or \nservant, and being in any manner entrusted in such capacity with \nproperty, or with any dominion over property, commits criminal \nbreach of trust in respect of that property, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which shall not be less than one year and not  \nmore than fourteen years and with whipping, and shall also be liable to \nfine. \n \n \nCriminal breach of trust by public servant or agent \n \n409. Whoever, being in any manner entrusted with property, or with \nany dominion over property, in his capacity of a public servant or an \nagent, commits criminal breach of trust in respect of that property, shall \nbe punished with imprisonment for a term which shall not be less than\n\nPenal Code                                            229 \n \ntwo years and not more than twenty years and with whipping, and shall \nalso be liable to fine. \n \n \nDefence not available \n \n409A. It is no defence for any offence prescribed in sections 403, 404, \n405, 406, 407, 408 and 409 to show that the property was openly \nappropriated or that the appropriation was duly recorded and entered \nin the books and accounts of any company or association or body of \nperson whether incorporated or not. \n \nExplanation\u2014The property of a company shall be regarded as belonging to \nthe company notwithstanding that the directors of the said company are, either \nsingly or jointly, entitled to the entire beneficial interest, of the shareholding in \nthe said company. \n \n \nPresumption \n \n409B. (1) Where in any proceeding it is proved\u2014 \n \n(a) for any offence prescribed in sections 403 and 404, that \nany person had misappropriated any property; or \n \n(b) for any offence prescribed in sections 405, 406, 407, 408 \nand 409, that any person entrusted with property or with \ndominion over property had\u2014 \n \n(i) misappropriated that property; \n \n(ii) used or disposed of that property in violation of \nany direction of law prescribing the mode in which \nsuch trust is to be discharged or of any legal \ncontract,  express or implied which he had made \ntouching the  discharge of such trust; or \n \n(iii) suffered any person to do any of the acts described \nin subparagraph (i) or (ii) above,\n\n230                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nit shall be presumed that he had acted dishonestly until  the contrary is  \nproved. \n \n(2) The presumption under subsection (1) shall apply mutatis \nmutandis to the offences prescribed in sections 109 and 511 of the \nCode in relation to any of the offences referred to in that section. \n \n \nReceiving Stolen Property \n \nStolen property \n \n410. (1) Property the possession whereof has been transferred by \ntheft, or by extortion, or by robbery, and property which has been \ncriminally misappropriated or in respect of which criminal breach of \ntrust or cheating has been committed, is designated as \u201cstolen \nproperty\u201d, whether the transfer has been made or the misappropriation \nor breach of trust or cheating has been committed within or without \nMalaysia. But if such property subsequently comes into the possession \nof a person legally entitled to the possession thereof, it then ceases to \nbe stolen property. \n \n(2) The expression \u201cstolen property\u201d includes any property into or \nfor which the same has been converted or exchanged and anything \nacquired by such conversion or exchange whether immediately or \notherwise. \n \n \nDishonestly receiving stolen property \n \n411. Whoever dishonestly receives or retains any stolen property, \nknowing or having reason to believe the same to be stolen property, \nshall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to \nfive years or with fine or with both; and if the stolen property is a motor \nvehicle or any component part of a motor vehicle as defined in section \n379A, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term of not less than \nsix months and not more than five years, and shall also be liable to fine.\n\nPenal Code                                            231 \n \nReceiving benefit derived from criminal activities of organized \ncriminal group \n \n411A. (1) Whoever receives from an organized criminal group a \nbenefit that is derived from the criminal activities of the organized \ncriminal group shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which \nmay extend to six years if the person\u2014 \n \n(a) knows that it is an organized criminal group; and \n \n(b) knows or is reckless as to whether the benefit is derived \nfrom criminal activities of the organized criminal group. \n \n(2) For the purpose of this section, a benefit derived from the \ncriminal activities of an organized criminal group is a benefit derived \nor realized or substantially derived or realized directly or indirectly \nfrom criminal activities of an organized criminal group. \n \n \nDishonestly receiving property stolen in the commission of a gang-\nrobbery \n \n412. Whoever dishonestly receives or retains any stolen property, the \npossession whereof he knows or has reason to believe to have been \ntransferred by the commission of gang-robbery, or dishonestly receives \nfrom a person, whom he knows or has reason to believe to belong or \nto have belonged to gang-robbers, property which he knows or has \nreason to believe to have been stolen, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to twenty years, and shall \nalso be liable to fine. \n \n \nHabitually dealing in stolen property \n \n413. Whoever habitually receives or deals in property which he \nknows or has reason to believe to be stolen property, shall be punished \nwith imprisonment for a term which may extend to twenty years, and \nshall also be liable to fine.\n\n232                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nAssisting in concealment of stolen property \n \n414. Whoever voluntarily assists in concealing or disposing of or \nmaking away with property which he knows or has reason to believe \nto be stolen property, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term \nwhich may extend to seven years or with fine or with both; and if the \nstolen property is a  motor vehicle or any component part of a motor \nvehicle as defined in section 379A, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term of not less than six months and not more than \nseven years, and shall also be liable to fine. \n \n \nCheating \n \nCheating \n \n415. Whoever by deceiving any person, whether or not such \ndeception was the sole or main inducement,\u2014 \n \n(a) fraudulently or dishonestly induces the person so deceived \nto deliver any property to any person, or to consent that \nany person shall retain any property; or \n \n(b) intentionally induces the person so deceived to do or omit \nto do anything which he would not do or omit to do if he \nwere not so deceived and which act or omission causes  or  \nis likely to cause damage or harm to any person in body, \nmind, reputation, or property, \n \nis said to \u201ccheat\u201d. \n \nExplanation 1\u2014A dishonest concealment of facts is a deception within the \nmeaning of this section. \n \nExplanation 2\u2014Mere breach of contract is not of itself proof of an original \nfraudulent intent. \n \nExplanation 3\u2014Whoever makes any representation through any person \nacting as an agent, or otherwise, for him, shall be deemed to have made the \nrepresentation himself.\n\nPenal Code                                            233 \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a)  A, by falsely pretending to be in the Government service, intentionally \ndeceives Z, and thus dishonestly induces Z to let him have on credit goods for \nwhich he does not mean to pay. A cheats. \n \n(b)  A, by putting a counterfeit mark on an article, intentionally deceives Z \ninto a belief that this article was made by a certain celebrated manufacturer,  and  \nthus  dishonestly  induces  Z  to  buy  and  pay  for  the article. A cheats. \n \n(c) A, by exhibiting to Z a false sample of an article, intentionally deceives \nZ into believing that the article corresponds with the sample, and  thereby  \ndishonestly  induces  Z  to  buy  and  pay  for  the  article.  A cheats. \n \n(d)  A, by tendering in payment for an article, a bill on a house with which \nA keeps no money, and by which A expects that the bill will be dishonoured, \nintentionally deceives Z, and thereby dishonestly induces Z to deliver the article, \nintending not to pay for it. A cheats. \n \n(e) A, by pledging as diamonds articles which he knows are not diamonds, \nintentionally deceives Z, and thereby dishonestly induces Z to lend money. A \ncheats. \n \n(f) A  intentionally  deceives  Z  into  a  belief  that  A  means  to  repay any \nmoney that Z may lend to him, and thereby dishonestly induces Z to lend him \nmoney, A not intending to repay it. A cheats. \n \n(g) A intentionally deceives Z into a belief that A means to deliver to Z a \ncertain quantity of pepper which he does not intend to deliver, and thereby \ndishonestly induces Z to advance money upon the faith of such delivery. A \ncheats; but if A, at the time of obtaining the money, intends to deliver the pepper, \nand afterwards breaks his contract and does not deliver it, he does not cheat, but \nis liable only to a civil action for breach of contract. \n \n(h) A intentionally deceives Z into a belief that A has performed A\u2019s part of \na contract made with Z, which he has not performed, and thereby dishonestly \ninduces Z to pay money. A cheats. \n \n(i)  A sells and conveys an estate to B. A, knowing that in consequence of \nsuch sale he has no right to the property, sells or mortgages the same to Z without \ndisclosing the fact of the previous sale and conveyance to B, and receives the \npurchase or mortgage money from Z. A cheats. \n \n(j) A, playing with false dice, or marked cards, wins money from B. A \ncheats.\n\n234                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \n \nCheating by personation \n \n416. A person is said to \u201ccheat by personation\u201d, if he cheats by \npretending to be some other person, or by knowingly substituting one \nperson for another, or representing that he or any other person is a \nperson other than he or such other person really is. \n \n \nExplanation\u2014The offence is committed whether the individual personated \nis a real or imaginary person. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a)  A cheats by pretending to be a certain rich banker of the same name. A \ncheats by personation. \n \n(b)  A  cheats by pretending to be B, a person who is deceased. A cheats by \npersonation. \n \n \nPunishment for cheating \n \n417. Whoever cheats shall be punished with imprisonment for a term \nwhich may extend to five years or with fine or with both. \n \n \nCheating with knowledge that wrongful loss may be thereby \ncaused to a person whose interest the offender is bound to protect \n \n418. Whoever cheats with the knowledge that he is likely thereby to \ncause wrongful loss to a person whose interest in the transaction to \nwhich the cheating relates, he was bound either by law, or by a legal \ncontract, to protect, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term \nwhich may extend to seven years or with fine or with both. \n \n \nPunishment for cheating by personation \n \n419. Whoever cheats by personation shall be punished with\n\nPenal Code                                            235 \n \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to seven years or with fine \nor with both. \n \n \nCheating and dishonestly inducing delivery of property \n \n420. Whoever cheats and thereby dishonestly induces the person \ndeceived, whether or not the deception practised was the sole or main \ninducement, to deliver any property to any person, or to make, alter, or \ndestroy the whole or any part of a valuable security, or anything which is \nsigned or sealed, and which is capable of being converted into a valuable \nsecurity, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which shall not \nbe less than one year and not more than ten years and with whipping, and \nshall also be liable to fine. \n \n \nFraudulent Deeds and Dispositions of Property \n \nDishonest or fraudulent removal or concealment of property to \nprevent distribution among creditors \n \n421. Whoever dishonestly or fraudulently removes, conceals, or \ndelivers to any person, or transfers or causes to be transferred to any \nperson, without adequate consideration, any property, intending \nthereby to prevent, or knowing it to be likely that he will thereby \nprevent, the distribution of that property, according to law, among his \ncreditors or the creditors of any other person, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to five years or with fine \nor with both. \n \n \nDishonestly or fraudulently preventing from being made \navailable for his creditors a debt or demand due to the offender \n \n422. Whoever dishonestly or fraudulently prevents any debt or \ndemand due to himself or to any other person from being made \navailable according to law for payment of his debts or the debts of \nsuch other person, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term \nwhich may extend to five years or with fine or with both.\n\n236                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \n \nDishonest or fraudulent execution of deed of transfer containing a \nfalse statement of consideration \n \n423. Whoever dishonestly or fraudulently signs, executes, or \nbecomes a party to any deed or instrument which purports to transfer \nor subject to any charge any property, or any interest therein, and which \ncontains any false statement relating to the consideration for such \ntransfer or charge, or relating to the person or persons for whose use or \nbenefit it is really intended to operate, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to five years or with fine \nor with both. \n \n \nDishonest or fraudulent removal or concealment of consideration \n \n424. Whoever dishonestly or fraudulently conceals or removes any \nproperty of himself or any other person, or dishonestly or fraudulently \nassists in the concealment or removal thereof, or dishonestly releases \nany demand or claim to which he is entitled, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to five years or with fine \nor with both. \n \n \nMischief \n \nMischief \n \n425. Whoever, with intent to cause, or knowing that he is likely to \ncause, wrongful loss or damage to the public or any person, causes the \ndestruction of any property, or any such change in any property, or in \nthe situation thereof, as destroys or diminishes its value or utility, or \naffects it injuriously, commits \u201cmischief\u201d. \n \nExplanation 1\u2014It is not essential to the offence of mischief that the offender \nshould intend to cause loss or damage to the owner of the property injured or \ndestroyed. It is sufficient if he intends to cause, or knows that he is likely to \ncause, wrongful loss or damage to any person by injuring any property, whether \nit belongs to that person or not.\n\nPenal Code                                            237 \n \nExplanation 2\u2014Mischief may be committed by an act affecting property \nbelonging to the person who commits the act, or to that person and others jointly. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a) A voluntarily burns a valuable security belonging to Z, intending to \ncause wrongful loss to Z. A has committed mischief. \n \n(b) A introduces water into an ice-house belonging to Z, and thus causes \nthe ice to melt, intending wrongful loss to Z. A has committed mischief. \n \n(c) A  voluntarily throws into a river a ring belonging to Z, with the \nintention of thereby causing wrongful loss to Z. A has committed mischief. \n \n(d) A, knowing that his effects are about to be taken in execution in order \nto satisfy a debt due from him to Z, destroys those effects, with the intention of \nthereby preventing Z from obtaining satisfaction of the debt, and of thus causing \ndamage to Z. A has committed mischief. \n \n(e) A, having insured a ship, voluntarily causes the same to be cast away, with the \nintention of causing damage to the underwriters. A has committed mischief. \n \n(f) A causes a ship to be castaway, intending thereby to cause damage to \nZ, who has lent money on bottomry on the ship. A has committed mischief. \n \n(g) A, having joint property with Z in a horse, shoots the horse, intending \nthereby to cause wrongful loss to Z. A has committed mischief. \n \n(h) A causes cattle to enter upon a field belonging to Z, intending to cause, and \nknowing that he is likely to cause, damage to Z\u2019s crop. A has committed mischief. \n \n \nPunishment for committing mischief \n \n426. Whoever \ncommits \nmischief \nshall \nbe \npunished \nwith \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to five years or with fine \nor with both. \n \n \nCommitting mischief and thereby causing damage to the amount \nof twenty-five ringgit \n \n427. Whoever commits mischief and thereby causes loss or damage \nto the amount of twenty-five ringgit or upwards, shall be punished with\n\n238                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nimprisonment for a term of not less than one year and not more than \nfive years or with fine or with both. \n \n \nMischief by killing or maiming any animal  \n \n428. Whoever commits mischief by killing, poisoning, maiming, or \nrendering useless, any animal or animals, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to three years or with fine \nor with both. \n \n \n429. (Deleted by Act A1471). \n \n \nMischief by injury to works of irrigation or by wrongfully \ndiverting water \n \n430. Whoever commits mischief by doing any act which causes, or \nwhich he knows to be likely to cause, a diminution of the supply of \nwater for agricultural purposes, or for food or drink for human beings \nor for animals which are property, or for cleanliness, or for carrying \non any manufacture, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term \nof not less than five years and not more than thirty years or with fine \nor with both. \n \n \nMischief affecting any public transportation \n \n430A. Whoever commits mischief by doing any act with intent or with \nthe knowledge that such act is likely to obstruct, upset, overthrow, \ninjure or destroy any railway engine, train, tender, carriage, truck or \nany form of public transportation, shall be punished with imprisonment \nfor a term which may extend to twenty years, and shall also be liable \nto fine or to whipping.\n\nPenal Code                                            239 \n \nMischief by injury to public road, bridge or river \n \n431. Whoever commits mischief by doing any act which renders, or \nwhich he knows to be likely to render, any public road, bridge, \nnavigable river, or navigable channel, natural or artificial, impassable \nor less safe for travelling or conveying property, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to five years or with fine \nor with both. \n \n \nMischief by injury to telegraph cable, wire, etc. \n \n431A. Whoever commits mischief by cutting or injuring any electric \ntelegraph cable, wire, line, post, instrument or apparatus for signalling, \nshall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to \ntwo years or with fine or with both. \n \n \nExplanation\u2014The injuring here must be of such a nature as to prevent the \nuse of the electric telegraph cable, wire or line, for telegraphing, otherwise the \noffence will be punishable under section 426. \n \n \nMischief by causing inundation or obstruction to public drainage, \nattended with damage \n \n432. Whoever commits mischief by doing any act which causes, or \nwhich he knows to be likely to cause, an inundation or an obstruction \nto any public drainage attended with injury or damage, shall be \npunished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to five years \nor with fine or with both. \n \n \nMischief by destroying or moving or rendering less useful a \nlighthouse or seamark, or by exhibiting false lights \n \n433. Whoever commits mischief by destroying or moving any lighthouse \nor other light used as a seamark, or any seamark or buoy or other thing \nplaced as a guide for navigators, or by any act which renders any such \nlighthouse, seamark, buoy or other such thing as aforesaid less useful as a\n\n240                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nguide for navigators, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which \nmay extend to seven years or with fine or with both. \n \n \nMischief by destroying or moving, etc., a landmark fixed by public \nauthority \n \n434. Whoever commits mischief by destroying or moving any \nlandmark fixed by the authority of a public servant, or by any act which \nrenders such landmark less useful as such, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to one year or with fine or \nwith both. \n \n \nMischief by fire or explosive substance with intent to cause \ndamage to amount of fifty ringgit \n \n435. Whoever commits mischief by fire or any explosive substance, \nintending to cause, or knowing it to be likely that he will thereby cause, \ndamage to any property to the amount of fifty ringgit or upwards, shall \nbe punished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to \nfourteen years, and shall also be liable to fine. \n \n \nMischief by fire or explosive substance with intent to destroy a \nhouse, etc. \n \n436. Whoever commits mischief by fire or any explosive substance, \nintending to cause, or knowing it to be likely that he will thereby cause, \nthe destruction of any building which is ordinarily used as a place of \nworship, or for the administration of justice, or for the transaction of \npublic affairs, or for education, or art, or for public use or ornament, or \nas a human dwelling, or as a place for the custody of property or any \ngovernment facility, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term \nwhich may extend to twenty years, and shall also be liable to fine.\n\nPenal Code                                            241 \n \nMischief with intent to destroy or make unsafe a decked vessel or \na vessel of 20 tons burden \n \n437. Whoever commits mischief to any decked vessel or any vessel \nof a burden of twenty tons or upwards, intending to destroy or render \nunsafe, or knowing it to be likely that he will thereby destroy or render \nunsafe that vessel, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term \nwhich may extend to ten years, and shall also be liable to fine. \n \n \nPunishment for the mischief described in the last section when \ncommitted by fire or any explosive substance \n \n438. Whoever commits or attempts to commit by fire or any \nexplosive substance, such mischief as is described in section 437, shall \nbe punished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to twenty \nyears, and shall also be liable to fine. \n \n \nPunishment for intentionally running vessels aground or ashore \nwith intent to commit theft, etc. \n \n439. Whoever intentionally runs any vessel aground or ashore \nintending to commit theft of any property contained therein or to \ndishonestly misappropriate any such property, or with intent that such \ntheft or misappropriation of property may be committed, shall be \npunished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to ten years, \nand shall also be liable to fine. \n \n \nMischief occurring during disturbances, etc. \n \n440. Whoever commits mischief\u2014 \n \n(a) while taking part in an unlawful assembly or in a riot; or \n \n(b) having made preparation for causing to any person death, \nor hurt or wrongful restraint, or fear of death, or of hurt or \nof wrongful restraint,\n\n242                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nshall be punished with imprisonment which may extend to five years, \nand shall also be liable to fine. \n \n \nCriminal Trespass \n \nCriminal trespass \n \n441. Whoever enters into or upon property in the possession of \nanother with intent to commit an offence or to intimidate, insult or \nannoy any person in possession of such property; or having lawfully \nentered into or upon such property, unlawfully remains there with \nintent thereby to intimidate, insult or annoy any such person, or with \nintent to commit an offence, is said to commit \u201ccriminal trespass\u201d. \n \n \nHouse-trespass \n \n442. Whoever commits criminal trespass by entering into or \nremaining in any building, tent or vessel used as a human dwelling or \nany building used as a place for worship, or as a place for the custody \nof property, is said to commit \u201chouse-trespass\u201d. \n \nExplanation\u2014The introduction of any part of the criminal trespasser\u2019s body \nis entering sufficient to constitute house-trespass. \n \n \nLurking house-trespass \n \n443. Whoever commits house-trespass, having taken precautions to \nconceal such house-trespass from some person who has a right to \nexclude or eject the trespasser from the building, tent or vessel which \nis the subject of the trespass, is said to commit, \u201clurking house-\ntrespass\u201d. \n \n \n444. (Deleted by Act A1273).\n\nPenal Code                                            243 \n \nHousebreaking \n \n445. A person is said to commit \u201chousebreaking\u201d, who commits \nhouse-trespass if he effects his entrance into the house or any part of it \nin any of the six ways hereinafter described; or if, being in the house \nor any part of it for the purpose of committing an offence, or having \ncommitted an offence therein, he quits the house or any part of it in \nany of such six ways: \n \n(a) if he enters or quits through a passage made by himself, or \nby any abettor of the house-trespass, in order to commit \nthe house-trespass; \n \n(b) if he enters or quits through any passage not intended by \nany person, other than himself or an abettor of the offence, \nfor human entrance; or through any passage to which he \nhas obtained access by scaling or climbing over any wall \nor building; \n \n(c) if he enters or quits through any passage which he or any \nabettor of the house-trespass has opened, in order to \ncommit the house-trespass, by any means by which that \npassage was not intended by the occupier of the house to \nbe opened; \n \n(d) if he enters or quits by opening any lock in order to commit \nthe house-trespass, or in order to quit the house after a \nhouse-trespass; \n \n(e) if he effects his entrance or departure by using criminal \nforce or committing an assault, or by threatening any \nperson with assault; \n \n(f)  if he enters or quits by any passage which he knows to \nhave been fastened against such entrance or departure, and \nto have been unfastened by himself or by an abettor of the \nhouse-trespass. \n \nExplanation\u2014Any outhouse or building occupied with a house and between \nwhich and such house there is an immediate internal communication, is part of \nthe house within the meaning of this section.\n\n244                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a) A commits house-trespass by making a hole through the wall of Z\u2019s \nhouse, and putting his hand through the aperture. This is housebreaking. \n \n(b) A commits house-trespass by creeping into a ship at a port-hole between \ndecks, although found open. This is housebreaking. \n \n(c) A commits house-trespass by entering Z\u2019s house through a window, \nalthough found open. This is housebreaking. \n \n(d) A commits house-trespass by entering Z\u2019s house through the door, \nhaving opened  a  door  which  was  fastened.  This is housebreaking. \n \n(e) A commits house-trespass by entering Z\u2019s house through the door, \nhaving lifted a latch by putting a wire through a hole in the door. This is \nhousebreaking. \n \n(f) A finds the key of Z\u2019s house-door, which Z had lost, and commits \nhouse-trespass by entering Z\u2019s house, having opened the door with that key. This \nis housebreaking. \n \n(g) Z is standing in his doorway. A forces a passage by knocking Z down, \nand commits house-trespass by entering the house. This is housebreaking. \n \n(h) Z, the door-keeper of Y, is standing in Y\u2019s door way. A commits house-\ntrespass by entering the house, having deterred Z from opposing him by \nthreatening to beat him. This is housebreaking. \n \n \n446. (Deleted by Act A1273). \n \n \nPunishment for criminal trespass \n \n447. Whoever commits criminal trespass shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to six months or with fine \nwhich may extend to three thousand ringgit or with both. \n \n \nPunishment for house-trespass \n \n448. Whoever commits house-trespass shall be punished with\n\nPenal Code                                            245 \n \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to three years or with fine \nwhich may extend to five thousand ringgit or with both. \n \n \nHouse-trespass in order to commit an offence punishable with \ndeath \n \n449. Whoever commits house-trespass in order to commit any offence \npunishable with death, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term \nwhich may extend to twenty years, and shall also be liable to fine. \n \n \nHouse-trespass in order to commit an offence punishable with \nimprisonment for life \n \n450. Whoever commits house-trespass in order to commit any \noffence punishable with imprisonment for life or imprisonment for a \nterm which may extend to twenty years, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term not exceeding ten years, and shall also be \nliable to fine. \n \n \nHouse-trespass in order to commit an offence punishable with \nimprisonment \n \n451. Whoever commits house-trespass in order to commit any \noffence punishable with imprisonment, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to two years, and shall also \nbe liable to fine; and if the offence intended to be committed is theft, \nthe term of the imprisonment may be extended to seven years. \n \n \nHouse-trespass after preparation made for causing hurt to any \nperson \n \n452. Whoever commits house-trespass, having made preparation for \ncausing hurt to any person, or for assaulting any person, or for \nwrongfully restraining any person, or for putting any person in fear of \nhurt or of assault, or of wrongful restraint, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to seven years, and shall\n\n246                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nalso be liable to fine. \n \n \nPunishment for lurking house-trespass or housebreaking \n \n453. Whoever commits lurking house-trespass or housebreaking, \nshall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to \nthree years, and shall also be liable to fine, and for every second or \nsubsequent offence shall be punished with imprisonment and shall also \nbe liable to fine or to whipping. \n \n \n454. (Deleted by Act A1273). \n \n \nLurking house-trespass or housebreaking after preparation made \nfor causing hurt to any person \n \n455. Whoever commits lurking house-trespass or housebreaking, \nhaving made preparation for causing hurt to any person, or for \nassaulting any person, or for wrongfully restraining any person, or for \nputting any person in fear of hurt or of assault or of wrongful restraint, \nshall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to \nfourteen years, and shall also be liable to fine or to whipping. \n \n \n456. (Deleted by Act A1273). \n \n \nLurking house-trespass or housebreaking in order to commit an \noffence punishable with imprisonment \n \n457. Whoever commits lurking house-trespass or housebreaking, in \norder to commit any offence punishable with imprisonment, shall be \npunished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to five years, \nand shall also be liable to fine; and if the offence intended to be \ncommitted is theft, the term of the imprisonment may be extended to \nfourteen years; and for every second or subsequent offence shall in \neither case be liable to fine or whipping.\n\nPenal Code                                            247 \n \n \nSubsequent offence under section 453 or 457 punishable with \nwhipping after first offence \n \n457A. Whoever, having been convicted of an offence under  \nsection 453 or 457 subsequently commits an offence under any other \nof the said two sections shall be deemed to have committed a second \noffence under the section under which he has been subsequently \nconvicted. \n \n \n458. (Deleted by Act A1273). \n \n \nGrievous hurt caused while committing lurking house-trespass or \nhousebreaking \n \n459. Whoever, while committing lurking house-trespass or \nhousebreaking, causes grievous hurt to any person, or attempts to cause \ndeath or grievous hurt to any person, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to twenty years, and shall \nalso be liable to fine or to whipping. \n \n \nAll persons jointly concerned in housebreaking, etc., to be punishable \nfor death, or grievous hurt caused by one of their number \n \n460. If, at the time of committing lurking house-trespass or \nhousebreaking, any person guilty of such offence shall voluntarily \ncause or attempt to cause death or grievous hurt of any person, every \nperson jointly concerned in committing such lurking house-trespass or \nhousebreaking, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which \nmay extend to thirty years, and shall also be liable to fine. \n \n \nDishonestly breaking open any closed receptacle containing or \nsupposed to contain property \n \n461. Whoever dishonestly, or with intent to commit mischief, breaks \nopen or unfastens any closed receptacle which contains or which he\n\n248                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nbelieves to contain property, shall be punished with imprisonment for a \nterm which may extend to two years or with fine or with both. \n \n \nPunishment for same offence when committed by person entrusted \nwith custody \n \n462. Whoever, being entrusted with any closed receptacle which \ncontains or which he believes to contain property, without having \nauthority to open the same, dishonestly, or with intent to commit \nmischief, breaks open or unfastens that receptacle, shall be punished \nwith imprisonment for a term which may extend to three years or with \nfine or with both. \n \n \nCHAPTER XVIII \n \nOFFENCES RELATING TO DOCUMENTS AND TO CURRENCY \nNOTES AND BANK NOTES \n \n \nForgery \n \n463. Whoever makes any false document or part of a document with \nintent to cause damage or injury to the public or to any person, or to \nsupport any claim or title, or to cause any person to part with property, \nor to enter into any express or implied contract, or with intent to commit \nfraud or that fraud may be committed, commits forgery. \n \n \nMaking a false document \n \n464. A person is said to make a false document\u2014 \n \n(a) who dishonestly or fraudulently makes, signs, seals or \nexecutes a document or part of a document, or makes any \nmark denoting the execution of a document, with the \nintention of causing it to be believed that such document or \npart of a document was made, signed, sealed or executed\n\nPenal Code                                            249 \n \nby, or by the authority of a person by whom or by whose \nauthority he knows that it was not  made, signed, sealed or \nexecuted, or at a time at which he knows that it was not \nmade, signed, sealed or executed; \n \n(b) who without lawful authority, dishonestly or fraudulently, \nby cancellation or otherwise, alters a document in any \nmaterial part thereof, after it has been made or executed \neither by himself or by any other person, whether such \nperson be living or dead at the time of such alteration; or \n \n(c) who dishonestly or fraudulently causes any person to sign, \nseal, execute or alter a document, knowing  that such \nperson by reason of unsoundness of mind or intoxication \ncannot, or that by reason of deception practised upon him \nhe does not, know the contents of the document or the \nnature of the alteration. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a)  A has a letter of credit upon B for ringgit 1,000 written by Z. A in order \nto defraud B, adds a cypher to the 1,000, and makes the sum 10,000, intending \nthat it may be believed by B that Z so wrote the letter. A has committed forgery. \n \n(b)  A, without Z\u2019s authority, affixes Z\u2019s seal to a document, purporting to \nbe a conveyance of an estate from Z to A, with the intention of selling the estate \nto B, and thereby of obtaining from B the purchase money. A has committed \nforgery. \n \n(c)  A picks up a cheque on a banker signed by B, payable to bearer, but \nwithout any sum having been inserted in the cheque. A fraudulently fills up the \ncheque by inserting the sum of one thousand ringgit. A commits forgery. \n \n(d)  A leaves with B his agent, a cheque on a banker, signed by A, without \ninserting the sum payable, and authorizes B to fill up the cheque by inserting a \nsum not exceeding one thousand ringgit for the purpose of making certain \npayments. B fraudulently fills up the cheque by inserting the sum of ten \nthousand. B commits forgery. \n \n(e)  A draws a bill of exchange on himself in the name of B without B\u2019s \nauthority, intending to discount it as a genuine bill with a banker, and intending \nto take up the bill on its maturity. Here, as A draws the bill with intent to deceive \nthe banker by leading him to suppose that he had the security of B, and thereby\n\n250                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nto discount the bill, A is guilty of forgery. \n \n(f) Z\u2019s will  contains  these  words:  \u201cI  direct  that  all  my  remaining \nproperty be equally divided between A, B and C\u201d. A dishonestly scratches out \nB\u2019s name, intending that it may be believed that the whole was left to himself \nand C. A has committed forgery. \n \n(g) A endorses a promissory note and makes it payable to Z, or his order, \nby writing on the bill the words \u201cPay to Z, or his order\u201d, and signing the \nendorsement. B dishonestly erases the words \u201cPay to Z, or his order\u201d, and \nthereby converts the special endorsement into a blank endorsement. B commits \nforgery. \n \n(h)  A sells and conveys an estate to Z. A afterwards, in order to defraud Z \nof his estate, executes a conveyance of the same estate to B, dated six months \nearlier than the date of the conveyance to Z, intending it to be believed that he \nhad conveyed the estate to B before he conveyed it to Z. A has committed \nforgery. \n \n(i)  Z dictates his will to A. A intentionally writes down a different legatee \nfrom the legatee named by Z, and by representing to Z that he has prepared the \nwill according to his instruction, induces Z to sign the will. A has committed \nforgery. \n \n(j) A writes a letter and sign sit with B\u2019s name without B\u2019s authority, \ncertifying that A is a man of good character and in distressed circumstances \nfrom unforeseen misfortune, intending by means of such letter to obtain alms \nfrom Z and other persons. Here, as A made a false document in order to induce \nZ to part with property, A has committed forgery. \n \n(k) A without B\u2019s authority writes a letter and signs it in B\u2019s name, \ncertifying to A\u2019s character, intending there by to obtain employment under Z. A \nhas committed forgery, inasmuch as he intended to deceive Z by the forged \ncertificate, and thereby to induce Z to enter into an express or implied contract \nfor service. \n \nExplanation 1\u2014A man\u2019s signature of his own name may amount to forgery. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a) A signs his own name to a bill of exchange, intending that it may be \nbelieved that the bill was drawn by another person of the same name. A has \ncommitted forgery. \n \n(b) A writes the word \u201caccepted\u201d on a piece of paper and signs it with Z\u2019s\n\nPenal Code                                            251 \n \nname, in order that B may afterwards write on the paper a bill of exchange \ndrawn by B upon Z, and negotiate the bill as though it had been accepted by Z. \nA is guilty of forgery; and if B knowing the fact draws the bill upon the paper \npursuant to A\u2019s intention, B is also guilty of forgery. \n \n(c) A picks up a bill of exchange payable to the order of a different person \nof the same name.
