A endorses the bill in his own name, intending to cause it to \nbe believed that it was endorsed by the person to whose order it was payable: \nhere A has committed forgery. \n \n(d) A purchases an estate sold under execution of a decree against B.  \nB after the seizure of the estate, in collusion with Z, executes a lease of the \nestate to Z at a nominal rent and for a long period, and dates the lease six months \nprior to the seizure with intent to defraud A, and to cause it to be believed that \nthe lease was granted before the seizure. B, though he executes the lease in his \nown name, commits forgery by antedating it. \n \n(e) A, a trader, in anticipation of insolvency, lodges effects with B for  A\u2019s  \nbenefit,  and  with  intent  to  defraud  his  creditors, and  in  order to give  a  \ncolour  to  the  transaction,  writes  a  promissory  note,  binding himself to pay \nto B a sum for value received, and antedates the note, intending that it may be \nbelieved to have been made before A was on the point of insolvency. A has \ncommitted forgery under the first head of the definition. \n \nExplanation 2\u2014The making of a false document in the name of a fictitious \nperson, intending it to be believed that the document was made by a real person, or \nin the name of a deceased person, intending it to be believed that the document was \nmade by the person in his lifetime, may amount to forgery. \n \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nA draws a bill of exchange upon a fictitious person, and fraudulently accepts  \nthe bill in the name of such fictitious person with intent to negotiate it. A commits \nforgery. \n \n \nPunishment for forgery \n \n465. Whoever commits forgery shall be punished with imprisonment \nfor a term which may extend to two years or with fine or with both.\n\n252                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nForgery of a record of a Court, or a public Register of Births, etc. \n \n466. Whoever forges a document, purporting to be a record or \nproceeding of or before a Court, or a Register of Birth, Baptism, \nMarriage or Burial, or a Register kept by a public servant as such, or a \ncertificate or document, purporting to be made by a public servant in \nhis official capacity, or an authority to institute or defend a suit or to \ntake any proceedings therein, or to confess judgment, or a power of \nattorney, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may \nextend to seven years, and shall also be liable to fine. \n \n \nForgery of a valuable security or will \n \n467. Whoever forges a document which purports to be a valuable \nsecurity or a will, or an authority to adopt a son, or which purports to \ngive authority to any person to make or transfer any valuable security, \nor to receive the principal, interest or dividends thereon, or to receive \nor deliver any money, movable property or valuable security, or any \ndocument purporting to be an acquittance or receipt, acknowledging \nthe payment of money, or an acquittance or receipt for the delivery of \nany movable property or valuable security, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to twenty years, and shall \nalso be liable to fine. \n \n \nForgery for the purpose of cheating \n \n468. Whoever commits forgery, intending that the document forged \nshall be used for the purpose of cheating, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to seven years, and shall \nalso be liable to fine. \n \n \nForgery for the purpose of harming the reputation of any person \n \n469. Whoever commits forgery, intending that the document forged \nshall harm the reputation of any party, or knowing that it is likely to \nbe used for that purpose, shall be punished with imprisonment for a\n\nPenal Code                                            253 \n \nterm which may extend to three years, and shall also be liable to fine. \n \n \n\u201cA forged document\u201d \n \n470. A false document, made wholly or in part by forgery, is \ndesignated \u201ca forged document\u201d. \n \n \nUsing as genuine a forged document \n \n471. Whoever fraudulently or dishonestly uses as genuine any \ndocument which he knows or has reason to believe to be a forged \ndocument, shall be punished in the same manner as if he had forged \nsuch document. \n \n \nMaking or possessing a counterfeit seal, plate, etc., with intent to \ncommit a forgery punishable under section 467 \n \n472. Whoever makes or counterfeits any seal, plate or other \ninstrument for making an impression, intending that the same shall be \nused for the purpose of committing any forgery which would be \npunishable under section 467, or with such intent has in his possession \nany such seal, plate or other instrument, knowing the same to be \ncounterfeit, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may \nextend to twenty years, and shall also be liable to fine. \n \n \nMaking or possessing a counterfeit seal, plate, etc., with intent to \ncommit a forgery punishable otherwise \n \n473. Whoever makes or counterfeits any seal, plate or other \ninstrument for making an impression, intending that the same shall be \nused for the purpose of committing any forgery which would be \npunishable under any section of this Chapter other than section 467, or \nwith such intent has in his possession any such seal, plate or other \ninstrument, knowing the same to be counterfeit, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to seven years, and shall \nalso be liable to fine.\n\n254                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \n \nHaving possession of a valuable security or will known to be \nforged, with intent to use it as genuine \n \n474. Whoever has in his possession any document, knowing the same \nto be forged, and intending that the same shall fraudulently or \ndishonestly be used as genuine, shall, if the document is one of the \ndescriptions mentioned in section 466, be punished with imprisonment \nfor a term which may extend to seven years, and shall also be liable to \nfine; and shall, if the document is one of the descriptions mentioned in \nsection 467, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which \nmay extend  to twenty years, and shall also be liable to fine. \n \n \nCounterfeiting a device or mark used for authenticating \ndocuments described in section 467, or possessing counterfeit \nmarked material \n \n475. Whoever counterfeits upon or in the substance of any material \nany device or mark used for the purpose of authenticating any \ndocument described in section 467, intending that such device or mark \nshall be used for the purpose of giving the appearance of authenticity \nto any document then forged or thereafter to be forged on such \nmaterial, or who with such intent has in his possession any material \nupon or in the substance of which any such device or mark has been \ncounterfeited, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which \nmay extend to twenty years, and shall also be liable to fine. \n \n \nCounterfeiting a device or mark used for authenticating \ndocuments other than those described in section 467 or possessing \ncounterfeit marked material \n \n476. Whoever counterfeits upon or in the substance of any material \nany device or mark used for the purpose of authenticating any \ndocument other than the documents described in section 467, intending \nthat such device or mark shall be used for the purpose of giving the \nappearance of authenticity to any document then forged or thereafter \nto be forged on such material, or who with such intent has in his\n\nPenal Code                                            255 \n \npossession any material upon or in the substance of which any such \ndevice or mark has been counterfeited, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to seven years, and shall \nalso be liable to fine. \n \n \nFraudulent cancellation, destruction, etc., of a will \n \n477. Whoever fraudulently or dishonestly, or with intent to cause \ndamage or injury to the public or to any person, cancels, destroys or \ndefaces, or attempts to cancel, destroy, or deface, or secretes, or \nattempts to secrete, any document which is or purports to be a will, or \nan authority to adopt a son, or any valuable security, or commits \nmischief in respect to such document, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to twenty years, and shall \nalso be liable to fine. \n \n \nFalsification of accounts \n \n477A. Whoever, being a clerk, officer or servant, or employed or \nacting in the capacity of a clerk, officer or servant, wilfully and with \nintent to defraud, destroys, alters, mutilates or falsifies any book, \npaper, writing, valuable security or account which belongs to or is in \nthe possession of his employer, or has been received by him for or on \nbehalf of his employer, or wilfully and with intent to defraud, makes \nor abets the making of any false entry in, or omits or alters, or abets the \nomission or alteration of any material particular from or in any such \nbook, paper, writing, valuable security or account, shall be punished \nwith imprisonment for a term which may extend to seven years, or with \nfine, or with both. \n \nExplanation\u2014It shall be sufficient in any charge under this section to allege \na general intent to defraud without naming any particular person intended to be \ndefrauded, or specifying any particular sum of money intended to be the subject \nof the fraud or any particular day on which the offence was committed. \n \n \n478\u2013489. (There are no ss.478\u2013489).\n\n256                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nCurrency Notes and Bank Notes \n \nForging or counterfeiting currency notes or bank notes \n \n489A. Whoever forges or counterfeits, or knowingly performs any \npart of the process of forging or counterfeiting, any currency note or \nbank note shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may \nextend to twenty years, and shall also be liable to fine. \n \nExplanation 1\u2014For the purposes of this section and of sections 489B, 489C   \nand 489D, the expression \u201cbank note\u201d means a promissory note or engagement \nfor the payment of money to bearer on demand issued by any person carrying \non the business of banking in any part of the world, or issued by or under the \nauthority of any State or Sovereign Power, and intended to be used as equivalent \nto, or as a substitute for, money. \n \nExplanation 2\u2014For the purpose of this section and of sections 489B, 489C \nand 489D the expression \u201ccurrency note\u201d includes any note (by whatever name \ncalled) which is legal tender in the country in which it is issued. \n \n \nUsing as genuine, forged or counterfeit currency notes or bank \nnotes \n \n489B. Whoever sells to, or buys or receives from, any other person, \nor otherwise traffics in or uses as genuine, any forged or counterfeit \ncurrency note or bank note, knowing or having reason to believe the \nsame to be forged or counterfeit, shall be punished with imprisonment \nfor a term which may extend to twenty years, and shall also be liable \nto fine. \n \n \nPossession of forged or counterfeit currency notes or bank notes \n \n489C. Whoever has in his possession any forged or counterfeit \ncurrency note or bank note, knowing or having reason to believe the \nsame to be forged or counterfeit and intending to use the same as \ngenuine or that it may be used as genuine, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to ten years.\n\nPenal Code                                            257 \n \nMaking or possessing instruments or materials for forging or \ncounterfeiting currency notes or bank notes \n \n489D. Whoever makes or performs any part of the process of making, \nor buys or sells or disposes of, or has in his possession, any machinery, \ninstrument or material for the purpose of being used, or knowing or \nhaving reason to believe that it is intended to be used, for forging or \ncounterfeiting any currency note or bank note, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to twenty years, and shall \nalso be liable to fine. \n \n \nCHAPTER XIX \n \nCRIMINAL BREACH OF CONTRACTS OF SERVICE \n \n490. (Deleted by Ord. 25 of 1957). \n \n \nBreach of contract to attend on and supply the wants of helpless \npersons \n \n491. Whoever, being bound by a lawful contract to attend on or to \nsupply the wants of any person who by reason of youth, or of \nunsoundness of mind, or of a disease or bodily weakness, is helpless \nor incapable of providing for his own safety or of supplying his own \nwants, voluntarily omits so to do, shall be punished with imprisonment \nfor a term which may extend to three months or with fine which may \nextend to four hundred ringgit or with both. \n \n \n492. (Deleted by F.M.S. En. 41 of 1936).\n\n258                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nCHAPTER XX \n \nOFFENCES RELATING TO MARRIAGE \n \nCohabitation caused by a man deceitfully inducing a belief of \nlawful marriage \n \n493. Every man who by deceit causes any woman who is not lawfully \nmarried to him, to believe that she is lawfully married to him and to \ncohabit or have sexual intercourse with him in that belief, shall be \npunished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to ten years, \nand shall also be liable to fine. \n \n \nMarrying again during the lifetime of husband or wife \n \n494. Whoever, having a husband or wife living, marries in any case \nin which such marriage is void by reason of its taking place during the \nlife of such husband or wife and whether such marriage has taken place \nwithin Malaysia or outside Malaysia, shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to seven years, and shall \nalso be liable to fine. \n \nException\u2014This section does not extend to any person whose marriage, \nwith such husband or wife, has been declared void by a Court  of competent \njurisdiction, nor  to any person who contracts a marriage during the life of a \nformer husband or wife, if such husband or wife, at the time of the subsequent \nmarriage, shall have been continually absent from such person for the space of \nseven  years, and shall not have been heard of by such person as being alive \nwithin that time, provided the person contracting such subsequent marriage \nshall, before such marriage takes place, inform the person with whom such \nmarriage is contracted, of the real state of facts so far as the same are within his \nor her knowledge. \n \n \nSame offence with concealment of the former marriage from the \nperson with whom subsequent marriage is contracted \n \n495. Whoever commits the offence defined in section 494, having \nconcealed from the person with whom the subsequent marriage is \ncontracted the fact of the former marriage, shall be punished with\n\nPenal Code                                            259 \n \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to ten years, and shall also \nbe liable to fine. \n \n \nMarriage ceremony gone through with fraudulent intent without \nlawful marriage \n \n496. Whoever dishonestly or with a fraudulent intention goes through \nthe ceremony of being married, knowing that he is not thereby lawfully \nmarried, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may \nextend to seven years, and shall also be liable to fine. \n \n \n497. (There is no s.497). \n \n \nEnticing or taking away or detaining with a criminal intent a \nmarried woman \n \n498. Whoever takes or entices away any woman who is and whom \nhe knows, or has reason to believe, to be the wife of any other man, \nfrom that man, or from any person having the care of her on behalf of \nthat man, with intent that she may have illicit intercourse with any \nperson, or conceals, or detains with that intent any such woman, shall \nbe punished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to two \nyears or with fine or with both. \n \n \nCHAPTER XXI \n \nDEFAMATION \n \nDefamation \n \n499. Whoever, by words either spoken or intended to be read or by \nsigns, or by visible representations, makes or publishes any imputation \nconcerning any person, intending to harm, or knowing or having \nreason to believe that such imputation will harm the reputation of such \nperson, is said, except in the cases hereinafter excepted, to defame that \nperson.\n\n260                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \n \nExplanation 1\u2014It may amount to defamation to impute anything to a \ndeceased person, if the imputation would harm the reputation of that person if \nliving,  and  is  intended  to  be  hurtful  to  the  feelings  of  his family or other \nnear relatives. \n \nExplanation 2\u2014It may amount to defamation to make an imputation \nconcerning a  company,  or  an  association  or  collection  of  persons  as such. \n \nExplanation 3\u2014An imputation in the form of an alternative, or expressed \nironically, may amount to defamation. \n \nExplanation 4\u2014No imputation is said to harm a person\u2019s reputation, unless \nthat imputation directly or indirectly, in the estimation of others, lowers the \nmoral or intellectual character of that person, or lowers the character of that \nperson in respect of his caste or of his calling, or lowers the credit of that person, \nor causes it to be believed that the body of that person is in a loathsome state, or \nin a state generally considered as disgraceful. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a) A says\u2014\u201cZ is an honest man; he never stole B\u2019s watch\u201d; intending to \ncause it to be believed that Z did steal B\u2019s watch. This is defamation, unless it \nfalls within one of the exceptions. \n \n(b) A is asked who stole B\u2019s watch. A points to Z, intending to cause it to \nbe believed that Z stole B\u2019s watch. This is defamation, unless it falls within one \nof the exceptions. \n \n(c) A draws a picture of Z running away with B\u2019s watch, intending it to be \nbelieved that Z stole B\u2019s watch. This is defamation, unless it falls within one of \nthe exceptions. \n \nFirst Exception\u2014It is not defamation to impute anything which is true \nconcerning any person, if it is for the public good that the imputation should be \nmade or published. Whether or not  it  is  for  the  public  good is a  question  of  \nfact. \n \nSecond Exception\u2014It  is  not  defamation  to  express  in  good  faith any \nopinion whatever respecting the conduct of a public servant in the discharge of \nhis public functions, or respecting his character, so far as his character appears \nin that conduct, and no further. \n \nThird Exception\u2014It is not defamation to express in good faith any opinion  \nwhatever  respecting the  conduct  of  any  person  touching  any public question, \nand respecting his  character,  so  far as  his  character appears in that conduct,\n\nPenal Code                                            261 \n \nand no further. \n \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nIt is not defamation in  A to express in good faith any opinion whatever \nrespecting Z\u2019s conduct in petitioning Government on a public question,  in  \nsigning  a  requisition  for  a  meeting  on  a  public  question, in presiding or \nattending at such a meeting, in forming or joining any society which invites the \npublic support, in voting or canvassing for a particular  candidate  for  any  \nsituation  in  the  efficient  discharge  of  the duties in which the public is \ninterested. \n \nFourth Exception\u2014It is not defamation to publish a substantially true report \nof the proceedings of a Court, or of any Legislative Assembly, or of the result of \nany such proceedings. \n \nExplanation\u2014A Justice of the Peace or other officer holding an inquiry in \nopen Court preliminary to a trial in a Court, is a Court within the meaning of the \nabove section. \n \nFifth Exception\u2014It is not defamation to express in good faith any opinion \nwhatever respecting the merits of any case, civil or criminal, which has been \ndecided by a Court, or respecting the conduct of any person as a party, witness \nor agent, in any such case, or respecting the character of such person, as far as \nhis character appears in that conduct, and no further. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a) A says\u2014\u201cI think Z\u2019s evidence on that trial is so contradictory that he \nmust be stupid or dishonest\u201d. A is within this exception if he says this in good \nfaith; inasmuch as the opinion which he expresses respects Z\u2019s character as it \nappears in Z\u2019s conduct as a witness, and no further. \n \n(b) But  if  A  says\u2014\u201cI  do  not  believe what  Z  asserted  at  that  trial, \nbecause I know him to be a man without veracity\u201d. A is not within this exception, \ninasmuch as the opinion which he expresses of Z\u2019s character, is an opinion not \nfounded on Z\u2019s conduct  as  a  witness. \n \nSixth Exception\u2014It is not defamation to express in good faith any opinion \nrespecting the merits of any performance which its author has submitted to the \njudgment of the public, or respecting the character of the author so far as his \ncharacter appears in such performance, and no further. \n \nExplanation\u2014A performance may be submitted to the judgment of the \npublic expressly or by acts on the part of the author which imply such submission\n\n262                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nto the judgment of the public. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a) A person who publishes a book, submits that book to the judgment of \nthe public. \n \n(b) A person who makes a speech in public, submits that speech to the \njudgment of the public. \n \n(c) An actor or singer who appears on a public stage, submits his acting \nor singing to the judgment of the public. \n \n(d) A says of a book published by Z\u2014\u201cZ\u2019s book is foolish, Z must be a \nweak man. Z\u2019s book is in decent, Z must be a man of impure mind\u201d .A is within \nthis exception, if he says this in good faith, inasmuch as the opinion which he \nexpresses of Z respects Z\u2019s character only so far as it appears in Z\u2019s book, and \nno further. \n \n(e) But if A says\u2014\u201cI am not surprised that Z\u2019s book is foolish and \nindecent, for he is a weak man and a libertine\u201d. A is not within this exception, \ninasmuch as the opinion which he expresses of Z\u2019s character is an opinion not \nfounded on Z\u2019s book. \n \nSeventh Exception\u2014It is not defamation in a person having over another \nany authority, either conferred by law, or arising out of a lawful contract made \nwith that other, to pass in good faith any censure on the conduct of that other in \nmatters to which such lawful authority relates. \n \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nA Judge censuring in good faith the conduct of a witness or of an officer of \nthe Court; a Head of a Department censuring in good faith those who are under \nhis orders; a parent censuring in good faith a child in  the  presence  of  other  \nchildren; a schoolmaster, whose authority  is derived from a parent, censuring in \ngood faith a pupil in the presence of other pupils; a master censuring a servant \nin good faith for remissness in service; a banker censuring in good faith the \ncashier of his bank for the conduct of such cashier as such cashier\u2014are within \nthis exception. \n \nEighth Exception\u2014It is not defamation to prefer in good faith an accusation \nagainst any person to any of those who have lawful authority over that person \nwith respect to the subject matter of accusation.\n\nPenal Code                                            263 \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nIf A in good faith accuses Z before a Magistrate; if A in good faith complains \nof the conduct of Z, a servant, to Z\u2019s master; if A in good faith complains of the \nconduct of Z, a child, to Z\u2019s father\u2014A is within this exception. \n \nNinth Exception\u2014It is not defamation to make an imputation on the \ncharacter of another, provided that the imputation be made in good faith for the \nprotection of the interests of the person making it, or of  any other person, or for \nthe public good. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a) A, a shopkeeper, says to B,  who  manages his  business\u2014\u201cSell nothing \nto Z unless he pays you ready money, for I have no opinion of his honesty\u201d. A is \nwithin the exception, if he has made this imputation on Z in good faith for the \nprotection of his own interests. \n \n(b)  A, a Magistrate, in making a report to his superior officer, casts an \nimputation on the character of Z. Here, if the imputation is made in good faith \nand for the public good, A is within the exception. \n \nTenth Exception\u2014It is not defamation to convey a caution, in good faith, to \none person against another, provided that such caution be intended for the good \nof the person to whom it is conveyed, or of some person in whom that person is \ninterested,  or for the public good. \n \nIn proving the existence of circumstances as a defence under the 2nd, 3rd, \n5th, 6th, 7th, 8th, 9th, or 10th exception, good faith shall be presumed unless the \ncontrary appears. \n \n \nPunishment for defamation \n \n500. Whoever defames another shall be punished with imprisonment \nfor a term which may extend to two years or with fine or with both. \n \n \nPrinting or engraving matter known to be defamatory \n \n501. Whoever prints or engraves any matter, knowing or having good \nreason to believe that such matter is defamatory of any person, shall be \npunished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to two years \nor with fine or with both.\n\n264                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \n \nSale of printed or engraved substance containing defamatory \nmatter \n \n502. Whoever sells or offers for sale any printed or engraved \nsubstance, containing defamatory matter, knowing that it contains such \nmatter, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may \nextend to two years or with fine or with both. \n \n \nCHAPTER XXII \n \nCRIMINAL INTIMIDATION, INSULT AND ANNOYANCE \n \n \nCriminal intimidation \n \n503. Whoever threatens another with any injury to his person, \nreputation or property, or to the person or reputation of any one in \nwhom that person is interested, with intent to cause alarm to that \nperson, or to cause that person to do any act which he is not legally \nbound to do, or to omit to do any act which that person is legally \nentitled to do, as the means of avoiding the execution of such threat, \ncommits criminal intimidation. \n \n \nExplanation\u2014A threat to injure the reputation of any deceased person in \nwhom the person threatened is interested, is with in this section. \n \n \nILLUSTRATION \n \nA, for the purpose of inducing B to desist from prosecuting a civil suit, \nthreatens to burn B\u2019s house. A is guilty of criminal intimidation. \n \n \nIntentional insult with intent to provoke a breach of the peace \n \n504. Whoever intentionally insults, and thereby gives provocation to \nany person, intending or knowing it to be likely that such provocation\n\nPenal Code                                            265 \n \nwill cause him to break the public peace, or to commit any other \noffence, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may \nextend to two years or with fine or with both. \n \n \nStatements conducing to public mischief \n \n505. Whoever makes, publishes or circulates any statement, rumour \nor report\u2014 \n \n(a) with intent to cause, or which is likely to cause, any officer, \nsoldier, sailor or airman in the Malaysian Armed Forces or \nany person to whom section 140B refers, to mutiny or \notherwise disregard or fail in his duty as such; \n \n(b) with intent to cause, or which his likely to cause, fear or \nalarm to the public, or to any section of the public where \nby any person may be induced to commit an offence against \nthe State or against the public tranquillity; or \n \n(c) with intent to incite or which is likely to incite any class or \ncommunity of persons to commit any offence against any \nother class or community of persons, \n \nshall be punished with imprisonment which may extend to two years \nor with fine or with both. \n \nException\u2014It  does  not  amount  to  an  offence  within  the  meaning of \nthis section, when the person making, publishing or circulating any such \nstatement, rumour or report has reasonable grounds for believing that such \nstatement, rumour or report is true and makes, publishes or circulates it without \nany such intent as aforesaid. \n \n \nPunishment for criminal intimidation \n \n506. Whoever commits the offence of criminal intimidation shall be \npunished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to two years \nor with fine or with both; if the threat is to cause death or grievous hurt, \nor to cause the destruction of any property by fire, or to cause an \noffence punishable with death or imprisonment, or with imprisonment\n\n266                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nfor a term which may extend to seven years, or to impute unchastity to \na woman, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may \nextend to seven years or with fine or  with both. \n \n \nCriminal intimidation by an anonymous communication \n \n507. Whoever commits the offence of criminal intimidation by an \nanonymous communication, or by having taken precautions to conceal \nthe name or abode of the person from whom the threat comes, shall be \npunished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to two years, \nin addition to the punishment provided for the offence by section 506. \n \n \nStalking \n \n507A. (1) Whoever repeatedly by any act of harassment, intending \nto cause, or knowing or ought to know that the act is likely to cause, \ndistress, fear or alarm to any person of the person\u2019s safety, commits an \noffence of stalking. \n \n(2) For the purposes of subsection (1), the act of harassment may \ninclude the following: \n \n(a) following or tracking a person in any manner or by any \nmeans; \n \n(b) communicating or attempting to communicate with a \nperson in any manner or by any means; \n \n(c) loitering at the place of residence or business of a person; \n \n(d) giving or sending any thing to a person in any manner or \nby any means. \n \n(3) Whoever commits the offence of stalking shall be punished with \nimprisonment for a term which may extend to three years or with fine \nor with both.\n\nPenal Code                                            267 \n \n(4) In this section, \u201crepeatedly\u201d shall refer to at least two occasions. \n \n \nAct caused by inducing a person to believe that he will be \nrendered an object of Divine displeasure \n \n508. Whoever voluntarily causes or attempts to cause any person to \ndo anything which that person is not legally bound to do, or to omit to \ndo anything which he is legally entitled to do, by inducing or \nattempting to induce that person to believe that he, or any person in \nwhom he is interested, will become or will be rendered by some act \nof the offender an object of Divine displeasure if he does not do the \nthing which it is the object of the offender to cause him to do, or if he \ndoes the thing which it is the object of the offender to cause him to \nomit, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which may \nextend to one year or with fine or with both. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a) A performs a ceremony at Z\u2019s door with the intention of causing it to \nbe believed that by so doing he renders Z an object of Divine displeasure. A has \ncommitted the offence defined in this section. \n \n(b)  A threatens Z that unless Z performs a certain act, A will kill one of A\u2019s \nown children, under such circumstances that the killing would be believed to \nrender Z an object of Divine displeasure. A has committed the offence defined \nin this section. \n \n \nWord or gesture intended to insult the modesty of a person \n \n509. Whoever, intending to insult the modesty of any person, utters \nany word, makes any sound or gesture, or exhibits any object, \nintending that such word or sound shall be heard, or that such gesture \nor object shall be seen by such person, or intrudes upon the privacy of \nsuch person, shall be punished with imprisonment for a term which \nmay extend to five years or with fine or with both.\n\n268                                         Laws of Malaysia                      ACT 574 \n \n \nMisconduct in public by a drunken person \n \n510. Whoever, in a state of intoxication, appears in any public place, \nor in any place which it is a trespass in him to enter, and there conducts \nhimself in such a manner as to cause annoyance to any person, shall \nbe punished with imprisonment for a term which may extend to ten \ndays or with fine which may extend to twenty ringgit or with both. \n \n \nCHAPTER XXIII \n \nATTEMPTS TO COMMIT OFFENCES \n \nPunishment for attempting to commit offences punishable with \nimprisonment \n \n511. Whoever attempts to commit an offence punishable by this \nCode or by any other written law with imprisonment or fine or with a \ncombination of such punishments, or attempts to cause such an offence \nto be committed, and in such attempt does any act towards the \ncommission of such offence, shall, where no express provision is made \nby this Code or by such other written law, as the case may be, for the \npunishment of such attempt, be punished with such punishment as is \nprovided for the offence: \n \nProvided that any term of imprisonment imposed shall not exceed \none-half of the longest term provided for the offence. \n \n \nILLUSTRATIONS \n \n(a) A makes an attempt to steal some jewels by breaking open a box, and \nfinds after so opening the box that there is no jewel in it. He has done  an  act  \ntowards  the  commission  of  theft,  and  therefore  is  guilty under this section. \n \n(b) A makes an attempt to pick the pocket of Z by thrusting his hand into \nZ\u2019s pocket.  A  fails  in  the  attempt  in  consequence  of  Z\u2019s  having nothing in \nhis pocket. A is guilty under this section.\n\n269 \n \nLAWS OF MALAYSIA \n \nAct 574 \n \nPENAL CODE \n \nLIST OF AMENDMENTS \n \n \nAmending law \nShort title \nIn force from \nF.M.S.
